# Woof App Audit - 2026-06-05

## Audit Plan

Role: senior lead project manager focused on launch readiness before marketing spend.

Audit tracks:
1. Launch-critical user journeys: first open, scan, search, result, history, paywall, sign-in, restore purchase, delete account.
2. Product data quality: search-result consistency, stale/low-quality rows, ingredient completeness, image coverage, cache-key behavior.
3. Performance: time to first feedback in store scanning, number of AI/network calls per scan, cache hit/miss paths, long-running timeout behavior.
4. Security and abuse resistance: secrets, Supabase RLS/RPC permissions, edge-function rate limits, paid-AI cost controls, CORS, public write surfaces.
5. Release readiness: Expo compatibility, dependency vulnerabilities, broken scripts, test coverage, logging, and operational observability.

Evidence gathered:
- Static code review of current worktree.
- `npm ci`
- `npm audit --json`
- `npx expo-doctor`
- `npx expo install --check`
- `npx tsc --noEmit`
- `npx expo export --platform web`
- `npx expo export --platform android --output-dir /tmp/woof-export-android`
- `npm test -- --watch=false`
- Live Supabase read-only count checks through the app's public client.

## Executive Summary

The app is functional in some paths, but it is not launch-ready for paid marketing. This audit now documents 164 findings. The biggest issues are not cosmetic. They are trust, conversion, security, and release-readiness issues: search can show products that the result screen rejects, stale visible search rows can remain tappable while a new query is pending, cleared or canceled search requests can repopulate old results after the user has dismissed search, search-selected products can be scored with unknown pet type, photo and ingredient-label scans can also proceed with unknown dog/cat context, recent-search rows can reopen stale products, search product-not-found errors can retry the same invalid row instead of routing to scan or label capture, user OCR fallback can overwrite existing catalog rows, guest human-food quota reset copy can disagree with server enforcement, signed-in scans can be saved into anonymous history when auth lookup times out, signed-in history saves can be dropped when local storage fails before remote sync starts, the visible history list caps "Show all" at 10 entries while the app stores and sells more history, retained history rows can outlive their replayable result payloads, repeated same-product scans can consume quota without creating matching history rows, post-scan upsell timing can miss the intended second-scan conversion moment, the first-scan quota education toast is marked shown but never rendered, replaying onboarding can erase the completed-onboarding key before the replay finishes, root crash recovery can also erase completed onboarding state during a reset retry, guest quota reconciliation can replay unbounded local counters into server quota state, scan can require multiple AI steps before giving a useful answer, the fastest barcode path exists but is not reachable from the UI, its miss event is not handled by Results, and barcode network failures can be misclassified as product misses, scanner photos can skip orientation correction before vision analysis, the capture button can call the camera before it is ready, the scanner cancel control can be rendered untouchable during processing, scanner back navigation can still launch Results after the user leaves, AI request timeouts can start only after unbounded auth/session refresh work, truncated streamed AI responses can be saved as completed local/history results, skeletal pet-food AI responses can be cached and rendered as successful results, shared cache metadata can mislabel search/photo analyses as barcode lookups, the streaming SSE parser can drop valid split event lines and force retries/fallbacks, app-triggered fetch timeouts can be classified as cancellations instead of offline signals, slow scan/cancel/retry paths can keep unnecessary AI work alive, helper timeouts can be swallowed as cancellations and leave Results waiting without error recovery, ingredient-label recovery can leave stale analyses marked as running and accepts malformed recovery routes, OCR-fallback analysis errors can leave the recovery flow spinning, rekeyed timeout/error paths can leave canonical analysis entries in memory, onboarding completion can be lost when local storage writes fail, guest users can open the paywall before RevenueCat initialization has finished, paywall purchase/restore callbacks can outlive a user dismissal, completed purchase flows without an active Pro entitlement can silently return users to the paywall, delete-account success can leave the Profile delete control stuck after re-authentication, negative analysis prewarm misses can suppress fresh shared cache hits, product-lookup cache hits can erase original source provenance, restored signed-in sessions can skip guest-history migration retries, oversized edge-function bodies can be parsed before size/rate checks reject them, native camera permission copy does not cover all camera uses, large scan photos are carried through navigation state, streamed analysis results can differ from normalized cached results, signed-in users can burn hourly rate limit on internal helper calls before a useful result, shared verified analysis cache rows can be written from caller-supplied data, guest scans can fail to migrate into the user's account after a later sign-in cycle, required onboarding assets, imported route screens, imported source modules, and Supabase backend contracts can be left out of release builds because they are untracked, direct runtime imports can depend on undeclared transitive Expo packages, untracked Supabase edge-function JWT settings and floating Edge Function imports can change guest scan/product-lookup behavior between local and clean deploys, missing Supabase env can crash before React recovery UI, root error recovery can render with an unreadable CTA, Supabase-backed search/history failures can leave the offline detector stuck online, the paid AI analyze endpoint allows browser calls from any origin, product images found during lookup are not persisted for later search/history surfaces, user OCR contributions become shared catalog data without clear disclosure/deletion terms, live App Store privacy labels do not cleanly match authenticated scan/history behavior, free result content does not match the in-app Terms promise, several SECURITY DEFINER functions run without pinned search paths, mobile Google OAuth uses implicit token redirects instead of PKCE, Apple sign-in can be shown before runtime availability is confirmed, transient RevenueCat failures can downgrade Pro users to free state, sign-out can reset the in-memory free scan counter, debug quota-reset helpers are exported without their own production guard, startup quota gates can open before persisted quota counts hydrate, missing signed-in profile rows can bypass server quota checks and leave counters unrepaired, product lookup can cache wrong Amazon/Chewy/OPFF name-search matches without title or brand validation, photo lookup can prefer broad AI search-term exact matches over the identified product row, expired sessions can silently downgrade paid analysis requests to guest identity, text human-food retries can lose the original food input, quota error CTAs can say upgrade while routing home, human-food caution results can be mislabeled as dangerous in explanatory copy, public and in-app legal surfaces are not synchronized, guest users can scan before seeing any terms/privacy acceptance surface, live App Store compatibility includes Mac and Apple Vision without matching QA evidence, the in-app appearance controls can conflict with the native light-only configuration, human-food answers are written into a shared authenticated cache, human-food history does not replay reliably across devices, safety/veterinary disclaimers are not consistently shown at decision time, startup can remain blank if initial auth session loading rejects, auth error recovery can dead-end instead of reopening sign-in, scraped and user-OCR catalog rows can be promoted as verified ingredient data, parts of the database contain low-quality/non-food rows, recall messaging can look more authoritative than the live data supports, Google sign-in can fail without visible feedback, photo/history retention does not match privacy copy, offline state can be misdetected at launch, users can potentially bypass entitlement/quota controls through profile writes, auth/session state is persisted in non-secure local storage, subscription identity can drift between guest and signed-in users, database/RLS contracts conflict with client behavior, native release identity/update surfaces are not fully hardened, release version sources are inconsistent, public/internal Supabase RPC boundaries are too loose, public marketing/support links and copy are inconsistent with the live app, quality scripts are not release-grade gates, and several Supabase RPC/edge-function permissions can be abused.

Immediate launch recommendation: do not scale marketing until the P0/P1 items and fourth/fifth-pass launch blockers below are fixed and verified on real devices in a store-like network environment.

## P0 - Fix Before Marketing

### 1. Search Can Return Rows The Result Screen Rejects

Impact: This directly explains the user complaint: "search product and click on them it says its not in the database anymore."

Evidence:
- Search UI calls `search_products` and renders returned rows: `screens/HomeScreen.js:305`.
- Tap starts `mode: "search"` with product name and brand: `screens/HomeScreen.js:374`.
- Search analysis then re-runs lookup through `getProductData(productName, brand)`: `services/analysisService.js:328`.
- Search RPC returns rows with `ingredient_count >= 3`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:64`.
- `getProductData` accepts only rows with at least 5 ingredients: `services/cache.js:163` and `services/cache.js:186`.
- `search_products` does not filter `expires_at`, while `getProductData` requires `expires_at > now`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:63`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:64`, `services/cache.js:159`, and `services/cache.js:187`.

Live data:
- `product_data`: 10,990 rows.
- Rows with `ingredient_count >= 3`: 10,984.
- Rows visible to search but rejected by tap path because ingredient count is 3-4: 222.
- Expired rows currently visible under the search ingredient threshold: 0 as of the June 6, 2026 live REST count, but the SQL contract still allows them.
- Examples include variety bundles, treats/toppers, and one non-food genetic test row.

Fix:
- Align `search_products` with the analysis contract: `ingredient_count >= 5` and `expires_at > now()`.
- Pass the selected row's `cache_key` into analysis and make `getProductData` support an exact trusted cache-key lookup.
- Hide or label products with insufficient data as "needs label photo" instead of opening an error state.

### 2. SECURITY DEFINER RPCs Allow Unauthorized Mutation

Impact: Quota and product-data mutation can be abused from the client/API.

Evidence:
- `increment_scan_count(p_user_id)` updates any `profiles.id = p_user_id` without checking `auth.uid()`: `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:10`.
- `increment_human_food_count(p_user_id)` and `get_human_food_count_today(p_user_id)` do the same: `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:22` and `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:48`.
- Human-food RPCs are explicitly granted to `authenticated, anon`: `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:56`.
- `save_product_data` is `SECURITY DEFINER` and writes directly to `product_data`: `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:20`.
- The app calls `save_product_data` through the normal Supabase client from the OCR fallback path, not through a trusted backend-only job: `services/cache.js:270`, `services/cache.js:275`, `services/cache.js:276`, `services/cache.js:281`, and `services/cache.js:282`.
- The migration creates/recreates `save_product_data(...)` but does not explicitly `REVOKE` default execution from `PUBLIC`, `anon`, or `authenticated`; repository search found no later `GRANT EXECUTE ON FUNCTION save_product_data` or `REVOKE ... save_product_data` migration, so the mutating RPC is not visibly locked down in source control.

Fix:
- Use `auth.uid()` inside all user-scoped RPCs and reject when `auth.uid() IS NULL OR auth.uid() <> p_user_id`.
- Revoke `anon` from quota RPCs.
- Move product-data saves behind an authenticated edge function that validates OCR provenance, ingredient count, and source.
- Explicitly `REVOKE ALL ON FUNCTION ... FROM PUBLIC` before granting minimal roles.
- Add a Supabase permissions test that introspects deployed function privileges and fails if any mutating catalog/quota RPC is executable by `PUBLIC`, `anon`, or broad `authenticated` roles without an in-function ownership/provenance check.

### 3. Paid AI Helper Modes Can Be Abused

Impact: Anonymous users can cause AI spend without going through normal scan limits.

Evidence:
- `identify`, `ingredients_lookup`, and `ocr_ingredients` are valid edge-function modes: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1027`.
- Anonymous IP rate limiting skips those modes: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1034`.
- User quota enforcement also skips them: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1063`.
- `ingredients_lookup` calls OpenAI with user-provided `productName`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1439`.

Fix:
- Rate-limit all modes, including helpers.
- Require a short-lived server-issued scan session ID for helper calls.
- Add stricter input length and request-shape validation to helper modes.
- Consider disabling `ingredients_lookup` if it is unused.

### 4. Secrets And Hardcoded Keys Exist In Local Scripts

Impact: Secret leakage risk and accidental commit risk. Several currently untracked maintenance, seeding, scraping, and test scripts contain live-looking vendor credentials or fallback keys. If those files are committed, shared, uploaded to CI logs, or pasted into support/debug conversations during the marketing push, OpenAI and ScrapingBee spend can be exposed and the Supabase project identity is unnecessarily spread across tooling.

Evidence:
- Local `.env` exists, but is currently ignored and not tracked.
- The affected scripts are currently untracked in git, which makes accidental addition the immediate risk: `scripts/backfill-images.js`, `scripts/build-database.js`, `scripts/fill-gaps.js`, `scripts/mega-scraper/lib.js`, `scripts/save-verified.js`, `scripts/scrape-brand-metadata.js`, `scripts/seed-accurate.js`, `scripts/seed-products.js`, `scripts/seed-universal.js`, `scripts/test-accuracy.js`, `scripts/test-calibration.js`, and `scripts/test-scan-flow.js`.
- `.gitignore` ignores `.env` but does not ignore local `scripts/` scratch/maintenance files, and `git check-ignore` returned no matching ignore rule for the affected scripts: `.gitignore:33`, `.gitignore:34`, and `.gitignore:35`.
- `scripts/scrape-brand-metadata.js` contains ScrapingBee and OpenAI fallback keys: `scripts/scrape-brand-metadata.js:33` and `scripts/scrape-brand-metadata.js:34`.
- `scripts/fill-gaps.js`, `scripts/build-database.js`, and `scripts/mega-scraper/lib.js` contain the same ScrapingBee/OpenAI fallback-key pattern: `scripts/fill-gaps.js:14`, `scripts/fill-gaps.js:15`, `scripts/build-database.js:18`, `scripts/build-database.js:19`, `scripts/mega-scraper/lib.js:8`, and `scripts/mega-scraper/lib.js:9`.
- `scripts/seed-universal.js` hardcodes ScrapingBee, OpenAI, and Supabase anon-style keys without env fallbacks: `scripts/seed-universal.js:14`, `scripts/seed-universal.js:15`, and `scripts/seed-universal.js:17`.
- `scripts/seed-products.js` contains a Supabase anon-style key and an OpenAI fallback key: `scripts/seed-products.js:12` and `scripts/seed-products.js:13`.
- `scripts/backfill-images.js`, `scripts/seed-accurate.js`, `scripts/test-accuracy.js`, `scripts/test-calibration.js`, `scripts/test-scan-flow.js`, and `scripts/save-verified.js` also hardcode Supabase project/anon-style values or ScrapingBee fallback keys: `scripts/backfill-images.js:17`, `scripts/backfill-images.js:19`, `scripts/seed-accurate.js:11`, `scripts/seed-accurate.js:13`, `scripts/test-accuracy.js:27`, `scripts/test-accuracy.js:29`, `scripts/test-calibration.js:33`, `scripts/test-scan-flow.js:17`, and `scripts/save-verified.js:7`.
- `git log --all -- .env ...` returned no tracked history for checked files, but the local files still need cleanup.

Fix:
- Rotate any secret value that ever appeared in scripts or local files.
- Replace hardcoded keys with required env vars.
- Add secret scanning before commit/push.
- Add the local scratch/maintenance scripts to an explicit ignore or move them into a private ops repository if they are not intended to ship with the app.
- Keep seed scripts out of app release bundles and CI artifacts.

## P1 - Product Quality And Conversion

### 5. Store Scanning Is Slow By Design On Misses

Impact: In-store users will abandon if they are holding a product and waiting through multiple AI/network steps.

Evidence:
- Scanner captures a full-quality photo, then resizes/compresses to 1600px before navigation: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:228`.
- Photo flow runs identify first: `services/analysisService.js:583`.
- Then it performs DB lookup only: `services/analysisService.js:644`.
- If the DB misses, scraping is disabled and the app asks for an ingredient-label photo: `services/analysisService.js:638` and `services/analysisService.js:743`.

Fix:
- Show a confirmed product card immediately after identification with a visible next-step timer.
- Add barcode scanning as a faster first path when barcode is visible.
- Preload popular products by retailer/brand before marketing.
- Track stage durations in analytics: capture, upload, identify, DB lookup, cache hit, AI analysis, label prompt.

### 6. Database Contains Low-Quality Searchable Rows

Impact: Search trust degrades when non-food products, bundles, supplements, treats, or thin ingredient rows appear as normal products.

Evidence:
- Live query found 222 search-visible rows with only 3-4 ingredients.
- Sample rows include variety packs, toppers/treats, and a non-food genetic test product.
- `search_products` has no source-quality filter, no pet-food category gate, and no product-type labels.

Fix:
- Add `product_type`, `is_complete_food`, `data_quality_score`, and `visible_in_search` columns.
- Exclude non-food and insufficient rows from search.
- Route treats/toppers/supplements to a different result template and scoring rubric.
- Add a data quarantine table for scraped rows that fail validation.

### 7. Free Quota Accounting Happens After The Result

Impact: Users can potentially consume backend/AI resources before quota is incremented, and failures in client increment paths can undercount usage. The highest-risk concrete path is slow scan abandonment: the background analysis service can finish and save history after Results has unmounted, but quota increments live only in the mounted Results component's `done` effect. That means a user can back out of a long scan, let the paid work finish in the singleton service, and avoid the free-scan counter that should correspond to the completed result.

Evidence:
- Edge function checks server quota but does not increment after success.
- Client increments only from a Results `useEffect` after `done` is true, and it skips errors, history mode, Pro users, and already-counted sessions: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:470`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:471`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:472`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:473`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:482`.
- The analysis service is explicitly designed to survive component unmounts and keep running with zero subscribers: `services/analysisService.js:17`, `services/analysisService.js:19`, `services/analysisService.js:20`, and `services/analysisService.js:21`.
- Results cleanup unsubscribes and clears local timers, but does not count, cancel, or transfer ownership of the pending scan before unmount: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:421`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:422`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:423`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:427`.
- Back and retry paths can leave the current Results instance before the old analysis has completed: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:570`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:575`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:579`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:587`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:588`.
- Background completion still writes local result/history and emits complete events from the service path, independent of whether a Results subscriber is still mounted: `services/analysisService.js:409`, `services/analysisService.js:415`, `services/analysisService.js:416`, `services/analysisService.js:473`, `services/analysisService.js:478`, `services/analysisService.js:480`, `services/analysisService.js:481`, `services/analysisService.js:722`, `services/analysisService.js:727`, and `services/analysisService.js:728`.

Fix:
- Count successful paid AI calls server-side in the edge function.
- Return updated quota in the edge response.
- Keep client local count as a display cache only.
- If a background analysis is intentionally allowed to continue after unmount, make the service own the corresponding quota ledger update; otherwise cancel it before it can finish and save history.
- Add a regression test that starts a slow scan, navigates away before completion, lets the service complete, and verifies server quota/history/accounting remain consistent.

### 8. Product Search Has No Error UI

Impact: If Supabase RPC fails, users just stop seeing results.

Evidence:
- Search catches and logs errors only: `screens/HomeScreen.js:321`.

Fix:
- Add visible search error state with retry.
- Track RPC latency/error rate.
- Add offline-specific search copy.

### 9. Product Names And Brands Are Not Clean Enough For Marketing Traffic

Impact: Search/results can look scraped and unprofessional. This damages trust immediately after a user arrives from an ad.

Live data:
- Rows with `&amp;` in `product_name`: 3,389.
- Rows with any sampled HTML entity in product/brand: 3,528.
- Rows with `brand` starting `Brand:`: 853.
- Amazon-sourced rows: 8,176; Amazon rows with `&amp;` in product name: 3,185.

Examples observed:
- `SIMPLY NOURISH Adult Canned Dog Food. Chicken &amp; Tuna...`
- `Brand: Dr. Marty`
- `Methylation &amp; Longevity Genetic Test...` appearing as a searchable product.

Fix:
- Add a cleanup migration/job to HTML-decode product/brand names and strip `Brand:` prefixes.
- Add a `visible_in_search` or `data_quality_status` gate.
- Re-run search ranking after cleanup; HTML entities and noisy Amazon titles are likely hurting matching.

### 10. Search Ranking Overweights Brand/Substring And Can Return Wrong Variants

Impact: Users can search a specific product and get plausible-looking but wrong variants.

Evidence:
- Live `search_products('open farm beef')` returned Open Farm rows that did not include beef in the top 5. They all scored `0.533`.
- Live `search_products('chicken')` returned high-ingredient variety packs and broad Amazon bundles, not necessarily direct single-SKU matches.
- The RPC ranks with product/brand trigram and substring signals but does not require variant token agreement: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:57`.

Fix:
- Tokenize query and require variant/protein overlap when the query includes a protein/flavor.
- Penalize variety packs unless the query asks for a variety pack.
- Prefer complete-food rows over treats/toppers/bundles.
- Add `product_type` and `is_variety_pack` fields to ranking.

### 11. Legal Copy Does Not Match Current App Behavior And Vendors

Impact: App Review and user trust risk.

Evidence:
- Terms say users "must sign in with Apple or Google": `legal.js:100`, but the app intentionally allows guest scanning.
- Privacy lists Anthropic but not OpenAI, while the analyze edge function uses OpenAI for identify and ingredient lookup: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1439`.
- Privacy says label photos are sent to "our servers" and Anthropic, but identify mode can send images to OpenAI too.

Fix:
- Update privacy/terms to reflect guest mode.
- Add OpenAI and any scraping/data vendors actually used in production.
- Clarify what is stored vs processed transiently: image photos, derived OCR text, scan history, product data contributions.

### 12. Paywall Trial Claims Are Hardcoded, Not Package-Driven

Impact: Subscription conversion and App Store compliance risk if RevenueCat products do not exactly match the copy.

Evidence:
- All plans have `hasTrial: true` in local constants: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:43`.
- Timeline hardcodes `Day 3` reminder and `Day 4` billing: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:65`.
- Trust copy says "Cancel before day 3 and you won't be charged": `screens/PaywallScreen.js:397`.
- Annual monthly equivalent is hardcoded as `$2.50 / month`, not derived from `annualPkg.product.price`.

Fix:
- Read introductory/trial eligibility and period from RevenueCat product metadata.
- Hide trial timeline when the selected package has no intro offer or the user is ineligible.
- Derive annual/monthly equivalent from actual localized price.
- Keep App Store cancellation language generic and accurate.

### 13. Verified Data Badge Exists But Is Not Rendered

Impact: Users cannot easily tell whether a score came from verified ingredients, an AI estimate, OPFF, or user OCR. This matters for trust.

Evidence:
- `DataSourceBadge` is imported in `ResultsScreen`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:59`.
- The component is defined: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2509`.
- It is not rendered in the pet-food result layout.
- Only AI-estimate ingredient source gets a small notice: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1101`.

Fix:
- Render the data-source badge near the title/score for every result.
- Distinguish "verified label", "product database", "user OCR", "AI estimate", and "cached result".
- Include source confidence in history rows where possible.

### 14. Human-Food Safety Entry Is Blocked By Pet-Food Scan Quota

Impact: A free user who has used 3 pet-food scans can be blocked before opening the human-food safety modal, even though human-food has a separate daily quota.

Evidence:
- Human-food card checks `canScan()` and routes to `scan_limit`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:787`.
- The actual submit/photo handlers correctly use `canCheckHumanFood()`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:474` and `screens/HomeScreen.js:488`.
- `services/auth.js` defines separate pet-food and human-food quotas.

Fix:
- Remove the `canScan()` check from the human-food card tap.
- Let users open the modal, then enforce `canCheckHumanFood()` when they submit text or photo.
- Use `human_food_limit` paywall source for human-food gating.

### 15. Onboarding And Support Copy Overpromise Or Describe Old Flows

Impact: Users arriving from marketing will expect instant search and a much larger catalog than exists today.

Evidence:
- Onboarding says "50,000+ products indexed" and "50,000+ verified recipes": `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:90` and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:224`.
- Live `product_data` count is 10,990.
- Support site says to point the camera at the ingredient list and mentions "live scan": `docs/support.html:114` and `docs/support.html:139`.
- Current scanner says to capture the front of the bag first: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:399`.

Fix:
- Replace count claim with the current measured number or a defensible rounded claim.
- Update support docs to describe the current two-step flow: front package first, ingredient label only when needed.
- Avoid "score appears instantly" unless the selected result has a cached analysis hit.

### 16. App Store / Public Site Metadata Has Mismatches

Impact: Public support pages can send users to the wrong App Store listing or show stale legal dates.

Evidence:
- Public site App Store link uses `id6760733995`: `docs/index.html:113`.
- EAS submit config uses `ascAppId` `6760733899`: `eas.json:36`.
- `docs/support.html` footer still says 2025 while app/legal files use 2026.
- `docs/privacy.html` says last updated March 17, 2025 while in-app `legal.js` uses March 16, 2026.

Fix:
- Verify the correct App Store ID and update every public link.
- Keep docs/legal generated from one source of truth.
- Add a release checklist item for legal/support page dates and links.

## P2 - Release Readiness

### 17. Expo SDK Patch Versions Are Behind

Evidence:
- `npx expo-doctor` failed 1 of 19 checks.
- `npx expo install --check` also failed.
- 17 packages are below the patch versions expected by Expo SDK 55, including `expo`, `expo-camera`, `expo-file-system`, `expo-updates`, and `react-native`.

Fix:
- Run `npx expo install --check`, then patch to the expected SDK 55 versions.
- Re-run `npx expo-doctor`.

### 18. Dependency Audit Has 19 Vulnerabilities

Evidence:
- `npm audit --json`: 19 total vulnerabilities: 17 moderate, 2 high.
- High severity packages include `@xmldom/xmldom` and `node-forge`, pulled transitively.

Fix:
- Apply compatible patch updates first.
- Avoid `npm audit fix --force` without testing because it can jump major Expo packages.

### 19. TypeScript Check Is Not Configured For Supabase Edge Functions

Evidence:
- `npx tsc --noEmit` fails on Deno imports and globals in `supabase/functions/*`.

Fix:
- Exclude Supabase edge functions from the app `tsconfig.json`, or add a separate Deno type-check path.
- Add a CI check for app JS bundling and a separate Supabase function check.

### 20. Web Script Is Broken

Evidence:
- `package.json` exposes `"web": "expo start --web"`.
- `npx expo export --platform web` fails because `react-dom` and `react-native-web` are missing.

Fix:
- Either install web dependencies or remove the web script/config from the release surface.

### 21. No Automated Test Script Or CI Gate

Impact: Regressions in scan/search/paywall/security can ship unnoticed.

Evidence:
- `npm test -- --watch=false` fails because there is no `test` script.
- No project-level `.github` workflow, Jest/Vitest config, or app test runner was found outside `node_modules`.
- Existing scripts under `scripts/test-*.js` are standalone utilities, not wired into package scripts or CI.

Fix:
- Add at least smoke tests for search result tap, scan miss flow, quota gating, auth, paywall restore, and history replay.
- Add database contract tests for `search_products` vs `getProductData`.
- Add CI gates for `expo-doctor`, native export/bundle, unit tests, dependency audit, and secret scan.

### 22. Android JS Export Succeeds, But Bundle Is Large And Not Enough As A Release Gate

Evidence:
- `npx expo export --platform android --output-dir /tmp/woof-export-android` succeeded.
- Exported Android JS/Hermes bundle was 7.4 MB; export directory was 8.4 MB.
- Asset folder is 4.5 MB; onboarding PNGs are the largest local assets.

Interpretation:
- This proves the current JS bundles for Android.
- It does not prove camera, RevenueCat, Apple/Google auth, deep links, push updates, Supabase edge functions, or native purchase flows work on a real device.

Fix:
- Keep Android export as a CI smoke gate.
- Add real device acceptance checks for camera capture, store purchase restore, OAuth redirect, and low-signal scan behavior.

### 23. Production Logging Is Too Noisy And Not Structured

Impact: Debugging launch issues will be hard, and console logs can expose product names, auth failures, vendor errors, and user behavior in production logs.

Evidence:
- `rg "console.log\\("` found 650 occurrences in app/source scripts.
- There is no structured analytics/error reporting service in the reviewed code.
- Auth logs the native OAuth redirect URI at module load, and Google sign-in parses access and refresh tokens from the redirect fragment in the same auth module. The tokens are not logged, but this is still a sensitive auth surface that should not rely on raw console logging around redirect handling: `services/auth.js:16`, `services/auth.js:17`, `services/auth.js:398`, `services/auth.js:400`, `services/auth.js:402`, and `services/auth.js:403`.
- Paywall logs the source, product name, score, selected plan, purchase result, and raw purchase error string with `console.log(...)`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:133`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:134`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:168`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:177`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:182`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:184`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:208`.
- Analysis logs user-selected product names and scores for search/OCR/DB-complete paths, which can expose scan behavior in production device or edge logs without consent-aware telemetry controls: `services/analysisService.js:418`, `services/analysisService.js:555`, and `services/analysisService.js:730`.
- The `analyze` edge function logs partial GPT identify output and raw Claude fetch errors, so backend logs can include model output snippets or upstream error objects instead of structured redacted error classes: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1398`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1399`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1548`.

Fix:
- Add a small logging wrapper with environment-based redaction.
- Send only structured, non-sensitive metrics: scan phase durations, cache hit/miss, error class, product data source, paywall source, purchase result.
- Remove or silence raw vendor/product logs in production.
- Define an allowlist of production log fields and explicitly prohibit raw product names, food names, OAuth redirect details, token-bearing URLs, model output snippets, and vendor error objects from console logs.
- Add a release check that fails when app or edge-function code calls `console.log/error` outside the logging wrapper, except in explicitly dev-only scripts.

## Fourth-Pass Launch Blockers

### 24. AuthProvider Has A Temporal-Dead-Zone Startup Crash Risk

Impact: The app can crash while rendering the auth provider before users reach the home screen.

Evidence:
- `fetchProfile` is created with `useCallback` before `_readLocalHumanFood` and `_writeLocalHumanFood` are declared: `services/auth.js:48` and `services/auth.js:100`.
- Those helpers are declared later as `const` callbacks: `services/auth.js:152` and `services/auth.js:163`.
- JavaScript evaluates the dependency array immediately, so reading those `const` bindings before initialization raises `ReferenceError: Cannot access ... before initialization`.
- `App.js` wraps the app in `AuthProvider`: `App.js:217`.

Fix:
- Move `_readLocalHumanFood` and `_writeLocalHumanFood` above `fetchProfile`, or change them to hoisted function declarations.
- Add a startup smoke test that renders `AuthProvider` and reaches `Home`.
- Do not rely on `expo export`; bundling succeeded but does not prove this render path is safe.

### 25. Users Can Self-Grant Pro Or Reset Quotas Through Profile Updates

Impact: Revenue and quota enforcement can be bypassed by any authenticated user who calls Supabase directly.

Evidence:
- The profile RLS policy allows users to update their own profile row: `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:18`.
- Subscription/quota columns are added to the same table: `supabase/migrations/003_scan_count.sql:2`.
- The client writes `is_pro` directly after RevenueCat status checks: `services/auth.js:108`.
- The client also contains direct profile updates for resetting `scan_count` and `human_food_count`: `services/auth.js:429` and `services/auth.js:438`.

Fix:
- Revoke broad client `UPDATE` on sensitive profile columns.
- Split editable profile fields from entitlement/quota fields, or enforce column-specific update policies.
- Update `is_pro`, `scan_count`, and human-food quota only from trusted server-side code after validating RevenueCat/App Store state.

### 26. Android RevenueCat Configuration Is Not Proven And Can Fall Back To A Placeholder Key

Impact: Android purchases, restores, and pro-status checks can silently fail even if the Android bundle exports.

Evidence:
- `app.config.js` only passes RevenueCat keys from environment variables: `app.config.js:10`.
- `services/purchases.js` falls back to `"goog_YOUR_ANDROID_KEY"` when `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_ANDROID` is missing: `services/purchases.js:7`.
- The local `.env` key inventory has `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_IOS` but no `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_ANDROID`.
- `eas.json` has a production Android build/submit path: `eas.json:24` and `eas.json:40`.

Fix:
- Make missing RevenueCat keys a build-time failure for each target platform.
- Verify EAS production secrets contain both iOS and Android keys.
- Add a real-device Android purchase/restore acceptance test before Android marketing.

### 27. Product Lookup Service-Role Bypass Trusts An Unverified JWT Payload

Impact: Attackers can avoid anonymous rate limiting for the public product-lookup function by sending a forged JWT-like string whose decoded payload says `role: service_role`.

Evidence:
- `product-lookup` is configured with `verify_jwt = false`: `supabase/config.toml:5`.
- The function decodes the JWT payload with `atob(token.split(".")[1])`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1061`.
- It sets `isServiceRole = true` based only on `payload.role === "service_role"`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1062`.
- Anonymous rate limiting is skipped when `isServiceRole` is true: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1080`.

Fix:
- Never trust decoded JWT claims without signature verification.
- Remove the service-role bypass from public functions, or verify service-role calls with Supabase JWT validation plus an internal secret.
- Keep product lookup disabled from the client until this is fixed.

### 28. Store Scan Flow Still Has A Retail-Aisle Latency Problem

Impact: Even when the scan eventually works, the current path can take too long for a user standing in a store.

Evidence:
- Camera capture asks for the front of the bag first, not the ingredient panel: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:226` and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:399`.
- The first AI identification call has a 15 second timeout: `services/claude.js:671`.
- If the database misses, the flow pauses and asks for an ingredient-label photo: `services/analysisService.js:743`.
- Ingredient OCR has a 20 second timeout: `services/claude.js:729`.
- Verified/photo analysis can try streaming twice and then fall back to non-streaming with a 90 second timeout: `services/claude.js:490` and `services/claude.js:511`.
- The outer hard timeout is 120 seconds: `services/analysisService.js:24`.
- The UI only marks loading as slow after 20 seconds: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:442`.

Fix:
- Define a store-scan SLA: first useful state under 3 seconds, next action under 8 seconds, hard failure/fallback under 15 seconds.
- Add barcode scanning or barcode lookup as the first fast path.
- If identification succeeds but DB misses, immediately show the product confirmation and one-tap label capture instead of waiting behind long analysis fallbacks.
- Instrument phase timings in production-safe analytics and measure p50/p90/p95 before paid acquisition.

## Fifth-Pass Release And Public-Surface Findings

### 29. Generated Android Manifest Requests Microphone Permission

Impact: Google Play privacy disclosures and user trust can be hurt by a microphone permission that the app does not appear to need.

Evidence:
- `app.json` explicitly lists only `INTERNET` and `CAMERA`: `app.json:38`.
- `npx expo config --json` generated Android permissions including `android.permission.RECORD_AUDIO`.
- Static search found still-photo camera usage through `takePictureAsync`, but no app code using video/audio recording.
- `expo-camera` is configured with a camera permission string only: `app.json:55`.

Fix:
- Configure the camera plugin to avoid microphone permission if video/audio is not needed.
- Re-run `npx expo config --json` and inspect generated native manifests before EAS production build.
- Keep Play Console data-safety declarations aligned with the final permissions.

### 30. Public Website App Store Link Is Broken

Impact: Paid traffic from the website can land on a 404 instead of the app listing.

Evidence:
- Public site links to `https://apps.apple.com/app/id6760733995`: `docs/index.html:113`.
- EAS submit config uses App Store Connect ID `6760733899`: `eas.json:36`.
- Direct HTTP check on June 5, 2026: `https://apps.apple.com/app/id6760733995` returned `404`.
- Direct HTTP check on June 5, 2026: `https://apps.apple.com/us/app/id6760733899` returned `200` and resolved to `Woof - Pet Food Scanner`.

Fix:
- Replace every public App Store URL with the canonical listing: `https://apps.apple.com/us/app/woof-pet-food-scanner/id6760733899`.
- Add link checking to release/marketing CI.
- Check support, privacy, terms, emails, and ad destination URLs before campaigns go live.

### 31. App Store Listing Copy Overpromises Current Scan Behavior

Impact: Users acquired from App Store search or ads may churn when the first scan is slower or less universal than the listing implies.

Evidence:
- Current App Store listing for ID `6760733899` says the app scans any dog/cat label and analyzes ingredients in seconds.
- The current scanner first captures the front of the bag: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:399`.
- If database lookup misses, the app pauses and asks for an ingredient-label photo: `services/analysisService.js:743`.
- The app has multiple long AI timeouts: 15 seconds for identification, 20 seconds for OCR, and up to 120 seconds outer analysis timeout.
- Live database checks found only 10,990 `product_data` rows and quality issues in searchable data.

Fix:
- Rewrite App Store copy around the actual flow: front-package identification, database match when available, label-photo fallback when needed.
- Avoid universal claims until the scan miss path is consistently fast and accurate on real devices.
- Add App Store copy review to the launch checklist any time scan/search behavior changes.

### 32. Ingredient-Label Recovery Screen Has Weaker Error And Offline Handling Than The Main Scanner

Impact: The most important recovery path after a database miss can fail silently or waste time.

Evidence:
- Main scanner checks network before capture and shows an alert: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:208`.
- Ingredient capture does not use the network state and does not preflight connectivity before taking the second photo: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:21`.
- Ingredient capture uses `const [permission] = useCameraPermissions()` but does not expose a permission request button: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:17`.
- On capture failure, it logs and clears loading state but shows no user-facing error: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:53`.
- The "Skip - use AI estimate instead" path navigates to `photo_with_ingredients` without `ingredientBase64`: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:59`.
- `_runPhotoWithIngredients` immediately calls OCR with that missing `ingredientBase64`, then falls back only after OCR failure: `services/analysisService.js:506`.

Fix:
- Give the ingredient capture screen the same offline, permission request, and capture-error UX as the main scanner.
- Split "AI estimate" into its own explicit mode instead of intentionally entering the OCR path with no image.
- Track recovery-step dropoff: identified product, label capture opened, label captured, OCR success, final result delivered.

### 33. Account Deletion Does Not Prove "All Associated Data" Is Removed

Impact: Legal/privacy trust risk. The UI and public privacy docs promise deletion of account and associated data, but local and contributed data paths remain.

Evidence:
- Profile delete copy says it deletes account, scan history, and associated data: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:75`.
- Public privacy page says users can delete account and all associated data from Profile: `docs/privacy.html:118`.
- Server RPC deletes `rate_limits` and the auth user, relying on cascade for `profiles` and `scan_history`: `supabase/migrations/006_delete_account.sql:12`.
- Client `deleteAccount` clears scan-count and human-food quota keys only: `services/auth.js:457`.
- It does not call `clearHistory()`, remove user-specific `@woof/scan_history_*`, remove local result cache keys, or clear recent searches.
- User OCR can write product rows with source `user_ocr`: `services/analysisService.js:534`, but `product_data` has no user owner column for later deletion.

Fix:
- On account deletion, clear all local user data: scan history, result cache, recent searches, migration flags, and quota mirrors.
- Add ownership metadata to contributed product rows, or change legal copy to explain that anonymized product contributions may remain.
- Add an account-deletion test that signs in, scans/saves history, deletes, restarts, and verifies no local or remote personal data remains.

## Sixth-Pass Runtime And Code-Quality Findings

### 34. Lint Gate Is Missing, And First Expo Lint Run Finds Real Errors

Impact: Preventable runtime and release defects are not being caught before build/submission.

Evidence:
- `package.json` does not define a lint script.
- Running `npx expo lint` on June 5, 2026 auto-configured ESLint, then reported 178 problems: 27 errors and 151 warnings.
- Errors included app source files, scripts, and Supabase functions.
- Notable app-source error: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:625` reports `cacheDirectory` not found in the `expo-file-system` namespace.
- Notable hook warnings include missing dependencies in `ResultsScreen` analysis startup and subscription effects: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:371`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:430`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:519`.

Fix:
- Add an intentional `eslint.config.js`, not the one-time auto-generated state.
- Scope linting separately for React Native app code, Node scripts, and Deno Supabase functions so environment globals are correct.
- Make lint a CI gate after either fixing or explicitly suppressing known-safe rules.

### 35. Results Screen Can Crash On Missing Route Params

Impact: A bad deep link, stale navigation state, or accidental route open can crash before the user sees an error state.

Evidence:
- `ResultsScreen` destructures `route.params` without a fallback: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:179`.
- Other route-driven screens defensively use `route.params || {}`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:105`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:95`, `screens/WebViewScreen.js:10`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:12`.
- The Results screen is a central destination for scan, search, history, human-food, and ingredient-label recovery flows.

Fix:
- Change Results route param handling to `route.params || {}`.
- Validate required params per mode and render a recovery error with "Scan again" / "Back home" actions.
- Add navigation smoke tests for missing or malformed params.

### 36. Pro Shareable Score Card Uses SDK 55 FileSystem APIs That Throw

Impact: A paid feature can silently degrade from image sharing to text sharing, reducing perceived Pro value.

Evidence:
- Pro sharing captures a score-card image, then calls `FileSystem.cacheDirectory`, `FileSystem.copyAsync`, and `FileSystem.deleteAsync`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:625`.
- The installed `expo-file-system` version is `55.0.11`.
- SDK 55's main `expo-file-system` export uses the new `File`, `Directory`, and `Paths` API.
- Legacy `copyAsync` and `deleteAsync` imported from `expo-file-system` intentionally throw at runtime and require either the new API or `expo-file-system/legacy`: `node_modules/expo-file-system/src/legacyWarnings.ts:62` and `node_modules/expo-file-system/src/legacyWarnings.ts:83`.
- `npx expo lint` also flags `FileSystem.cacheDirectory` as missing from the imported namespace.

Fix:
- Either import legacy APIs from `expo-file-system/legacy`, or migrate to `new File(Paths.cache, ...)` and `File.copy()` / `File.delete()`.
- Add a real-device share-card acceptance test for iOS and Android.
- If image sharing fails, show a user-facing fallback message instead of silently downgrading.

## Seventh-Pass Conversion And Support Findings

### 37. Paywall Shows Fallback Prices Before Products Are Actually Purchasable

Impact: Users can see prices and a "Try Free" CTA even when RevenueCat offerings are unavailable, then hit a "Not Available" alert. That is a direct conversion loss.

Evidence:
- `getOfferings()` returns `null` on failure: `services/purchases.js:45`.
- Paywall stores the offering but has no loading/error state beyond `offerings = null`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:97`.
- Price labels fall back to hardcoded values when packages are missing: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:149`.
- All plan rows remain selectable regardless of whether the corresponding package exists: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:289`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:315`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:333`.
- Purchase only discovers the missing package after CTA tap and shows an alert: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:163`.

Fix:
- Show an explicit loading state until RevenueCat offerings are loaded.
- Disable or hide plan rows whose packages are missing.
- Replace fallback prices with package-derived prices only; if unavailable, show a retry/support state.
- Log offering load failures as a launch-blocking monetization event.

### 38. Support Restore Instructions Do Not Match The App

Impact: Paying users who need restore help can be sent to the wrong screen/action.

Evidence:
- Support FAQ says: "Go to your Profile in the app and tap Restore Purchases": `docs/support.html:128`.
- Profile's subscription row opens system subscription management when `isPro`, or navigates to Paywall when not Pro: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:223`.
- There is no `Restore Purchases` button on `ProfileScreen`.
- The restore button is inside `PaywallScreen`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:410`.

Fix:
- Add a visible Restore Purchases action to Profile for signed-in and guest users, or update support copy to say Profile > Upgrade > Restore Purchases.
- Add a support acceptance check: user with stale entitlement can find restore in under 2 taps.
- Keep public support FAQ generated from the same copy source as in-app support/legal text.

## Eighth-Pass Database And Schema Findings

### 39. Scan History Sync Uses Upsert But RLS Does Not Allow Update

Impact: authenticated history sync and migration can fail for existing rows, leaving history inconsistent across devices.

Evidence:
- `scan_history` RLS has SELECT, INSERT, and DELETE policies only: `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:61`.
- No migration adds an UPDATE policy for `scan_history`.
- `addHistoryEntry` writes to Supabase with `.upsert(..., { onConflict: "id,user_id" })`: `services/history.js:194`.
- `migrateLocalHistoryToSupabase` also uses `.upsert(...)`: `services/history.js:279`.
- Later history migration adds `product_image_url` but does not add an UPDATE policy: `supabase/migrations/022_history_image_url.sql:3`.

Fix:
- Either add a user-owned UPDATE policy for `scan_history`, or change client sync to insert-only with conflict-ignore semantics.
- Add a contract test that creates a local row, syncs it, syncs it again, and confirms no RLS error.
- Surface history sync failures in telemetry instead of only console logs.

### 40. Guest Users Cannot Directly Benefit From Shared Analysis Cache Prewarm

Impact: guest users, the top of the acquisition funnel, can miss instant cached results and wait for an unnecessary edge-function roundtrip.

Evidence:
- Guest mode is supported throughout the app.
- `analysis_cache` SELECT policy is granted only `TO authenticated`: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:25`.
- Home search prewarms visible results by querying `analysis_cache` directly from the client: `screens/HomeScreen.js:315` and `services/cache.js:312`.
- Search/photo analysis checks `getCachedAnalysis()` on the client before calling the edge function: `services/analysisService.js:341` and `services/analysisService.js:656`.
- Live anon-key read-only check on June 5, 2026 saw zero visible `analysis_cache` rows.

Fix:
- Decide explicitly whether guest users may read shared cached analyses.
- If yes, add an anon-safe SELECT policy for non-sensitive shared cache rows.
- If no, move cache prewarm/hit checks behind an edge function so guests still get fast cached results without broad table access.

### 41. Cache Hit Counters Likely Never Increment From The Client

Impact: popularity metrics, prewarming decisions, and product-ranking analytics based on `hit_count` can be wrong.

Evidence:
- `increment_cache_hit(p_key)` is a plain SQL function, not `SECURITY DEFINER`: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:47`.
- It updates `analysis_cache.hit_count`: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:49`.
- `analysis_cache` UPDATE policy allows only `auth.role() = 'service_role'`: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:38`.
- Client cache hits call `supabase.rpc("increment_cache_hit", ...)` fire-and-forget: `services/cache.js:397`.
- Because the function runs as invoker, anon/authenticated callers are still subject to RLS and cannot update the row.

Fix:
- Move hit counting into the edge function/service-role path, or make a narrowly scoped `SECURITY DEFINER` RPC that only increments hit counters.
- Add telemetry/tests that prove hit_count increases after a cache hit.
- Do not use `hit_count` for prioritization until the counter path is verified.

## Ninth-Pass Native Release Configuration Findings

### 42. Required Runtime Environment Values Are Not Validated At Build Time

Impact: EAS can produce a build with missing Supabase or RevenueCat configuration, leading to blank network clients, broken auth/search/scan, or non-working purchases.

Evidence:
- `app.config.js` injects `SUPABASE_URL`, `SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `GOOGLE_WEB_CLIENT_ID`, `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_IOS`, and `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_ANDROID` directly from `process.env`: `app.config.js:7`.
- It does not throw if a required value is missing.
- `config/env.js` falls back to empty strings for Supabase values: `config/env.js:15`.
- `services/supabase.js` creates the Supabase client from those values: `services/supabase.js:5`.
- Generated Expo config on June 5, 2026 included `SUPABASE_URL`, `SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`, `GOOGLE_WEB_CLIENT_ID`, and `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_IOS`, but did not include `REVENUECAT_API_KEY_ANDROID`.

Fix:
- Add build-time validation in `app.config.js` for required values per platform/profile.
- Fail production builds when Supabase or platform RevenueCat keys are missing.
- Add a redacted `expo config --json` check to CI so every production build proves its required `extra` values exist.

### 43. Android Play Submit Configuration Is Not Public-Launch Ready

Impact: Android marketing cannot be scaled from the current submit setup without changing release track and credential handling.

Evidence:
- Production Android submit is configured with `"track": "internal"`: `eas.json:40`.
- Production Android submit expects `serviceAccountKeyPath` at `./google-services.json`: `eas.json:39`.
- No `google-services.json` file was found in the project root during the audit.
- The generated Android config uses package `com.app.woof`: `app.json:37`.

Fix:
- Decide whether Android is part of the marketing launch.
- If yes, configure Play Console release track intentionally: internal for QA, closed/open testing for beta, production for public marketing.
- Store Google Play service-account credentials securely through EAS/CI and verify `eas submit --platform android --profile production` before launch.

## Tenth-Pass Runtime Security And Store-Speed Findings

### 44. Supabase Auth Session Tokens Are Persisted In AsyncStorage

Impact: If a device backup, rooted device, debug tooling, or another local compromise exposes app storage, long-lived Supabase refresh tokens are easier to extract than they would be with platform secure storage. This is a user-account security risk before scaling sign-ups.

Evidence:
- The Supabase client is configured with `storage: AsyncStorage`, `autoRefreshToken: true`, and `persistSession: true`: `services/supabase.js:6`.
- `@react-native-async-storage/async-storage` is a normal dependency: `package.json:13`.
- No `expo-secure-store` dependency or secure storage adapter exists in `package.json`.
- The app uses persistent Apple/Google auth sessions through Supabase: `services/auth.js:349` and `services/auth.js:381`.

Fix:
- Add a Supabase auth storage adapter backed by `expo-secure-store` on native platforms.
- Keep AsyncStorage only for non-sensitive preferences and caches.
- On migration, sign users out or carefully rehydrate existing sessions into secure storage.
- Document the storage model in the privacy/security review.

### 45. Barcode Fast Path Exists But Is Not Exposed Or Reachable

Impact: The app has code for the fastest in-store lookup path, but users cannot trigger it. That keeps the live store experience dependent on slower front-photo identification and database lookup, which is exactly where latency and "not in database" complaints show up.

Evidence:
- `analysisService.startAnalysis` supports `mode === "barcode"` and routes to `_runBarcode`: `services/analysisService.js:161` and `services/analysisService.js:212`.
- `_runBarcode` performs a quick OPFF lookup and caches the result: `services/analysisService.js:245`.
- `services/opff.js` implements `lookupBarcode(barcode)` with a 4-second timeout and local cache: `services/opff.js:88`.
- `ScannerScreen` renders `CameraView` without `onBarcodeScanned` or `barcodeScannerSettings`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:319`.
- `ScannerScreen` only navigates to `Results` with `mode: "photo"` or `mode: "human_food"`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:247`.
- `ResultsScreen` destructures no `barcode` param and calls `startAnalysis` without a `barcode` argument: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:179` and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:358`.
- Static search found no app call that navigates with `mode: "barcode"`.

Fix:
- Add barcode scanning to `CameraView` with supported UPC/EAN formats.
- Add a segmented scanner mode or automatic barcode detection while the camera is open.
- Pass `{ mode: "barcode", barcode }` through navigation and `ResultsScreen` into `startAnalysis`.
- Track barcode hit/miss latency separately from photo identification.
- Use barcode as the default store-speed path when visible, with photo identification as fallback.

### 46. Public Product Lookup Can Spend ScrapingBee Credits And Write Cache Rows

Impact: Anyone who can call the edge function can trigger third-party scraping work and potentially fill `product_data` with new rows. The current protection is only an anonymous IP limit, and a separate finding already shows that forged service-role JWT payloads can bypass that limit.

Evidence:
- `product-lookup` has Supabase JWT verification disabled: `supabase/config.toml:5`.
- The function uses wildcard CORS: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:4`.
- Anonymous requests are allowed and rate-limited by IP at 10 requests per hour: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1078`.
- When `SCRAPINGBEE_API_KEY` is configured, the handler runs Amazon/OPFF, then DFA/CFA/universal ScrapingBee lookups on misses: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1174`.
- Comments document ScrapingBee credit cost for lookup tiers: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:147` and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:527`.
- Successful scraped results are upserted into `product_data` using the service-role Supabase client: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1240`.
- The request validates only that `productName` is a string with length at least 3; there is no maximum length or allowlist for unauthenticated use: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1114`.

Fix:
- Require authenticated users or a server-issued scan session for ScrapingBee-backed lookup tiers.
- Keep OPFF-only lookup available to guests if needed, but gate paid scraping behind quota/entitlement checks.
- Cap `productName`, `brand`, and derived query length.
- Add source-quality fields and quarantine scraped rows before making them searchable.
- Add budget alerts and per-mode telemetry for ScrapingBee spend, cache writes, and lookup misses.

## Eleventh-Pass Recall And Trust Findings

### 47. Recall Claims Are More Authoritative Than The Live Coverage Supports

Impact: Marketing copy promises recall alerts, but the live authoritative recall table is sparse. When no FDA-backed row matches a brand, the app can still display AI-inferred recall fields as if "No recalls found" means the product/brand was checked against a complete source.

Evidence:
- Public website feature copy says "Recall Alerts" and "Know if a product has been recalled": `docs/index.html:146`.
- Support says Pro includes "recall alerts": `docs/support.html:124`.
- The analyze prompt tells the model to use training-data knowledge for recall history: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:199` and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:241`.
- `applyBrandProfile` overrides recall fields only when `get_brand_profile` returns a matched recall brand with `recall_count > 0`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:888`.
- `RecallCard` displays severity `none` as "No recalls found for this product or brand.": `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:1877`.
- Live production checks on June 5, 2026 found `brand_recalls` has 22 rows covering an estimated 22 of 1,949 distinct product-data brand strings. `brand_metadata` has 95 rows covering an estimated 151 of 1,949 distinct brand strings.
- Live product data contains brand normalization problems that reduce matching, including top uncovered brands such as `stella &amp; chewy's`, `brand: generic`, and `nutrish`.

Fix:
- Only show "No recalls found" when a current authoritative recall source was actually queried for that matched brand.
- Add `recallCheckedAt`, `recallSource`, and `recallMatchConfidence` to analysis output.
- For unmatched brands, show "Recall record not verified" instead of "No recalls found."
- Expand and regularly refresh `brand_recalls`, and add monitoring for brand coverage percentage before using recall alerts in paid marketing.
- Fix brand HTML entities/prefixes before recall matching.

### 48. Top Summary Can Hide Recall Status Even When The Safety Section Has It

Impact: Users scanning results quickly can miss recall risk because the high-level summary card has a recall row implementation, but the data produced by analysis does not populate the fields that row requires.

Evidence:
- `SummaryRows` only renders the "Recall history" row when `result.recallCount` exists or `result.recalls` is an array: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:798`.
- The analyze output schema includes `recallSeverity` and `recallHistory`, but not `recallCount` or `recalls`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:93` and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:130`.
- `applyBrandProfile` sets `analysis.recallSeverity`, `analysis.recallHistory`, and `analysis.recallSource`, but not `recallCount`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:889`.
- The lower Safety section renders from `recallHistory`/`recallSeverity`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1115`.
- Result: a major recall can be shown lower on the page while the top summary omits the recall row entirely.

Fix:
- Add `recallCount` and `recallMostRecentDate` to the analysis result when `get_brand_profile` returns them.
- Or change `SummaryRows` to derive recall status from `recallSeverity` and `recallSource`.
- For safety-sensitive rows, prefer "Unknown" over hiding the row when recall state is unverified.
- Add a fixture/test for FDA-verified recall, AI-unknown recall, and no-authoritative-match states.

## Twelfth-Pass Privacy And History Findings

### 49. Scan Photo URIs Are Retained Despite Privacy Copy Saying Photos Are Not Stored

Impact: Privacy and trust risk. The app says scan photos are not stored after processing, but the local history path stores the original camera URI and can sync that local URI to Supabase. This can also create broken cross-device history thumbnails because a local file URI from one device is meaningless on another.

Evidence:
- Public privacy copy says camera images are processed in real time and "not stored permanently": `docs/privacy.html:84`.
- In-app privacy copy says photos "are not stored after processing": `legal.js:40`.
- Scanner captures a local `photo.uri` and passes it to Results: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:228` and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:249`.
- `startAnalysis` stores that URI in analysis state: `services/analysisService.js:204`.
- `_saveHistory` persists it as `photoUri`: `services/analysisService.js:852`.
- `addHistoryEntry` always writes history to AsyncStorage: `services/history.js:175`.
- Authenticated history upsert includes `photo_uri`: `services/history.js:65`.
- The initial `scan_history` schema includes a `photo_uri` column: `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:52`.
- Home history renders `item.photoUri` as an image thumbnail when no product image exists: `screens/HomeScreen.js:161`.

Fix:
- Decide the product policy: either do not retain scan image URIs, or explicitly disclose local thumbnail retention.
- Prefer product images from verified sources for history thumbnails.
- Do not sync local device file URIs to Supabase; store remote image URLs only when intentionally uploaded with consent.
- If thumbnails are retained locally, add a clear retention window and delete them on history clear/account deletion.
- Update privacy copy and App Store privacy answers to match actual behavior.

## Thirteenth-Pass Offline, QA Gate, And Accessibility Findings

### 50. Accuracy And Scan-Flow Scripts Are Production-Bound, Costly, And Not Release-Grade Gates

Impact: The repo contains useful manual quality scripts, but they are not wired into package scripts/CI and several hit production Supabase edge functions or third-party services with hardcoded keys. That makes launch verification non-reproducible, potentially costly, and risky to run casually.

Evidence:
- `package.json` has only `start`, `android`, `ios`, and `web` scripts; there is no `test`, `lint`, `doctor`, `accuracy`, or `calibration` script.
- `scripts/test-accuracy.js` hardcodes the Supabase project URL, Supabase anon key, and a ScrapingBee fallback key: `scripts/test-accuracy.js:27`.
- `scripts/test-calibration.js` hardcodes the deployed analyze URL and Supabase anon key: `scripts/test-calibration.js:31`.
- `scripts/test-scan-flow.js` hardcodes the Supabase URL and anon key: `scripts/test-scan-flow.js:16`.
- `scripts/test-calibration.js` says it requires the deployed analyze edge function: `scripts/test-calibration.js:25`.
- `node scripts/test-scoring-math.js` passed locally with 24/24 checks, but it tests only a Node mirror of scoring normalization.
- `node scripts/test-scan-flow.js` passed the two Canidae matcher/verified-analysis cases, but the script header says it skips actual photo identification. The two verified analysis calls took 19.4s and 18.3s.

Fix:
- Move hardcoded URLs/keys to required env vars and remove fallback service keys.
- Add package scripts such as `test:unit`, `test:scan-flow`, `test:calibration`, and `test:accuracy`.
- Split CI-safe unit tests from opt-in production smoke tests.
- Add a stubbed/local edge-function test path for search/scan parity so it can run without spending AI/ScrapingBee credits.
- Require an explicit `LIVE_PROD_SMOKE=1` flag before scripts hit production services.

### 51. Offline Detection Starts Optimistically Online And Does Not Preflight On App Launch

Impact: A user who opens the app in a store with no signal can be allowed into capture/analysis before the app knows it is offline. That creates a slow failure path instead of an immediate "connect to internet" state.

Evidence:
- `NetworkContext` defaults to `isOnline: true`: `services/network.js:21`.
- Module state also starts as `_onlineState = true`: `services/network.js:25`.
- `NetworkProvider` initializes React state to `true`: `services/network.js:80`.
- The provider only runs `recheck()` on AppState `"active"` changes, not on mount: `services/network.js:126`.
- A single failed ping does not flip to offline; the app waits for reported network errors: `services/network.js:96`.
- `HomeScreen.handleScan` navigates to Scanner without checking network: `screens/HomeScreen.js:446`.
- `ScannerScreen` preflights only the cached `isOnline` value before capture: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:208`.

Fix:
- Run `recheck()` on `NetworkProvider` mount and expose a `checking` state.
- On scan CTA tap, perform a fresh network check or block capture while network state is unknown.
- Flip offline after a failed explicit preflight for network-required actions.
- Add low-signal/airplane-mode acceptance tests for launch, scan tap, capture, search, and result retry.

### 52. Accessibility Metadata Is Incomplete On Critical Controls

Impact: Users relying on VoiceOver/TalkBack will have a rougher experience, and App Review/manual QA can flag missing semantics on purchase, scanner recovery, and error states. This matters before scaling consumer acquisition.

Evidence:
- Static control count found many interactive controls without labels/roles: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js` has 12 touchables but only 2 `accessibilityLabel` entries and 1 `accessibilityRole`; `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js` has 2 touchables and no accessibility labels or roles.
- `IngredientCaptureScreen` renders camera capture/back controls with no accessibility metadata: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:24`.
- `ErrorState` retry button is a `TouchableOpacity` without `accessibilityRole`, `accessibilityLabel`, or disabled state: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2798`.
- Paywall pricing rows are pressable plan selectors but do not expose button/radio role or selected state: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:291`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:317`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:335`.
- Several animated/visual result controls rely on icons or custom rows; there is no automated accessibility audit in package scripts.

Fix:
- Add `accessibilityRole`, `accessibilityLabel`, `accessibilityHint`, and selected/disabled state to all tappable controls.
- Treat plan rows as selectable controls with `accessibilityState={{ selected: ... }}`.
- Add labels to ingredient capture controls and result error/retry CTAs.
- Add a manual VoiceOver/TalkBack pass to the launch checklist for onboarding, scan, label recovery, search, results, paywall, restore, and account deletion.
- Add lint rules or component tests that catch missing labels on custom controls.

## Fourteenth-Pass Native Identity And Update Findings

### 53. Native App Display Name Is Lowercase In Release Config

Impact: The product is branded as "Woof" across the app UI, public docs, and App Store listing, but Expo's native app name is configured as lowercase "woof". That can surface as a lower-polish home-screen/app-switcher identity and makes the release artifacts inconsistent with the public brand before paid traffic arrives.

Evidence:
- Expo native config sets `"name": "woof"`: `app.json:3`.
- The app UI uses "Woof" as the visible product name: `screens/HomeScreen.js:549`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:59`, and `screens/AuthScreen.js:142`.
- Public docs use "Woof - Pet Food Scanner" and hero title "Woof": `docs/index.html:6` and `docs/index.html:111`.
- The live App Store metadata for the working app id resolves to "Woof - Pet Food Scanner" based on the App Store HTTP check performed during this audit.

Fix:
- Change Expo `"name"` to `"Woof"` and verify generated iOS `CFBundleDisplayName` and Android `app_name` in a production build.
- Add a release checklist item that compares app icon label, splash, app switcher, store listing, website title, and support/legal pages.

### 54. iPad/Tablet Support Is Declared Without Tablet-Specific QA Evidence

Impact: iOS tablet support is declared, so iPad users and App Review can exercise a scanner experience that appears designed and tuned for phone portrait dimensions. A poor iPad camera overlay or paywall/search layout can damage first impressions even if the phone build is acceptable.

Evidence:
- Expo iOS config declares `"supportsTablet": true`: `app.json:23`.
- The app locks orientation to portrait: `app.json:8`.
- Scanner overlay geometry is based on `Dimensions.get("window")` with a fixed 260px scan square and static percentages: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:35`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:36`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:37`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:38`.
- The mask and instruction placement use those fixed constants directly: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:328`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:331`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:449`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:451`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:500`.
- Current launch/test gates do not include any iPad/tablet run; existing package scripts only start Expo and there is no device matrix script or checklist entry in `package.json`.

Fix:
- Either set `supportsTablet` to false for the first launch or complete an iPad QA pass for onboarding, scanner, ingredient recovery, search, results, paywall, restore, profile, and legal web views.
- Make scanner geometry responsive with min/max constraints and tablet-safe instruction placement.
- Capture iPad screenshots for App Store Connect if tablet support remains enabled.

### 55. OTA Updates Are Enabled Without A Release Or Rollback Gate

Impact: Expo Updates can change production JavaScript after store approval. That is useful, but without a documented update gate, staged rollout plan, crash monitoring, and rollback process, a bad OTA can break the scan funnel for already-acquired users while marketing is running.

Evidence:
- `expo-updates` is installed: `package.json:31`.
- Expo update URL is configured: `app.json:14`.
- Runtime version follows `appVersion`, so updates share a production runtime until the native app version changes: `app.json:11`.
- EAS production builds publish to `"channel": "production"`: `eas.json:21`.
- Package scripts do not include `eas update`, update validation, rollback, or production smoke-test commands: `package.json:5`.
- Earlier audit findings already show no automated test script/CI gate, noisy production logging, and no proven crash/error telemetry gate.

Fix:
- Add an OTA release checklist: build provenance, branch/channel, runtime version, smoke tests, manual device install, staged rollout, monitoring window, and rollback command.
- Add crash/error telemetry before using production OTA updates during marketing campaigns.
- Require the scan/search/paywall/offline smoke suite before publishing to the production channel.
- Document when a change requires a native store build instead of OTA.

## Fifteenth-Pass Subscription, Legal WebView, And Account Journey Findings

### 56. RevenueCat Identity Can Stay Anonymous After A Guest User Signs In

Impact: Guest users can open the app, initialize purchases anonymously, then sign in later. Because the RevenueCat wrapper uses a module-level `initialized` flag and returns early on subsequent calls, RevenueCat may remain configured for the anonymous app user instead of the signed-in Supabase user. That can make entitlement checks, restore behavior, and cross-device subscription support harder to reason about during conversion traffic.

Evidence:
- `initializePurchases(userId)` returns immediately when `initialized` is true: `services/purchases.js:10` and `services/purchases.js:13`.
- It configures RevenueCat with `appUserID: userId`: `services/purchases.js:15` and `services/purchases.js:20`.
- On cold start with no Supabase session, `AuthProvider` calls `initializePurchases(null)` for guest users: `services/auth.js:292` and `services/auth.js:294`.
- On later sign-in, the auth state handler calls `initializePurchases(s.user.id)`, but that call is skipped if the guest init already set `initialized = true`: `services/auth.js:307` and `services/auth.js:317`.
- The app never calls a RevenueCat identity transition method such as log-in/log-out; repository search found only local `initializePurchases`, `resetPurchases`, `getCustomerInfo`, `getOfferings`, `purchasePackage`, and `restoreTransactions` calls.

Fix:
- Track the configured RevenueCat app user id, not just a boolean.
- When a guest signs in, call the RevenueCat identity transition API and then refresh customer info.
- On sign-out/delete, call the RevenueCat log-out/reset identity flow, not only the local `resetPurchases()` flag.
- Add real-device tests for guest purchase, guest-to-sign-in restore, signed-in purchase, sign-out/sign-in, and cross-device restore.

### 57. Legal WebViews Are Not Sandboxed For Static Legal Content

Impact: Terms/privacy screens are part of App Review and purchase trust. They render static in-app legal HTML, but the WebView defaults allow JavaScript and broad HTTP/HTTPS navigation. If legal HTML links are tapped, the user can navigate away inside a screen still titled "Privacy Policy" or "Terms of Use" without browser controls, and static legal pages have more WebView capability than they need.

Evidence:
- `WebViewScreen` accepts either `html` or `url` from route params and passes the computed source directly to `WebView`: `screens/WebViewScreen.js:10`, `screens/WebViewScreen.js:12`, and `screens/WebViewScreen.js:35`.
- Auth legal modal also renders legal HTML directly in a WebView: `screens/AuthScreen.js:277`.
- Paywall and Profile open Terms/Privacy through `WebViewScreen`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:430`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:440`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:280`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:300`.
- No legal WebView sets `javaScriptEnabled={false}`, `originWhitelist`, `onShouldStartLoadWithRequest`, `onError`, or `startInLoadingState`.
- Current `react-native-webview` defaults enable JavaScript and whitelist `http://*` and `https://*`: `node_modules/react-native-webview/src/WebView.ios.tsx:54`, `node_modules/react-native-webview/src/WebView.android.tsx:67`, and `node_modules/react-native-webview/lib/WebViewShared.js:1`.

Fix:
- For bundled legal HTML, set `javaScriptEnabled={false}` and a restrictive `originWhitelist`.
- Intercept external links and open them in the system browser with visible URL context.
- Add WebView loading/error UI and accessibility labels for legal screens.
- Avoid accepting arbitrary `url` route params unless there is an allowlist and a product need.

### 58. Manage Subscription Opens External Store Links Without Failure Handling

Impact: A paid user tapping "Manage subscription" can hit a dead end if the subscription settings URL cannot open, is blocked, or the platform handler fails. There is no visible error, fallback instructions, or support CTA, which is risky for refund pressure and App Review subscription-management expectations.

Evidence:
- Profile selects the subscription-management URL by platform: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:228`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:229`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:230`.
- It calls `Linking.openURL(url)` without `await`, `canOpenURL`, `try/catch`, or an alert fallback: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:232`.
- The support page tells users to manage/cancel through system subscription settings, so this path is part of the user-facing subscription support journey: `docs/support.html:134`.

Fix:
- Wrap the call in `canOpenURL`/`openURL` with `await` and error handling.
- If opening fails, show manual iOS/Android instructions and a support email link.
- Add real-device QA for manage subscription from Profile on iOS and Android.

## Sixteenth-Pass Supabase Function Boundary Findings
