### 59. Internal Rate-Limit And Cleanup RPCs Are SECURITY DEFINER Without Explicit Public Revokes

Impact: Abuse-control helpers should not be callable as product APIs. Several functions mutate rate-limit/cache tables under `SECURITY DEFINER`, but the migrations do not explicitly revoke public execute permissions from them. In Postgres/Supabase, newly created functions should be treated as callable by `PUBLIC` unless the migration revokes them. That means anonymous/authenticated clients may be able to burn another user's rate-limit counter, manipulate IP counters, or trigger cleanup routines through PostgREST RPC.

Evidence:
- `check_rate_limit(p_user_id, ...)` is `SECURITY DEFINER` and inserts/updates `rate_limits`: `supabase/migrations/002_rate_limits.sql:13`.
- `check_ip_rate_limit(p_ip_address, ...)` is `SECURITY DEFINER` and inserts/updates `ip_rate_limits`: `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:17`.
- `cleanup_stale_rate_limits()` and `cleanup_stale_ip_rate_limits()` are `SECURITY DEFINER` delete helpers: `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:34` and `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:67`.
- `cleanup_expired_cache()` is a `SECURITY DEFINER` delete helper for `analysis_cache`: `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:13`.
- Repository search found an explicit `REVOKE` only for `delete_own_account`; the rate-limit and cleanup functions do not have matching `REVOKE ALL ON FUNCTION ... FROM PUBLIC/anon/authenticated` statements.

Fix:
- Add migrations that `REVOKE ALL ON FUNCTION ... FROM PUBLIC, anon, authenticated` for internal helpers.
- Grant execute only to `service_role` where Edge Functions or scheduled jobs need them.
- For user-scoped rate-limit helpers, validate `auth.uid()` or require service-role execution only.
- Add a Supabase permission audit script that fails CI when a mutating `SECURITY DEFINER` function is publicly executable.

### 60. Authenticated Users Can Write Long-Lived Nutrient Claims Into Product Data

Impact: A signed-in user can potentially poison public product data with fake nutrient panels or "published nutrients" claims that last for 365 days. That directly affects trust in nutrition scoring, search results, and marketing claims about better analysis quality.

Evidence:
- `save_product_data_with_nutrients(...)` inserts or updates `product_data` with `nutrient_panel` and `has_published_nutrients`: `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:48`.
- It runs as `SECURITY DEFINER`, so it bypasses table RLS: `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:58`.
- It sets `expires_at = NOW() + INTERVAL '365 days'`: `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:74` and `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:99`.
- It is granted to `service_role, authenticated`: `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:109`.
- The function accepts caller-provided `p_source`, `p_image_url`, and `p_nutrient_panel` without source allowlisting, provenance validation, ingredient-count threshold enforcement, or ownership checks.

Fix:
- Revoke the function from `authenticated`; keep it service-role only.
- Route nutrient writes through a server-side validation job with source allowlists and provenance requirements.
- Add constraints or validation for `source`, nutrient schema, ingredient minimums, and trusted source URLs.
- Mark user-submitted nutrient data as unverified and exclude it from scoring until reviewed.

### 61. Public Search RPC Has No Upper Bound On Requested Result Count

Impact: The app UI asks for 10 results, but the public RPC lets any anon caller choose `max_results`. During marketing traffic or scraping, a caller can request very large result sets from a trigram search function, increasing database load and making the product catalog easier to scrape in bulk.

Evidence:
- `search_products(q, max_results INT DEFAULT 10)` exposes caller-controlled `max_results`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:28`.
- The function only rejects queries shorter than two characters; it does not clamp `max_results`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:41`.
- The query runs trigram similarity and substring checks against `product_name` and `brand`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:56`.
- The final `LIMIT` uses the caller-provided `max_results`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:73`.
- Execute is granted to `anon` and `authenticated`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:76` and `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:77`.
- The app itself only requests 10 results from Home search: `screens/HomeScreen.js:306`.

Fix:
- Clamp `max_results` inside the function, for example `LEAST(GREATEST(max_results, 1), 20)`.
- Add query normalization and rate limiting for public search RPC calls.
- Consider a separate public search edge function if telemetry/rate control is needed before marketing.
- Add load tests for common two-character and high-cardinality search terms.

## Seventeenth-Pass Scan Cancellation And Retry Findings

### 62. Scanner Cancel Button Does Not Cancel The Capture Pipeline

Impact: During a slow capture/compression moment in a store, the user can tap Cancel but still get pushed into Results when the original async capture pipeline finishes. That makes the app feel unresponsive and can start analysis work the user explicitly tried to stop.

Evidence:
- The processing card renders a Cancel button wired to `onCancel`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:48` and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:57`.
- `handleCancelCapture` only calls `setCapturing(false)`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:261`.
- `handleCapture` does not check a cancellation ref after `takePictureAsync` or `ImageManipulator.manipulateAsync`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:228` and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:241`.
- After compression, it unconditionally calls `navigation.push("Results", ...)`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246`.
- The `finally` block also sets `capturing` false, but it does not prevent navigation or discard the completed capture: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:255`.

Fix:
- Add a capture session id/cancelled ref and check it after each async step before navigating.
- Disable or hide Cancel if the current native operation cannot be interrupted, or label it as "Stop after capture" only if that is true.
- If possible, use abortable image processing or ignore late completion from canceled sessions.
- Add a manual QA case: tap capture, immediately tap Cancel, verify no Results screen opens and no analysis starts.

### 63. Leaving Or Retrying Results Does Not Abort Running Analysis

Impact: If a scan is slow and the user backs out or retries, the original network/AI work can keep running in the background. That wastes paid vendor calls, can keep old analyses around for up to two minutes, and can make retries launch duplicate work instead of canceling the stale attempt.

Evidence:
- The analysis service explicitly says analyses survive component unmount and keep going with zero subscribers: `services/analysisService.js:17`, `services/analysisService.js:19`, and `services/analysisService.js:21`.
- `startAnalysis` creates an `AbortController` and stores it in state: `services/analysisService.js:195` and `services/analysisService.js:206`.
- The only code path found that aborts the controller is the 120-second hard timeout: `services/analysisService.js:98` and `services/analysisService.js:108`.
- Results unsubscribe cleanup removes listeners/timers but does not abort the service entry: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:421`.
- Loading and error back buttons call `handleBack`, which only `navigation.popToTop()`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:587`.
- Retry replaces the screen with the same inputs but does not cancel the old service entry first: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:568`.
- Photo/search analyses use generated temp ids, so the reuse guard only applies when a concrete `cacheKey` exists: `services/analysisService.js:183` and `services/analysisService.js:187`.

Fix:
- Add `cancelAnalysis(key, reason)` to the analysis service and call it from Results back, scan-another, retry, and unmount where the user has abandoned the analysis.
- For retry, cancel the current entry before creating a new one.
- Keep background continuation only for explicit workflows that need it, such as navigating from Results to ingredient capture.
- Track cancellation telemetry separately from timeout/error telemetry.

### 64. "Use AI Estimate" Pays An OCR Round Trip Before Falling Back

Impact: When the app identifies a product but has no verified data, the user can choose "Use AI estimate instead" for speed. That path still enters `photo_with_ingredients` without an ingredient photo, calls the OCR endpoint with no ingredient image, waits for failure, and only then falls back to photo-only analysis. This makes the explicitly faster path slower and spends an avoidable edge-function request.

Evidence:
- The "Use AI estimate instead" CTA calls `handleUseEstimate`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:554`.
- It navigates to `mode: "photo_with_ingredients"` with `base64`, `productName`, and `brand`, but no `ingredientBase64`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:558`.
- `_runPhotoWithIngredients` always starts by notifying "Reading ingredient label..." and calling `ocrIngredients(ingredientBase64, productName, ...)`: `services/analysisService.js:503` and `services/analysisService.js:506`.
- `ocrIngredients` posts `mode: "ocr_ingredients"` and `imageBase64: base64Image` to the analyze function, with a 20-second timeout: `services/claude.js:723`, `services/claude.js:729`, and `services/claude.js:736`.
- Only after OCR fails does the service fall back to `analyzeIngredients(base64, ...)`: `services/analysisService.js:510` and `services/analysisService.js:515`.

Fix:
- Split the estimate path into a distinct mode, for example `photo_estimate`, that skips OCR entirely.
- Or, in `_runPhotoWithIngredients`, branch immediately when `ingredientBase64` is missing and go straight to photo-only analysis.
- Change loading copy for the estimate path so it does not say "Reading ingredient label..." when no label image exists.
- Add an acceptance test that verifies the estimate CTA makes exactly one analysis request and no OCR request.

## Eighteenth-Pass Client Funnel And State Findings

### 65. Large Scan Images Are Passed Through Navigation Params

Impact: The scan flow serializes large base64 JPEGs into React Navigation route params. That can increase memory pressure, slow screen transitions, make retry/back stacks heavy, and become worse in the ingredient-label flow where both the front photo and label photo are carried together.

Evidence:
- Scanner captures a photo, resizes it to width 1600, and asks `ImageManipulator` to return `base64: true`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:241` and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:244`.
- Scanner then pushes Results with `base64: resized.base64`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246` and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:248`.
- Results destructures `base64` from route params and passes it into `analysisService.startAnalysis`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:179` and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:358`.
- When the app asks for an ingredient label, Results replaces the screen with `IngredientCapture` while carrying the original front-photo `base64`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:541` and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:547`.
- IngredientCapture captures a second 1800px image with `base64: true` and replaces Results with both `base64` and `ingredientBase64`: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:39`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:42`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:44`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:46`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:47`.
- Retry repeats the same route-param payload: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:579` and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:580`.

Fix:
- Store captured images in a short-lived analysis service entry or temp file and pass only an opaque analysis id / file URI through navigation.
- Add client-side image byte-size validation before analysis starts.
- Avoid keeping both front and label base64 strings in route params at the same time.
- Add memory/transition-time QA on low-RAM Android devices.

### 66. Search Passes The Selected Cache Key But Analysis Ignores It

Impact: The search UI now passes the selected row's `cacheKey`, but the search analysis path still recomputes lookup from product name and brand. That means the intended exact-row handoff is not actually wired, so search can still lose the user's selected row and fall back to broader matching or "not found" behavior. It also wastes the pre-warm path: Home warms analysis rows by selected `cache_key`, then Results asks the service to analyze a different normalized key.

Evidence:
- Home search tap computes a row-specific `cacheKey`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:379`.
- It navigates to Results with that `cacheKey`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:389` and `screens/HomeScreen.js:393`.
- Results destructures `cacheKey` from route params: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:179`.
- In `mode === "search"`, Results calls `analysisService.startAnalysis` with `mode`, `productName`, `brand`, `petType`, and `isPro`, but not `cacheKey`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:331` and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:336`.
- `startAnalysis` accepts no selected cache key parameter for search; it initializes `cacheKey` only from barcode: `services/analysisService.js:161` and `services/analysisService.js:183`.
- `_runSearch` recomputes `realCacheKey = normalizeCacheKey(productName)` and calls `getProductData(productName, brand)` instead of exact lookup by the selected row key: `services/analysisService.js:322` and `services/analysisService.js:329`.
- Home pre-warms cached analyses using the selected row keys: `screens/HomeScreen.js:315`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:318`, `services/cache.js:300`, `services/cache.js:312`, and `services/cache.js:315`.
- `_runSearch` then checks cached analysis under `dbResult.productCacheKey || realCacheKey`, not the route `cacheKey` that Home warmed: `services/analysisService.js:338`, `services/analysisService.js:341`, `services/analysisService.js:342`, and `services/analysisService.js:343`.
- Search history is saved under the recomputed `realCacheKey`, not necessarily the selected row key, so later history/recent replay can drift from the exact product the user tapped: `services/analysisService.js:354`, `services/analysisService.js:371`, and `services/analysisService.js:415`.

Fix:
- Add a `selectedCacheKey` argument to `startAnalysis` and `_runSearch`.
- Make `getProductData` support an exact trusted cache-key lookup for selected search rows.
- Use the selected row's `cache_key` as the shared analysis/cache key.
- Pre-warm, analysis lookup, cache writes, and history writes should all use the same canonical selected key for the tapped row.
- Add a regression test where a visible search row with a non-normalized cache key opens the exact row, not a recomputed name match.

### 67. Clear History Can Show Success Before Supabase Deletion Succeeds

Impact: A signed-in user can tap "Clear all scan history" and see the local list cleared while remote Supabase history deletion is still fire-and-forget. If that remote delete fails, history can reappear on the next load/device, which is a trust and privacy problem.

Evidence:
- `clearHistory()` removes the local AsyncStorage key and invalidates memory cache immediately: `services/history.js:210`, `services/history.js:212`, and `services/history.js:213`.
- For signed-in users, Supabase deletion is launched without `await`: `services/history.js:216`, `services/history.js:217`, and `services/history.js:218`.
- Remote delete errors are only logged inside `.then(...)`: `services/history.js:221` and `services/history.js:222`.
- Home's clear-history handler calls `clearHistory().then(() => setHistory([]))`, so the UI clears when the local portion resolves, not when remote deletion is confirmed: `screens/HomeScreen.js:504`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:515`.
- `getHistory()` prefers Supabase when a user is signed in, so failed remote deletion can repopulate rows later: `services/history.js:132` and `services/history.js:134`.

Fix:
- Await Supabase deletion for signed-in users and return a success/error result to the UI.
- If remote deletion fails, keep a visible error state and do not imply history is fully cleared.
- Add a pending tombstone or retry queue if offline clearing is allowed.
- Add a QA case that simulates Supabase delete failure and confirms history does not silently reappear.

## Nineteenth-Pass Edge Runtime And Response-Contract Findings

### 68. Streaming Results Can Diverge From Cached And Non-Streaming Results

Impact: First-time scan users can see a live streamed analysis that has not gone through the same server-side normalization and brand/recall override path used for cache writes and non-streaming responses. A later cache hit or non-stream fallback can therefore show a different score, recall state, or trust metadata for the same product, which is especially damaging for safety claims and launch credibility.

Evidence:
- The streaming branch tees the Claude response, sends `clientStream` directly to the app, and only normalizes the separate cache branch: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1568`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1570`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1592`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1595`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1600`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1616`.
- The non-streaming branch parses, runs `normalizeAnalysis(...)`, applies the brand profile, and rewrites `data.content[0].text` before returning to the client: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1634`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1637`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1642`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1645`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1646`.
- The mobile client consumes the raw streamed SSE text, parses it locally, calls `onUpdate(final)`, and returns that object: `services/claude.js:344`, `services/claude.js:347`, `services/claude.js:416`, `services/claude.js:436`, and `services/claude.js:439`.
- The verified-data path prefers streaming when `onUpdate && canStream`, then returns the streamed result with only ingredient augmentation: `services/claude.js:551`, `services/claude.js:555`, `services/claude.js:561`.
- `ResultsScreen` shows service update and complete events directly in state: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:392`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:393`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:395`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:396`.

Fix:
- Make the exact same normalized/brand-profile object drive both the client final state and the cache write.
- Either transform the server stream before sending it, send a final normalized correction event after the stream, or disable streaming for modes whose safety/recall fields require server post-processing.
- Add a regression test where a product with a brand profile/recall override produces identical fields across streaming, non-streaming, and cache-hit paths.

### 69. Product Lookup Rate Limiting Fails Open On Missing IP Or RPC Error

Impact: Anonymous `product-lookup` traffic can bypass the intended ScrapingBee credit protection if the edge runtime/request path does not provide a recognizable client IP or if the rate-limit RPC errors. During marketing traffic or abuse, that means vendor spend and cache writes can continue exactly when the guardrail is unavailable.

Evidence:
- Anonymous requests are supposed to be rate limited before request parsing: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1078`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1080`.
- The IP is set to `"unknown"` when forwarded IP headers are absent: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1081`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1085`.
- The rate-limit RPC only runs when `clientIp !== "unknown"`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1087`.
- If `check_ip_rate_limit` returns an error, the function logs it and continues instead of denying the request or falling back to an authenticated/quota gate: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1093`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1094`.
- The only blocking path is `allowed === false`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1095`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1097`.

Fix:
- Fail closed for anonymous lookup when the client IP cannot be established or the rate-limit RPC errors.
- Prefer requiring an authenticated session/quota for ScrapingBee-backed lookups; reserve anonymous lookup for cache-only reads.
- Add telemetry for rate-limit-denied, missing-IP-denied, and rate-limit-RPC-error-denied cases.

### 70. Human-Food Safety Answers Are Stored In The Shared Analysis Cache

Impact: Human-food checks can include sensitive household/pet safety questions. The edge function writes valid human-food analyses into the same shared `analysis_cache` table that authenticated clients can read by cache key. Even if the current UI does not prewarm human-food cache hits, an authenticated client can query the table directly through the Supabase API when it can guess or enumerate normalized food/pet keys. That is a privacy and data-minimization issue for a feature users may treat as personal advice.

Evidence:
- `analysis_cache` is explicitly described as shared across all users and stores the full `analysis` JSON: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:1`, `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:2`, and `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:5`.
- Authenticated users have a SELECT policy with `USING (true)`: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:24`, `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:25`, `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:27`, and `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:28`.
- `writeToCache(...)` derives a human-food cache key from `foodName` and `petType`, sets `lookupType` to `"human_food"`, and upserts the analysis into `analysis_cache`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:913`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:914`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:916`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:923`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:928`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:934`.
- Both streaming and non-streaming human-food success paths call `writeToCache(...)` after `isValidHumanFoodAnalysis(...)` passes: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1602`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1606`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1649`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1654`.
- Client cache reads are direct Supabase table reads from `analysis_cache`: `services/cache.js:370`, `services/cache.js:371`, `services/cache.js:372`, and `services/cache.js:373`.

Fix:
- Do not write `human_food` results to the shared cache unless there is an explicit privacy design and disclosure.
- If caching is needed, store human-food cache rows in a user-scoped table with `user_id` RLS or in device-local storage only.
- Add a migration that deletes existing `lookup_type = 'human_food'` shared cache rows or quarantines them behind service-role-only access.

### 71. Main Analyze Anonymous Rate Limiting Also Fails Open

Impact: The main paid AI endpoint can run unmetered anonymous scan and human-food work if forwarded IP headers are missing or the IP rate-limit RPC fails. This undermines the abuse controls protecting Anthropic/OpenAI spend and makes the app less predictable under store/network/proxy conditions.

Evidence:
- Anonymous rate limiting is intended for non-helper modes: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1034`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1035`.
- The IP defaults to `"unknown"` and the check only runs when it is not unknown: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1036`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1040`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1042`.
- If `check_ip_rate_limit` errors, the function logs and continues; only `allowed === false` blocks: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1048`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1049`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1050`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1052`.
- The stricter anonymous human-food daily cap has the same missing-IP bypass and does not inspect the RPC error at all: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1107`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1112`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1113`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1114`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1119`.

Fix:
- Fail closed or require sign-in when anonymous IP identity cannot be established.
- Treat rate-limit RPC errors as deny-by-default for anonymous paid AI work.
- Log separate metrics for missing IP, RPC error, and allowed/denied states so production traffic can be audited.

## Twentieth-Pass Auth Conversion Finding

### 72. Google Sign-In Can Fail Silently

Impact: If Google/Supabase OAuth returns a redirect without both `access_token` and `refresh_token`, or if the browser session is dismissed/cancelled, `signInWithGoogle()` resolves without throwing. `AuthScreen` then clears the loading state and shows no error, leaving the user on the auth screen with no explanation. This is a conversion risk before marketing because OAuth configuration mistakes, denied consent, and redirect errors look like dead taps.

Evidence:
- `AuthScreen` only alerts when `signInWithGoogle()` throws: `screens/AuthScreen.js:97`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:101`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:102`, and `screens/AuthScreen.js:103`.
- `signInWithGoogle()` opens the auth session, but only handles `result.type === "success"`: `services/auth.js:393`, `services/auth.js:398`.
- On success, it parses only the URL fragment for `access_token` and `refresh_token`: `services/auth.js:399`, `services/auth.js:400`, `services/auth.js:402`, and `services/auth.js:403`.
- It calls `setSession(...)` only if both tokens exist, and otherwise falls through without throwing: `services/auth.js:405`, `services/auth.js:406`, `services/auth.js:409`, and `services/auth.js:411`.
- There is no handling for OAuth error fragments/query params or non-success browser results: `services/auth.js:398` through `services/auth.js:411`.

Fix:
- Throw a user-readable error when the browser result is cancelled/dismissed, when OAuth returns `error`/`error_description`, or when tokens are missing.
- Log structured auth failure reasons without leaking token values.
- Add simulator/device QA for Google success, cancel, denied consent, and bad redirect URI.

## Twenty-First-Pass Release Provenance Finding

### 73. App Version Sources Are Out Of Sync

Impact: The app footer, Expo runtime/versioning, package metadata, and support/debug conversations can disagree about what build a user is running. That makes App Store review, crash triage, customer support, and OTA rollback decisions harder during a marketing launch, especially when users report "Woof v1.1.1" while npm/package metadata still says `1.0.0`.

Evidence:
- `app.json` declares Expo app version `1.1.1`: `app.json:6`.
- `package.json` still declares package version `1.0.0`: `package.json:3`.
- Profile reads the displayed app version from `Constants.expoConfig?.version`, falling back to `1.0.0`: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:121`.
- The Profile footer renders `Woof v{appVersion}` to users: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:543`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:545`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:546`.
- EAS is configured with remote app versioning and production `autoIncrement`, so release provenance already depends on disciplined version tracking: `eas.json:4`, `eas.json:24`, and `eas.json:26`.
- `npx expo config --type public --json` currently resolves the public Expo version to `1.1.1`, confirming the user-visible app config and package metadata are already divergent.

Fix:
- Pick a single source of truth for marketing/support version labels and release notes.
- Keep `package.json`, Expo `version`, EAS remote version/build numbers, and store release notes in the same release checklist.
- Add a pre-release script that prints and validates all version/build identifiers before `eas build` or `eas submit`.

## Twenty-Second-Pass Search Persistence Finding

### 74. Recent Searches Can Reopen Stale Or No-Longer-Valid Product Rows

Impact: Even if live search is fixed, a user can tap a locally persisted recent-search row that no longer exists, has expired, or no longer satisfies the analysis contract. That can recreate the "product is not in the database anymore" experience from an entry the app itself still displays under Recent.

Evidence:
- Recent searches are hydrated directly from AsyncStorage with no TTL, schema check, or database revalidation: `screens/HomeScreen.js:334`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:336`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:338`.
- The persisted recent object stores only `product_name`, `brand`, `cache_key`, and `image_url`; it does not store `ingredient_count`, `expires_at`, or a validated analysis-ready flag: `screens/HomeScreen.js:342`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:345`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:348`.
- Recent rows call the same `handleSearchResultPress(item)` as live search results: `screens/HomeScreen.js:743`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:746`.
- The press handler immediately navigates to Results using the stale local values and does not re-query `product_data` before navigation: `screens/HomeScreen.js:374`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:379`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:389`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:393`.
- The downstream analysis path then requires current valid product data through `getProductData(...)`: `services/analysisService.js:328`, `services/cache.js:159`, `services/cache.js:164`, `services/cache.js:186`, and `services/cache.js:187`.

Fix:
- Revalidate recent-search rows by exact `cache_key` before navigating, or remove invalid recents from AsyncStorage when tapped.
- Store a short TTL for recents and clear stale rows on app launch.
- If revalidation fails, keep the user on Home with a clear "This product needs a new scan" action instead of opening Results into an error.

## Twenty-Third-Pass History Replay Finding

### 75. Human-Food History Sync Loses Safety Data And Uses An Unreplayable Cache Key

Impact: A signed-in user can complete a human-food safety check, see it in local history, then fail to replay it from another device or after local cache loss. The Supabase history row does not preserve `safetyLevel`, and its `cache_key` is a random temp id, while the server stores the actual human-food analysis cache under normalized `foodName + petType`. That makes cross-device history unreliable for a feature users may revisit for safety advice.

Evidence:
- Human-food analysis saves the local result under `tempId` and saves history with the same `tempId`: `services/analysisService.js:452`, `services/analysisService.js:478`, and `services/analysisService.js:480`.
- `_saveHistory(...)` includes `safetyLevel` only in the in-memory/local entry object: `services/analysisService.js:842`, `services/analysisService.js:844`, and `services/analysisService.js:854`.
- The Supabase `scan_history` schema has columns for `overall_score`, `pet_type`, `cache_key`, `scan_mode`, and `data_source`, but no human-food `safety_level` or serialized analysis payload: `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:42`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:46`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:47`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:49`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:50`, and `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:51`.
- `toSupabaseRow(...)` drops `safetyLevel`, and `fromSupabaseRow(...)` cannot restore it: `services/history.js:54`, `services/history.js:62`, `services/history.js:70`, and `services/history.js:77`.
- History replay loads by the history row's `cacheKey`, first from local result cache and then from shared `analysis_cache`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:293`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:298`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:309`.
- The edge function writes human-food cache rows under `normalizeHumanFoodCacheKey(foodName, petType)`, not the client's random `tempId`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:913`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:914`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:916`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:932`.
- If both lookups miss, Results shows "This result is no longer available": `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:319`.

Fix:
- Use the same deterministic human-food cache key on the client and server if replay is intended.
- Or store enough user-scoped history payload to render human-food history without a shared cache lookup.
- Add `safety_level` and any needed human-food detail columns to `scan_history`, or keep human-food history local-only with explicit copy.
- Add a cross-device signed-in QA case for text and photo human-food checks.

## Twenty-Fourth-Pass Safety Copy Finding

### 76. Veterinary Disclaimer Is Not Consistently Visible At Decision Time

Impact: The Terms and Privacy pages contain AI/veterinary disclaimers, but the product surfaces that users actually rely on for feeding decisions use strong labels like "Safe", "Toxic for dogs", "Safe in moderation", and "Human food safety checker" before showing any caveat. For pet-food results, the in-result disclaimer is rendered only for Pro users. This creates legal, App Review, and trust risk when marketing drives new users straight into safety-sensitive claims.

Evidence:
- Legal copy does include the right caveats: AI can be wrong and results are not veterinary advice: `legal.js:54`, `legal.js:55`, `legal.js:90`, `legal.js:91`, `legal.js:93`, `legal.js:94`, `legal.js:96`, and `legal.js:97`.
- Home's human-food entry point says "Is This Safe for My Pet?" and "Check any human food item" without nearby veterinary/emergency caveat: `screens/HomeScreen.js:783`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:799`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:802`.
- The human-food modal says "Can my pet eat that?" and asks the user to type or photograph food, again without visible "not veterinary advice" or poison-control/emergency guidance before submission: `screens/HomeScreen.js:922`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:924`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:926`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:927`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:981`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:993`.
- Onboarding says Woof "tells you what's actually safe to share from your plate" and shows "Toxic for dogs" / "Safe in moderation" examples without the legal caveat: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:67`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:68`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:279`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:282`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:315`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:317`.
- Paywall markets "Human food safety checker" as a Pro feature: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:40`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:42`.
- Human-food results use a large `SafetyBadge` label of "Safe", "Caution", or "Dangerous": `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2864`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2868`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2869`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2870`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2883`.
- The generic in-result disclaimer exists only as small footer text: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2892` and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2895`.
- Human-food results render the disclaimer after the result is done, but pet-food results render it only when `done && isPro`, so free scan users can miss it: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:903`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:904`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:907`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1146`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1147`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1150`.

Fix:
- Add short, visible safety copy at human-food entry and submit points: "AI estimate, not veterinary advice; contact a vet/poison control for ingestion concerns."
- Show the result disclaimer for all pet-food and human-food users, not only Pro users.
- Rename absolute labels where possible: "Likely safe in moderation" / "Potentially dangerous" / "Verify with your vet" instead of unconditional "Safe".
- Add QA that verifies disclaimer visibility on onboarding, home human-food modal, free pet-food result, Pro pet-food result, and human-food result.

## Twenty-Fifth-Pass Startup Resilience Finding

### 77. Initial Auth Session Failure Can Leave A Permanent Blank Screen

Impact: If the initial Supabase session read rejects during cold start, the app can stay on a blank screen indefinitely. This is high-risk for marketing because a transient storage/auth SDK failure, corrupted session, or platform-specific Supabase error can block users before Home, scan, search, paywall, or support are reachable.

Evidence:
- `AuthProvider` initializes `loading` to `true`: `services/auth.js:33`.
- The initial startup effect calls `supabase.auth.getSession().then(...)` but has no `.catch(...)` or `.finally(...)`: `services/auth.js:263`, `services/auth.js:264`, and `services/auth.js:298`.
- `setLoading(false)` is only called inside the `.then(...)` success path: `services/auth.js:297`.
- `AppNavigator` renders a plain blank view while `loading` is true: `App.js:96`, `App.js:98`, `App.js:99`, and `App.js:100`.
- The app shell places `AppNavigator` under `AuthProvider`, so this loading state gates the main app: `App.js:216`, `App.js:217`, and `App.js:218`.
- The root `ErrorBoundary` catches render errors, but not rejected promises from this async startup path: `App.js:22`, `App.js:25`, `App.js:29`, and `App.js:213`.

Fix:
- Wrap initial `getSession()` in `try/catch/finally` and always clear loading after a bounded timeout.
- On auth-init failure, fall back to guest mode with a visible non-blocking warning and a sign-in retry path.
- Add a startup test/mocked Supabase failure that proves the app reaches Home instead of a blank screen.

### 78. Results Auth Error Recovery Does Not Actually Reopen Sign-In

Impact: If a scan/result request fails because the user's session expired, the UI can show a "Sign In Again" CTA, but tapping it only calls `supabase.auth.signOut()`. It does not navigate to the Auth screen, does not retry the original action after sign-in, and does not give the user a clear next step. This can turn recoverable auth/token failures into abandoned scans.

Evidence:
- `classifyError(...)` marks auth failures with `action: "sign_in"`: `services/errors.js:127`, `services/errors.js:130`, `services/errors.js:131`, and `services/errors.js:133`.
- `ErrorState` changes the CTA label to "Sign In Again" for auth/sign-in errors: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2770` and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2771`.
- The button action only calls `supabase.auth.signOut().catch(...)`; it does not call navigation, does not emit an auth modal event, and does not retry after reauth: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2772`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2773`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2774`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2775`.
- `ErrorState` receives only `error`, `mode`, `onRetry`, and `onScanAnother`, so it has no direct way to open the Auth screen: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2757`.
- Results renders `ErrorState` with retry/home handlers but no auth handler: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:737`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:740`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:741`.

Fix:
- Pass an `onSignInAgain` handler from Results that navigates to Auth and resumes/retries the scan after successful sign-in.
- Or make auth errors route to Home/Profile with a clear sign-in prompt and preserve the pending scan payload.
- Add a test that forces a 401/expired JWT during analysis and verifies the CTA opens sign-in rather than silently signing out.

## Twenty-Sixth-Pass Data Provenance Finding

### 79. Scraped And User-OCR Catalog Rows Are Promoted As "Verified" Ingredients

Impact: Search and photo flows treat any `product_data` hit with enough ingredients as verified input, even when the row came from Amazon scraping or user OCR. This can make low-provenance, stale, or user-contributed rows look as trustworthy as OPFF/brand/manufacturer data, and then cache the resulting score for future users.

Evidence:
- `getProductData(...)` returns `source` and `sourceUrl`, but does not classify whether the source is authoritative before handing the row to analysis: `services/cache.js:91`, `services/cache.js:100`, `services/cache.js:112`, and `services/cache.js:113`.
- User OCR writes product rows with default source `user_ocr`: `services/cache.js:270`, `services/cache.js:275`, `services/cache.js:281`, and `services/cache.js:282`.
- Search mode calls the DB lookup under the comment "verified ingredients" and accepts any found row with at least 5 ingredients: `services/analysisService.js:328`, `services/analysisService.js:329`, and `services/analysisService.js:332`.
- Search cached/local hits force `ingredientSource = "verified"` regardless of `dbResult.source`: `services/analysisService.js:346`, `services/analysisService.js:347`, `services/analysisService.js:364`, and `services/analysisService.js:365`.
- Search first-analysis path tells the UI it is "Analyzing ... verified ingredients" and sets final `ingredientSource` to `"verified"`: `services/analysisService.js:378`, `services/analysisService.js:379`, `services/analysisService.js:404`, and `services/analysisService.js:405`.
- Photo DB hits have the same behavior: `services/analysisService.js:649`, `services/analysisService.js:650`, `services/analysisService.js:661`, `services/analysisService.js:662`, `services/analysisService.js:679`, `services/analysisService.js:680`, `services/analysisService.js:693`, `services/analysisService.js:694`, `services/analysisService.js:717`, and `services/analysisService.js:718`.
- Home search UI only shows a "verified" pill for `opff`, `verified`, or `web_verified`, so the UI already knows not every source is equal, but the analysis path collapses them anyway: `screens/HomeScreen.js:708`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:709`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:710`.

Live data:
- Exact live counts from Supabase on June 6, 2026: `amazon`: 8,176 rows; `user_ocr`: 47; `dfa`: 1,053; `web_verified`: 940; `opff`: 477; `brand`: 182; `manufacturer`: 10.
- 10,985 of 10,990 `product_data` rows have no `source_url`, so most rows cannot show a traceable source URL.

Fix:
- Split source trust levels into `authoritative`, `scraped`, `user_ocr`, and `unknown`, and carry that through Results, history, and cache.
- Only use "verified" copy for OPFF/brand/manufacturer rows with provenance strong enough for the claim.
- Show user-OCR and scraped rows as "label-derived" or "community/scraped estimate" and avoid caching them as authoritative for all users until reviewed.
- Add source allowlists and validation jobs before rows enter search or shared analysis cache.

## Twenty-Seventh-Pass Rate-Limit Finding

### 80. Helper OCR Calls Burn The Same Authenticated Hourly Limit As Completed Scans

Impact: A signed-in user can hit the 20/hour authenticated rate limit after a handful of difficult scans because the edge function rate-limits every authenticated request before it knows whether the request is a top-level scan or an internal helper call. In the in-store path, one product can require identify, OCR, and final analysis calls before the user sees a useful answer. That makes rate-limit errors possible for legitimate shoppers even when their free/Pro scan quota should still allow the workflow.

Evidence:
- The `analyze` edge function runs `check_rate_limit` for any authenticated request before parsing the body or reading `mode`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:991`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:993`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1000`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1002`.
- The request body and `mode` are parsed only after that rate-limit check: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1011`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1013`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1018`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1027`.
- Helper modes are exempted from scan/quota enforcement later, but not from the earlier authenticated rate bucket: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1060`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1063`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1064`.
- The normal photo path starts with an `identifyProduct(...)` helper call before checking the product database: `services/analysisService.js:579`, `services/analysisService.js:583`, `services/claude.js:683`, and `services/claude.js:687`.
- If the user has to photograph the ingredient label, the app makes an `ocr_ingredients` helper request before final scoring: `services/analysisService.js:503`, `services/analysisService.js:506`, `services/claude.js:736`, and `services/claude.js:740`.
- The final scoring call then uses `verified` or `photo` mode and consumes the same authenticated rate bucket again: `services/analysisService.js:543`, `services/analysisService.js:714`, `services/claude.js:555`, and `services/claude.js:556`.

Fix:
- Parse and validate `mode` before applying authenticated rate limits.
- Use separate buckets for top-level user-visible analyses, helper OCR/identify calls, and abuse-prone anonymous helper traffic.
- Count one logical scan attempt per user workflow, not every internal sub-call.
- Add a load/flow test that performs repeated hard scans with identify + ingredient-label OCR and proves a legitimate signed-in user does not hit the hourly limiter prematurely.

## Twenty-Eighth-Pass Cache Integrity Finding

### 81. Public Verified Analysis Mode Can Poison Shared Cache Rows

Impact: The `analyze` edge function accepts caller-supplied `opffProduct` data in `verified` mode, scores it as verified product data, and can upsert the result into the shared `analysis_cache` using a caller-provided `cacheKey`. A malicious or buggy client can therefore seed a 30-day "verified" analysis for a real product key, and later users can receive that cached score instantly through search/photo flows without the app re-checking provenance.

Evidence:
- Auth is optional for the `analyze` edge function; missing auth leaves `user` as `null` and the request can continue: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:963`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:970`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:972`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:987`.
- `verified` mode is accepted as a public request mode: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1018`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1027`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1164`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1167`.
- The verified prompt is built from request-provided `opffProduct` and tells the model it is verified OPFF data: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1174`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1175`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1201`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1204`.
- The cache writer uses the caller-provided `cacheKey` for non-human-food modes and labels `verified` mode cache rows as `data_source = "verified"`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:904`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:908`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:919`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:923`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:924`.
- The edge function writes through the service-role client and upserts into `analysis_cache`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:965`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:966`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:968`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:928`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:932`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:941`.
- Search reads the shared cache key before scoring and treats a hit as verified ingredients: `services/analysisService.js:338`, `services/analysisService.js:341`, `services/analysisService.js:345`, `services/analysisService.js:346`, and `services/analysisService.js:347`.
- The cache read returns `analysis`, `data_source`, and `opff_data` for any unexpired matching key: `services/cache.js:370`, `services/cache.js:372`, `services/cache.js:373`, `services/cache.js:374`, `services/cache.js:400`, and `services/cache.js:403`.

Fix:
- Do not let public/client requests choose arbitrary shared analysis cache keys.
- Only write shared `verified` cache rows after the server has loaded the product row from `product_data` by key and confirmed source provenance.
- Treat user-OCR/client-supplied verified analyses as user-scoped or review-pending until promoted by a trusted job.
- Add a cache-integrity test that attempts to POST `mode: "verified"` with a known product cache key and verifies no shared verified cache row is created.

## Twenty-Ninth-Pass Monetization And Quota Findings

### 82. Transient RevenueCat Errors Can Downgrade Pro Users To Free

Impact: Paid users can be treated as free when RevenueCat is unavailable, slow, misconfigured, or temporarily returns an SDK error. The app converts any customer-info error into `false`, then uses that false value for the client-side Pro gate and can even write it back to `profiles.is_pro`. The same pattern can happen immediately after a successful purchase because Paywall re-checks entitlement through `refreshProStatus()` before closing. For marketing, this is a high-conversion-risk failure mode: a paying user can see scan limits/paywalls because entitlement status was unknown, not because they lost access.

Evidence:
- `checkProStatus()` returns `false` for any `Purchases.getCustomerInfo()` exception; it does not return an "unknown" state: `services/purchases.js:36`, `services/purchases.js:38`, `services/purchases.js:40`, and `services/purchases.js:41`.
- `refreshProStatus()` calls `checkProStatus()`, immediately updates local `isPro`, and writes the same boolean to `profiles.is_pro`: `services/auth.js:102`, `services/auth.js:104`, `services/auth.js:105`, `services/auth.js:107`, `services/auth.js:110`, and `services/auth.js:111`.
- Purchase success is first derived from the `Purchases.purchasePackage(...)` customer info, but Paywall then calls `refreshProStatus()` and closes the screen regardless of that refresh return value. A transient second `getCustomerInfo()` failure can therefore undo the successful purchase state without showing a purchase-specific recovery path: `services/purchases.js:86`, `services/purchases.js:88`, `services/purchases.js:89`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:176`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:178`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:180`.
- On startup/sign-in, `checkProStatus()` can overwrite `isPro` after `fetchProfile(...)` has set it from the database: `services/auth.js:73`, `services/auth.js:285`, `services/auth.js:286`, `services/auth.js:287`, `services/auth.js:317`, `services/auth.js:319`, and `services/auth.js:326`.
- The scan gate uses `isPro` directly, so a transient false sends users to the paywall instead of allowing Pro access or showing a restore/checking state: `services/auth.js:235`, `services/auth.js:237`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:451`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:452`.
- Human-food quota uses the same local `isPro` gate: `services/auth.js:197`, `services/auth.js:198`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:474`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:475`.

Fix:
- Make entitlement status tri-state: `active`, `inactive`, and `unknown`.
- After purchase success, trust the returned purchase customer info or pass it into the auth state update; do not immediately downgrade based on a second transient refresh failure.
- Never write `profiles.is_pro = false` from a transient RevenueCat read failure.
- Preserve the last known active entitlement for a short grace period and show a visible restore/checking state when status is unknown.
- Add tests/mocks for RevenueCat timeout, network error, empty offerings, expired subscription, and active subscription.

### 83. Sign-Out Resets The In-Memory Free Scan Counter

Impact: A user who has reached the free scan limit while signed in can sign out and immediately get a fresh in-memory guest scan counter until the app restarts or another storage hydration path runs. This weakens the free-to-paid conversion gate and makes quota behavior inconsistent between same-session sign-out, app restart, and server-side profile state.

Evidence:
- Free pet-food access is gated by local `scanCount < 3` unless `isPro` is true: `services/auth.js:235`, `services/auth.js:236`, and `services/auth.js:237`.
- Successful scans increment server state when signed in, but then mirror the count to local `AsyncStorage`: `services/auth.js:207`, `services/auth.js:212`, `services/auth.js:216`, and `services/auth.js:217`.
- Guest/fallback scans increment only local state and local storage: `services/auth.js:225`, `services/auth.js:226`, `services/auth.js:227`, and `services/auth.js:228`.
- The normal sign-out path only calls `supabase.auth.signOut()`; it does not clear or preserve local quota state itself: `services/auth.js:445`, `services/auth.js:446`, `services/auth.js:447`, and `services/auth.js:448`.
- The auth state listener handles `SIGNED_OUT` by setting `scanCount` to `0`, but it does not remove or rewrite `@woof_scan_count` and does not reset human-food quota consistently: `services/auth.js:334`, `services/auth.js:335`, `services/auth.js:336`, `services/auth.js:337`, and `services/auth.js:338`.
- Home uses that in-memory `canScan()` result to decide whether to open the scanner or paywall: `screens/HomeScreen.js:445`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:451`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:452`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:454`.

Fix:
- Treat free quota as device/user scoped and deterministic across sign-in/sign-out, not reset by auth state transitions.
- On sign-out, hydrate the guest quota from local storage instead of forcing `scanCount = 0`, or maintain separate explicit guest and account quota states.
- Move free quota enforcement for authenticated and anonymous users to a server-owned workflow token where possible.
- Add a test that consumes three signed-in scans, signs out, and verifies the next scan still routes to paywall or a clearly intended guest-quota state.

## Thirtieth-Pass Results Recovery Findings

### 84. Text Human-Food Retry Drops The Original Food Name

Impact: If a text-based human-food safety check fails, the "Try Again" recovery path cannot replay the original request. The app supports text-only human-food analysis, but the Results retry handler only retries `human_food` when a `base64` image exists. Users who typed a food name and hit a transient analysis/network error are sent back home instead of getting a real retry.

Evidence:
- Home starts text human-food checks by navigating to Results with `mode: "human_food"`, `foodName`, and `petType`, with no `base64`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:478`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:479`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:480`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:481`.
- `startAnalysis(...)` explicitly supports `human_food` with either `base64` or `foodName`: `services/analysisService.js:161`, `services/analysisService.js:170`, `services/analysisService.js:174`, and `services/analysisService.js:175`.
- The human-food runner chooses the text path when `foodName` exists: `services/analysisService.js:452`, `services/analysisService.js:460`, `services/analysisService.js:461`, and `services/analysisService.js:462`.
- Results receives `foodName` as `preFoodName` and uses it for the initial analysis call: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:179`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:358`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:359`.
- The retry handler only retries `human_food` when `base64` exists and does not include `foodName` in the replacement params; otherwise it falls back to `popToTop()`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:570`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:579`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:580`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:583`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:584`.
- ErrorState wires "Try Again" to that retry handler: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:737`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:738`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:739`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:740`.

Fix:
- Add a `mode === "human_food" && preFoodName` retry branch that preserves `foodName` and `petType`.
- Include `foodName` in the existing human-food retry params.
- Add a test for text-only human-food failure followed by retry.

### 85. Quota Error CTA Says "Upgrade To Pro" But Routes Home

Impact: If the Results screen receives a quota/paywall error from the edge function, the error button is labeled "Upgrade to Pro" but the action is wired to the scan-another/home handler. This creates a direct conversion leak at the moment the user is most ready to upgrade.

Evidence:
- `ErrorState` sets `buttonLabel = "Upgrade to Pro"` for quota/upgrade-classified errors: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2782` and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2783`.
- The same branch assigns `buttonAction = onScanAnother` instead of a paywall navigation handler: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2784` and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2785`.
- Results passes `handleScanAnother` into `ErrorState` as `onScanAnother`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:737`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:740`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:741`.
- `handleScanAnother` only calls `navigation.popToTop()`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:534`.
- The app can still surface server-side quota/rate-limit errors during Results because the analysis service stores edge-function errors and notifies Results: `services/analysisService.js:465`, `services/analysisService.js:466`, `services/analysisService.js:467`, and `services/analysisService.js:468`.

Fix:
- Pass an `onUpgrade` handler into `ErrorState` that navigates to Paywall with source/error context.
- Keep "Back to Home" separate from "Upgrade to Pro" so button labels and actions always match.
- Add a Results error-state test for quota errors.

## Thirty-First-Pass Privacy And Contribution Finding

### 86. User OCR Contributions Become Public Catalog Data Without Clear Disclosure

Impact: When a user photographs an ingredient label for a product Woof does not know, the app saves the OCR'd ingredient list into the shared `product_data` catalog for future users. That can be a legitimate growth loop, but the privacy and delete-account copy does not clearly disclose that user-contributed product text may become shared catalog data, may be readable by all clients, and may outlive account deletion. This is a trust/App Review risk and makes the "all associated data" deletion promise too broad.

Evidence:
- The ingredient-label flow saves successful OCR output to the database as source `user_ocr`: `services/analysisService.js:530`, `services/analysisService.js:532`, `services/analysisService.js:533`, and `services/analysisService.js:534`.
- The cache helper describes this as a growth engine where every successful OCR enriches the database for future users: `services/cache.js:266`, `services/cache.js:267`, `services/cache.js:268`, and `services/cache.js:270`.
- `saveProductData(...)` writes product name, brand, ingredients, full ingredient text, ingredient count, and source via the `save_product_data` RPC: `services/cache.js:275`, `services/cache.js:277`, `services/cache.js:278`, `services/cache.js:279`, `services/cache.js:280`, `services/cache.js:281`, and `services/cache.js:282`.
- `product_data` is explicitly not user-specific and has an "Anyone can read product data" RLS policy: `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:25`, `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:28`, `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:29`, and `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:30`.
- The in-app privacy policy only says label photos are sent for analysis and not stored after processing; it does not explain that OCR-derived label text can become shared catalog data: `legal.js:37`, `legal.js:40`, `legal.js:46`, `legal.js:48`, and `legal.js:50`.
- The same policy promises users can delete their account and "all associated data" from Profile: `legal.js:66` and `legal.js:67`.
- The public privacy page similarly says scan images are not stored beyond analysis and that account deletion removes all associated data, without carving out shared catalog contributions: `docs/privacy.html:114`, `docs/privacy.html:115`, `docs/privacy.html:117`, and `docs/privacy.html:118`.
- Profile deletion UI repeats the broad "all associated data" promise: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:73`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:75`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:87`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:89`.

Fix:
- Decide whether user OCR catalog contributions are personal data, anonymous contributions, or review-pending operational data.
- Add an explicit disclosure before/within ingredient-label capture that OCR text may improve the shared catalog for other users.
- Store contribution provenance separately from user identity, or store enough ownership metadata to honor deletion/export requests.
- Update privacy/delete copy to distinguish account/history deletion from retained anonymized/shared product catalog data.
- Add an admin/review workflow for removing bad or user-requested contribution rows.

## Thirty-Second-Pass Human-Food Safety Copy Finding

### 87. Human-Food Caution Results Are Explained As "Dangerous"

Impact: Human-food safety results have three states: `safe`, `caution`, and `dangerous`. The explanation header only checks for `safe`; every non-safe result is titled "Why It's Dangerous." That means a caution result can be exaggerated as dangerous, which undermines trust, confuses feeding guidance, and makes the safety feature look less calibrated during first-use marketing traffic.

Evidence:
- The edge function requires human-food responses to use `safetyLevel: "safe" | "caution" | "dangerous"`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:381`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:384`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:759`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:760`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:761`.
- The result UI renders a three-state badge for the same values: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2864`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2868`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2869`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2870`.
- The human-food result card uses the correct badge state and food name before the explanation: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:804`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:807`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:808`.
- The explanation title maps only `safe` to "Safe" and maps both `caution` and `dangerous` to "Dangerous": `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:864`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:867`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:869`.
- The symptoms block later treats `caution` differently from `dangerous`, confirming the UI already expects a distinct caution state: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:876`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:880`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:882`.

Fix:
- Map `safe` to "Why It's Likely Safe", `caution` to "Why To Use Caution", and `dangerous` to "Why It's Dangerous".
- Add a UI test or fixture render for all three human-food safety levels.
- Review all human-food labels for exact state mapping before marketing the safety checker.

## Thirty-Third-Pass Appearance Configuration Finding

### 88. Appearance Controls Conflict With Native Light-Only Configuration

Impact: The Profile screen offers Auto, Light, and Dark appearance settings, and the theme system resolves against the OS color scheme. The native Expo config, however, pins `userInterfaceStyle` to `light`. That makes the Auto option unreliable in production builds and can create mismatched system surfaces, status-bar behavior, permission sheets, and first-launch screenshots when users expect the app to follow dark mode.

Evidence:
- The native app config sets `userInterfaceStyle` to `light`: `app.json:9`.
- The theme provider reads the OS color scheme with `useColorScheme()` and treats `"system"` as a supported preference: `theme.js:193`, `theme.js:195`, and `theme.js:233`.
- The app exposes an in-profile Appearance section with `Auto`, `Light`, and `Dark` choices: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:318`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:329`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:332`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:334`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:335`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:336`.
- The app changes the Expo status bar based on the resolved theme: `App.js:106` and `theme.js:70`, `theme.js:84`.

Fix:
- Set `userInterfaceStyle` to `automatic` if Auto/Dark remain supported.
- If the release intentionally supports light mode only, remove the Auto/Dark controls and dark palette from public UI.
- Add launch QA screenshots for light, dark, and system modes on iOS and Android before using store screenshots or paid ads.

## Thirty-Fourth-Pass Startup Quota Finding

### 89. Free Quota Gates Can Open Before Persisted Counts Hydrate

Impact: Free quota state starts at zero and is hydrated from AsyncStorage asynchronously. For guest users, app loading can finish before the persisted scan and human-food counts have been read, so a fast tap after launch can evaluate `canScan()` / `canCheckHumanFood()` against the default zero counts. That weakens the paywall gate and makes first-session quota behavior depend on storage timing instead of an explicit source of truth.

Evidence:
- `AuthProvider` initializes `scanCount` and `humanFoodCountToday` to `0`: `services/auth.js:35` and `services/auth.js:36`.
- The scan gate allows free users while `scanCount < 3`: `services/auth.js:235`, `services/auth.js:236`, and `services/auth.js:237`.
- The human-food gate allows free users while `humanFoodCountToday < 1`: `services/auth.js:197`, `services/auth.js:198`, and `services/auth.js:199`.
- Persisted scan count hydration is fire-and-forget and not awaited before app loading ends: `services/auth.js:248`, `services/auth.js:249`, `services/auth.js:250`, and `services/auth.js:297`.
- Persisted human-food quota hydration is also fire-and-forget and not awaited before app loading ends: `services/auth.js:260`, `services/auth.js:261`, and `services/auth.js:297`.
- Guest startup explicitly does not await purchases init and then clears loading, leaving local quota hydration as the only guest source of truth: `services/auth.js:292`, `services/auth.js:293`, `services/auth.js:294`, and `services/auth.js:297`.
- Home immediately routes scan and human-food actions using those gate functions: `screens/HomeScreen.js:445`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:451`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:452`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:454`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:467`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:474`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:475`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:485`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:488`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:489`.

Fix:
- Add an explicit `quotaLoaded` state and keep quota-gated actions disabled/loading until local or server quota has hydrated.
- For guests, await scan and human-food quota reads before setting auth loading false, or make the gate pessimistic until hydrated.
- Separate auth loading from quota loading only if Home/Scanner/Results can reliably block quota-sensitive actions.
- Add a cold-start regression test with persisted exhausted guest counts and immediate scan/human-food taps.

## Thirty-Fifth-Pass Legal Versioning Finding

### 90. Public And In-App Legal Documents Are Not Version-Synchronized

Impact: App Review, subscription trust, and privacy support depend on users seeing one authoritative set of terms and privacy promises. Today the in-app legal HTML and the public `docs/` legal pages have different effective dates and materially different subscription/account wording. A user can read one policy from the app and another from the website/App Store privacy URL, which makes marketing, review responses, and customer disputes harder to defend.

Evidence:
- In-app legal uses a shared `EFFECTIVE_DATE` of March 16, 2026 for both Terms and Privacy: `legal.js:3`, `legal.js:33`, and `legal.js:86`.
- The public Privacy Policy page says it was last updated March 17, 2025, not March 16, 2026: `docs/privacy.html:79`.
- The public Terms page says it was last updated March 23, 2026, also not March 16, 2026: `docs/terms.html:79`.
- In-app Terms say some plans include a free trial and do not list exact public prices: `legal.js:102`, `legal.js:103`, `legal.js:106`, and `legal.js:107`.
- Public Terms hardcode all three plan prices and a 3-day free trial: `docs/terms.html:95`, `docs/terms.html:99`, `docs/terms.html:100`, and `docs/terms.html:101`.
- In-app Privacy lists Open Pet Food Facts as a third-party service: `legal.js:57`, `legal.js:61`.
- Public Privacy omits Open Pet Food Facts from its third-party services list: `docs/privacy.html:105`, `docs/privacy.html:108`, `docs/privacy.html:109`, `docs/privacy.html:110`, and `docs/privacy.html:111`.

Fix:
- Generate in-app and public legal pages from one source of truth, or add a release checklist item that diffs them before each submission.
- Avoid hardcoding subscription prices/trial periods in static public Terms unless they are updated automatically from store metadata.
- Keep App Store privacy URL, in-app legal modal, support site, and any marketing pages on the same effective date and content version.
- Add a simple CI check that fails if legal effective dates or required third-party-service lists diverge.

## Thirty-Sixth-Pass Guest Consent Finding

### 91. Guest Users Can Scan Before Seeing Any Terms Or Privacy Acceptance Surface

Impact: The app intentionally supports guest scanning, but the only explicit "By continuing, you agree to our Terms and Privacy Policy" copy is on the sign-in screen. A new user can complete or skip onboarding, land on Home, scan pet food, and run human-food safety checks without seeing that consent surface. That is a legal/App Review and trust risk because the Terms claim use of the app implies agreement, while the product funnel does not put those terms in front of the highest-volume guest path.

Evidence:
- The main navigator always shows the app after auth loading, and the code comments that guest users can scan without signing in: `App.js:103`, `App.js:104`, `App.js:107`, and `App.js:114`.
- If the onboarding storage read times out or rejects, the app sets `showOnboarding(false)` and enters the app anyway: `App.js:152`, `App.js:156`, `App.js:159`, `App.js:160`, `App.js:161`, `App.js:171`, `App.js:175`, and `App.js:176`.
- Onboarding can be skipped and marks onboarding complete without any Terms/Privacy link or acceptance copy: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:390`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:392`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:393`.
- Finishing onboarding also only writes `@woof_onboarding_complete` and enters the app: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:396`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:400`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:401`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:402`.
- Home routes the primary scan action directly to Scanner when `canScan()` passes: `screens/HomeScreen.js:445`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:451`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:452`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:454`.
- Home routes text and photo human-food checks directly to Results/Scanner when quota checks pass: `screens/HomeScreen.js:467`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:474`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:478`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:485`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:488`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:492`.
- The only explicit acceptance copy is on `AuthScreen`: `screens/AuthScreen.js:224`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:229`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:230`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:235`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:239`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:245`, and `screens/AuthScreen.js:249`.
- In-app Terms say that by using Woof, the user agrees to the terms: `legal.js:88`.

Fix:
- Add Terms/Privacy links and acceptance copy to onboarding's final CTA, or show a first-scan consent sheet before guest scans/human-food checks.
- Track a distinct accepted legal version key, not only `@woof_onboarding_complete`.
- Treat first-run storage timeout/rejection as "legal acceptance unknown"; allow the app shell to load, but gate scan/search/human-food analysis behind the same legal notice.
- If passive browse/use is intended to imply agreement, make the notice visible before any safety-sensitive or paid-vendor analysis starts.
- Add a first-run QA test that a brand-new guest cannot start Scanner, search analysis, or human-food analysis without seeing the legal notice.

## Thirty-Seventh-Pass Session Downgrade Finding

### 92. Expired Sessions Can Silently Downgrade Paid Analysis Requests To Guest Identity

Impact: When a signed-in user's Supabase token is expired or refresh fails, the analysis client signs the user out and sends the paid analysis request with anonymous guest headers. That means a signed-in or Pro user can lose authenticated quota/profile context, hit anonymous IP-rate-limit behavior, miss authenticated server quota checks, and save/history behavior can diverge from what the UI implied. This is especially risky during launch because token refresh failures become inconsistent guest scans rather than a visible "sign in again" recovery.

Evidence:
- `_getAuthHeaders()` returns guest headers when there is no session: `services/claude.js:35`, `services/claude.js:42`, `services/claude.js:43`, and `services/claude.js:44`.
- If a token refresh fails, `_getAuthHeaders()` signs out locally and still returns `GUEST_HEADERS`: `services/claude.js:50`, `services/claude.js:53`, `services/claude.js:57`, `services/claude.js:59`, `services/claude.js:60`, `services/claude.js:61`, and `services/claude.js:62`.
- Every paid analysis/helper wrapper uses `_getAuthHeaders()` before calling the edge functions, including streaming analysis, non-streaming analysis, identification, OCR, ingredient lookup, and product lookup: `services/claude.js:260`, `services/claude.js:446`, `services/claude.js:669`, `services/claude.js:727`, `services/claude.js:776`, and `services/claude.js:839`.
- The main analyze edge function treats auth as optional; it only returns `401` if an `Authorization` header is present and invalid: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:963`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:972`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:973`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:981`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:983`.
- Authenticated analysis is rate-limited and quota-checked by user id/profile, but anonymous requests use IP behavior instead: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:991`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:993`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1034`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1035`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1064`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1066`.
- The product-lookup edge function also treats failed auth as non-blocking and then applies anonymous rate limiting: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1056`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1065`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1068`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1069`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1078`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1080`.

Fix:
- For an existing signed-in session, treat refresh failure as an auth error, not a guest fallback.
- Preserve the pending scan/search payload and route the user through sign-in/restore before starting paid analysis.
- Only use guest headers when the app is explicitly in guest mode before the request starts.
- Add tests for expired token, failed refresh, revoked session, and guest mode to prove they produce distinct UI and server behavior.

## Thirty-Eighth-Pass Store Compatibility Finding

### 93. Live App Store Compatibility Includes Mac And Apple Vision Without Matching QA Evidence

Impact: The live App Store page exposes Woof beyond iPhone/iPad: it lists compatibility for Mac with Apple silicon and Apple Vision. The app is a mobile camera-first scanner with phone/tablet-oriented UI assumptions, and the existing local release configuration/test evidence does not show any Mac or visionOS validation. Paid traffic or App Review can therefore exercise platforms where camera permission, scanner framing, purchase restore, WebViews, and layout behavior may be untested.

Evidence:
- The live App Store page for `id6760733899`, checked on June 6, 2026, lists the app as "Designed for iPad. Not verified for macOS" and includes compatibility entries for Mac and Apple Vision: `https://apps.apple.com/us/app/woof-pet-food-scanner/id6760733899`.
- The same live page lists Mac requirements as macOS 12.0 or later on Apple M1 or later, and Apple Vision requirements as visionOS 1.0 or later: `https://apps.apple.com/us/app/woof-pet-food-scanner/id6760733899`.
- Local Expo config declares iPad support but has no explicit Mac/Vision gating or QA profile: `app.json:22`, `app.json:23`, and `eas.json:24`.
- The scanner is camera-first and uses static window dimensions and a fixed 260px scan square: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:27`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:35`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:36`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:37`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:38`.
- Existing package scripts only start Expo targets and do not define a desktop/spatial acceptance matrix: `package.json:5`, `package.json:6`, `package.json:7`, `package.json:8`, and `package.json:9`.

Fix:
- Decide whether Mac and Apple Vision are supported launch platforms.
- If not, opt out or restrict availability in App Store Connect where possible, and update store metadata accordingly.
- If yes, add a Mac/visionOS acceptance pass for onboarding, camera permissions, scan fallback, search, results, paywall, restore, profile, legal WebViews, and account deletion.
- Add App Store compatibility review to every release checklist alongside iPhone/iPad screenshots.

## Thirty-Ninth-Pass App Store Privacy Label Finding

### 94. Live App Store Privacy Label Does Not Cleanly Match Authenticated Scan And History Behavior

Impact: App Review, paid-user trust, and privacy compliance can be hurt if Apple's privacy nutrition label understates how scan content is tied to an account. The live App Store page says photos/videos are collected as user content but not linked to identity, while signed-in scan requests carry an auth token and the app syncs scan history fields, including the local `photo_uri`, under `user_id`. Even if the intended policy is "process photos transiently," the live privacy label, public privacy page, in-app legal copy, and actual authenticated data paths need to describe the same model.

Evidence:
- The live App Store page for `id6760733899`, checked on June 6, 2026, lists `User Content -> Photos or Videos` under `Data Not Linked to You`: `https://apps.apple.com/us/app/woof-pet-food-scanner/id6760733899`.
- The same live page lists linked data only as purchases, email address, user ID, and product interaction, and links to the public privacy policy: `https://apps.apple.com/us/app/woof-pet-food-scanner/id6760733899`.
- The live privacy policy says camera images are sent for analysis and not stored permanently, but it still names Anthropic rather than the OpenAI image-identify path: `https://aizakmi08.github.io/woof/privacy.html`.
- Client analysis requests use `_getAuthHeaders()` and attach `Authorization: Bearer <token>` whenever a Supabase session exists: `services/claude.js:35`, `services/claude.js:36`, `services/claude.js:68`, and `services/claude.js:71`.
- Photo analysis sends `imageBase64` through that authenticated analysis path: `services/claude.js:481`, `services/claude.js:485`, and `services/claude.js:523`.
- The analyze edge function reads the `Authorization` header and treats authenticated calls as user-scoped traffic: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:972`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:973`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:981`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:985`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:991`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:995`.
