- History saving persists `photoUri` from scan state, maps it to `photo_uri`, and upserts it into Supabase with `user_id`: `services/analysisService.js:844`, `services/analysisService.js:852`, `services/history.js:55`, `services/history.js:57`, `services/history.js:65`, `services/history.js:192`, `services/history.js:193`, and `services/history.js:194`.
- The `scan_history` table schema stores `user_id` and `photo_uri` in the same row: `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:42`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:44`, and `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:52`.

Fix:
- Re-run App Store Connect privacy answers from the real production data map, not only from intended policy.
- Decide whether scan photos/derived photo references are linked, transient, local-only, or synced, then make code, App Store privacy labels, public privacy policy, and in-app legal copy match that decision.
- Stop syncing local `photo_uri` to Supabase unless it is intentionally disclosed and useful across devices.
- Add a privacy review checklist item for every release that touches scan, history, auth, AI/vendor routing, or product-data contribution behavior.

## Fortieth-Pass Free Result Entitlement Finding

### 95. Free Result Content Does Not Match The In-App Terms Promise

Impact: The free-to-Pro funnel and legal trust are inconsistent. The in-app Terms say free scans show the first 3 ingredients, but the pet-food Results screen only renders the ingredient list inside the Pro-only branch. A free user can therefore receive less than the app's own legal copy promises, while the paywall asks them to upgrade for "Full ingredients." That mismatch is risky before marketing because disappointed users may view the gate as misleading rather than as a clear upgrade boundary.

Evidence:
- In-app Terms promise that free scans show "the overall score, quick stats, a summary verdict, and the first 3 ingredients": `legal.js:102`, `legal.js:103`, and `legal.js:104`.
- Free pet-food results render summary rows, quick stats, verdict, and then `ProGateOverlay`; there is no free `IngredientsSection` call before the gate: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:987`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:993`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1003`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1006`.
- The full ingredient section is rendered only inside the `isPro` branch: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1016`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1017`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1093`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1094`.
- `IngredientsSection` has explicit support for a free preview contract: its comment says free users should see all passed ingredients after the caller slices to 3 with `fadeLastItem`, but the current pet-food Results caller does not use that path for free users: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:1336`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:1353`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:1354`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:1355`.
- The paywall gate copy sells "Full ingredients," so a limited preview would still preserve the upgrade value if implemented consistently: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:190`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:193`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:226`.

Fix:
- Decide the exact free-result product contract: no ingredients, first 3 ingredients, or a faded preview.
- If free users should see the first 3 ingredients, render `IngredientsSection` before `ProGateOverlay` with `ingredients={result.ingredients.slice(0, 3)}`, `totalCount={result.ingredients.length}`, and the intended locked/fade behavior.
- If free users should not see ingredients, update in-app Terms, public Terms, paywall, and onboarding/support copy to remove the first-3-ingredients promise.
- Add a free-vs-Pro result smoke test that verifies visible sections for score, quick stats, verdict, ingredients, quality breakdown, recalls, reviews, and disclaimer.

## Forty-First-Pass Database Function Hardening Finding

### 96. Several SECURITY DEFINER Functions Run Without A Pinned Search Path

Impact: Database hardening is incomplete for privileged RPCs. Several `SECURITY DEFINER` functions mutate quota, rate-limit, cleanup, and product-data tables while relying on unqualified table names and the caller/session `search_path`. Even if the current public schema privileges make exploitation harder, launch readiness should not depend on implicit schema resolution for functions that bypass RLS or update shared data. This compounds the existing public-execute and unauthorized-mutation findings because the same functions are high-value abuse targets.

Evidence:
- `delete_own_account` and `search_products` show the safer local pattern by explicitly setting `SET search_path = public`: `supabase/migrations/006_delete_account.sql:8`, `supabase/migrations/006_delete_account.sql:9`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:39`, and `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:40`.
- `check_rate_limit(...)` is `SECURITY DEFINER`, uses unqualified `rate_limits`, and has no `SET search_path`: `supabase/migrations/002_rate_limits.sql:13`, `supabase/migrations/002_rate_limits.sql:20`, and `supabase/migrations/002_rate_limits.sql:29`.
- `increment_scan_count(...)` is `SECURITY DEFINER`, uses unqualified `profiles`, and has no `SET search_path`: `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:2`, `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:5`, and `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:10`.
- `save_product_data(...)` is `SECURITY DEFINER`, uses unqualified `product_data`, and has no `SET search_path`: `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:8`, `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:20`, and `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:23`.
- Human-food quota RPCs are `SECURITY DEFINER`, use unqualified `profiles`, and have no `SET search_path`: `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:13`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:16`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:22`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:38`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:41`, and `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:49`.
- Cleanup/rate-limit helper functions also appear as `SECURITY DEFINER` without a pinned `search_path`: `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:13`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:16`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:34`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:37`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:17`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:24`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:67`, and `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:70`.

Fix:
- Add `SET search_path = public` to every `SECURITY DEFINER` function that intentionally works only with public tables, or schema-qualify all table/function references.
- Recreate privileged functions in migrations after adding search-path hardening; do not rely on comments or caller-side behavior.
- Combine this with explicit `REVOKE`/minimal `GRANT` statements so privileged functions are both hard to call and hard to redirect.
- Add a migration lint/check that fails when a `SECURITY DEFINER` function lacks `SET search_path` or schema-qualified references.

## Forty-Second-Pass OAuth Hardening Finding

### 97. Mobile Google OAuth Uses Implicit Token Redirects Instead Of PKCE

Impact: Google sign-in is implemented with the implicit OAuth flow on a native mobile app. The redirect URL can carry both access and refresh tokens, and the app manually extracts those tokens from the URL fragment before calling `setSession`. That is weaker than the installed Supabase client's own PKCE code-exchange path for mobile apps, and it compounds the existing AuthStorage finding because long-lived refresh tokens are both delivered through the redirect and then persisted in AsyncStorage. For paid marketing, OAuth must be boring and defensible: failed redirects should be visible, and successful redirects should not depend on bearer tokens being returned through a custom-scheme URL.

Evidence:
- The Supabase client sets storage, refresh, persistence, and `detectSessionInUrl: false`, but does not set `flowType: "pkce"`: `services/supabase.js:5`, `services/supabase.js:6`, `services/supabase.js:7`, `services/supabase.js:8`, `services/supabase.js:9`, and `services/supabase.js:10`.
- The installed Supabase client types say the OAuth flow defaults to implicit and that PKCE is recommended for mobile and server-side applications: `node_modules/@supabase/supabase-js/src/lib/types.ts:109`.
- The installed default auth options confirm `flowType: 'implicit'`: `node_modules/@supabase/supabase-js/src/lib/constants.ts:28`, `node_modules/@supabase/supabase-js/src/lib/constants.ts:31`, and `node_modules/@supabase/supabase-js/src/lib/constants.ts:32`.
- Google sign-in asks Supabase for an OAuth URL with `skipBrowserRedirect: true`, opens it with `WebBrowser.openAuthSessionAsync`, and then parses only the redirect hash fragment for `access_token` and `refresh_token`: `services/auth.js:383`, `services/auth.js:386`, `services/auth.js:387`, `services/auth.js:393`, `services/auth.js:398`, `services/auth.js:399`, `services/auth.js:400`, `services/auth.js:401`, `services/auth.js:402`, and `services/auth.js:403`.
- When both tokens are present, the app directly installs them with `supabase.auth.setSession(...)`: `services/auth.js:405`, `services/auth.js:406`, `services/auth.js:407`, and `services/auth.js:408`.
- The installed Supabase auth client already has a PKCE exchange path that stores a code verifier and posts to `/token?grant_type=pkce`: `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:1294`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:1298`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:1302`, and `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:1305`.
- The same client adds `code_challenge` and `code_challenge_method` to the OAuth URL when `flowType === 'pkce'`: `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:3293`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:3294`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:3299`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:3300`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:3301`, and `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:3303`.

Fix:
- Configure the Supabase client with `flowType: "pkce"` on native builds.
- In Google sign-in, parse the returned `code` query parameter and call `supabase.auth.exchangeCodeForSession(code)` instead of accepting access/refresh tokens from the redirect fragment.
- Keep `detectSessionInUrl: false` for React Native, but make the manual redirect handler validate OAuth `error`, `error_description`, `state`, and missing-code cases.
- Pair this with the secure-storage migration so PKCE verifier/session data and refresh tokens do not live in plain AsyncStorage on native devices.
- Add device tests for Google success, cancel, denied consent, bad redirect URI, missing verifier, and repeated sign-in after app restart.

## Forty-Third-Pass History Migration Finding

### 98. Guest History Migration Is One-Time Per User And Can Drop Later Guest Scans

Impact: Guest scans are part of the acquisition funnel, but the history migration only runs once per signed-in user. If a user signs in, signs out, scans products as a guest, and then signs back into the same account, those later guest scans stay in the anonymous legacy key instead of being moved into the user's account or Supabase history. The user can perceive this as lost scan history right after account conversion, which is exactly the kind of trust break that hurts paid marketing.

Evidence:
- Anonymous/guest history uses the shared legacy AsyncStorage key because `getStorageKey(null)` returns `@woof/scan_history`: `services/history.js:4`, `services/history.js:5`, `services/history.js:32`, `services/history.js:33`, and `services/history.js:34`.
- Every scan history entry writes to the storage key for the current user id, which is the legacy key when no session exists: `services/history.js:177`, `services/history.js:179`, `services/history.js:180`, `services/history.js:185`, and `services/history.js:186`.
- On sign-in, the auth provider starts `migrateLocalHistoryToSupabase(s.user.id)`: `services/auth.js:329` and `services/auth.js:330`.
- The migration has a per-user `@woof/history_migrated_<userId>` flag and returns immediately when that flag is already `"true"`: `services/history.js:236`, `services/history.js:237`, `services/history.js:240`, `services/history.js:241`, `services/history.js:242`, and `services/history.js:243`.
- The code only checks the legacy guest history key after that early return, so any guest scans created after the first completed migration are skipped on later sign-ins: `services/history.js:246`, `services/history.js:248`, `services/history.js:251`, `services/history.js:257`, and `services/history.js:260`.
- Signing out does not clear, migrate, or otherwise account for local guest history; it only calls `supabase.auth.signOut()`, while the auth listener clears profile/pro state and resets the in-memory scan count: `services/auth.js:446`, `services/auth.js:447`, `services/auth.js:334`, `services/auth.js:335`, `services/auth.js:336`, `services/auth.js:337`, and `services/auth.js:338`.

Fix:
- Replace the one-time migration flag with an idempotent merge that always checks the anonymous legacy key on sign-in.
- Track a migrated entry-id set or source marker instead of a coarse per-user done flag, then merge only entries not already present in user-specific local storage or Supabase.
- After successful merge, clear only the migrated anonymous entries; do not leave new guest scans stranded behind a stale flag.
- Add a regression test: sign in, migrate, sign out, create a guest scan, sign in again, and verify the new guest scan appears in account history locally and in Supabase.

## Forty-Fourth-Pass Product Image Cache Finding

### 99. Product Lookup Finds Images But Does Not Persist Them Into Product Data

Impact: Product imagery is treated as part of the search and history polish, but the product-lookup edge function drops image URLs when it writes or returns cached rows. A first lookup can return an image from Amazon, Chewy, or another source, but later search results, recent searches, and history backfill depend on `product_data.image_url`. That makes the catalog look less complete over time and pushes history back toward local camera URI thumbnails, which already conflict with the privacy/retention model.

Evidence:
- Product lookup result types include `imageUrl`, and multiple scraper paths extract or return it: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:140`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:141`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:335`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:347`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:768`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:787`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:871`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:890`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:960`.
- The fresh lookup response includes `imageUrl: best.imageUrl || null`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1264`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1273`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1274`.
- The cache write into `product_data` persists `source_url` but omits `image_url`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1238`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1240`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1248`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1249`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1250`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1251`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1252`.
- The cache-hit response also returns `sourceUrl` but not `imageUrl`, even if the row has one: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1137`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1139`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1147`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1148`.
- The database schema and older `save_product_data` RPC already support `image_url`: `supabase/migrations/011_add_image_url.sql:1`, `supabase/migrations/011_add_image_url.sql:2`, `supabase/migrations/011_add_image_url.sql:20`, `supabase/migrations/011_add_image_url.sql:21`, and `supabase/migrations/011_add_image_url.sql:27`.
- Search results render `item.image_url` when present: `screens/HomeScreen.js:683`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:684`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:685`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:686`.
- History enrichment explicitly looks up `product_data.image_url` to avoid missing thumbnails: `services/history.js:100`, `services/history.js:107`, `services/history.js:109`, `services/history.js:113`, and `services/history.js:116`.

Fix:
- Include `image_url: best.imageUrl || null` in the product-lookup `product_data` upsert, preserving an existing image when the fresh lookup does not provide one.
- Return `imageUrl: cached.image_url || null` from product-lookup cache hits.
- Add a cache contract test that a scraped lookup with an image writes `product_data.image_url`, search returns it, and history enrichment can use it after app reinstall.
- Backfill `product_data.image_url` for rows where `source_url` points to a known product page and an image can be safely extracted without rerunning full paid scraping.

## Forty-Fifth-Pass Timeout Recovery Finding

### 100. Helper Timeouts Can Be Swallowed As User Aborts And Leave Results Spinning

Impact: The photo scan flow has short helper-level timeouts, but at least the product-identification timeout is surfaced as a generic `AbortError`. `_runPhoto` treats every `AbortError` as user cancellation and returns without setting an error, notifying subscribers, or scheduling cleanup. Because that silent return resolves the analysis promise, `_withTimeout` clears the global timeout instead of firing the 120-second safety net. The Results screen can therefore remain in its loading state indefinitely after the first helper already timed out at 15 seconds. In a store aisle, this turns a recoverable timeout into a perceived frozen scan.

Evidence:
- The analysis service global hard timeout is 120 seconds, but it is cleared when the analysis promise resolves: `services/analysisService.js:24`, `services/analysisService.js:98`, `services/analysisService.js:101`, `services/analysisService.js:104`, `services/analysisService.js:105`, `services/analysisService.js:107`, `services/analysisService.js:116`, and `services/analysisService.js:117`.
- `identifyProduct(...)` creates an internal `AbortController` and aborts it after 15 seconds: `services/claude.js:665`, `services/claude.js:671`, `services/claude.js:672`, `services/claude.js:683`, and `services/claude.js:691`.
- `_runPhoto(...)` catches identification errors and immediately returns on `err.name === "AbortError"` or `signal.aborted`, before setting `state.error`, `state.status`, `_notify(...)`, or cleanup: `services/analysisService.js:574`, `services/analysisService.js:581`, `services/analysisService.js:583`, `services/analysisService.js:588`, and `services/analysisService.js:589`.
- The user-facing Results screen only has progressive loading timers at 8, 20, and 30 seconds while the hard timeout is handled by `analysisService._withTimeout`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:434`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:438`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:439`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:442`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:445`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:446`.
- Because `_runPhoto` returns without an error notification, the subscriber path that would set `error`, stop streaming, and mark the result done is not reached: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:414`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:415`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:416`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:417`.

Fix:
- Distinguish user cancellation from helper timeout. Use an explicit timeout error/reason, such as `IDENTIFY_TIMEOUT`, instead of bare `controller.abort()` for helper deadlines.
- In `_runPhoto`, handle helper timeouts as visible, retryable failures or route to the ingredient-label fallback instead of returning silently.
- Make `signal.aborted` mean user/global cancellation only; do not collapse internal helper aborts into the same branch.
- Add a regression test with a mocked 15-second identification timeout verifying that Results exits loading with an actionable error or label fallback before the global 120-second timeout.

## Forty-Sixth-Pass Ingredient-Label Lifecycle Finding

### 101. Ingredient-Label Recovery Leaves Background Analyses Marked Running

Impact: When a photo scan identifies a product but cannot find verified product data, the UI correctly asks the user to photograph the ingredient label. The background service, however, never marks that analysis as paused, complete, cancelled, or cleaned up. It schedules cleanup while the state is still `running`, and the cleanup helper refuses to delete running entries. Repeated scans of products missing from the catalog can therefore leave stale in-memory analyses and key aliases for the rest of the app session, making diagnostics, deduplication, and memory behavior less predictable during exactly the hard-scan path the app needs to survive in stores.

Evidence:
- `startAnalysis(...)` creates a running state and stores it in the process-level `analyses` map: `services/analysisService.js:198`, `services/analysisService.js:199`, `services/analysisService.js:200`, `services/analysisService.js:210`, and `services/analysisService.js:234`.
- After product identification, `_runPhoto(...)` rekeys the temp entry to the normalized product key: `services/analysisService.js:620`, `services/analysisService.js:621`, and `services/analysisService.js:622`.
- On a database miss, `_runPhoto(...)` emits `need_ingredient_photo` and schedules cleanup, but never changes `state.status` away from `"running"` before returning: `services/analysisService.js:743`, `services/analysisService.js:745`, `services/analysisService.js:746`, `services/analysisService.js:747`, `services/analysisService.js:756`, `services/analysisService.js:758`.
- `_scheduleCleanup(...)` only deletes entries when `entry.status !== "running"`: `services/analysisService.js:62`, `services/analysisService.js:66`, `services/analysisService.js:68`, `services/analysisService.js:69`, and `services/analysisService.js:70`.
- The Results subscriber handles `need_ingredient_photo` by stopping streaming and showing `NeedsLabelCard`, but does not mark the service entry done or call any cancellation/cleanup API: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:402`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:406`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:407`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:413`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:687`.
- The global timeout is also cleared once `_runPhoto(...)` returns, so it does not later transition the stale running entry to an error state: `services/analysisService.js:104`, `services/analysisService.js:105`, `services/analysisService.js:116`, and `services/analysisService.js:117`.

Fix:
- Add an explicit `paused_for_label` or `needs_input` status for this branch, and make cleanup rules account for it.
- When `need_ingredient_photo` is emitted, either mark the original analysis complete/paused with a bounded TTL or cancel and remove it once the UI has navigated to `IngredientCapture`.
- When the user chooses "Capture ingredient label" or "Use AI estimate instead", cancel or finalize the original front-photo analysis entry before starting the next Results analysis.
- Add a regression test that simulates repeated unknown-product scans and verifies the analysis map/aliases do not grow with stale `running` entries.

## Forty-Seventh-Pass Search Pet-Type Finding

### 102. Search-Selected Products Can Be Scored With Unknown Pet Type

Impact: Search is marketed as the fast alternative to scanning, but the search path does not know whether the selected food is for dogs or cats. It sends verified ingredient data to analysis with `petType: "unknown"`, then saves history from that result. For a safety product that advertises dog/cat ingredient judgment, this can make search results less species-specific than photo scans and can produce inconsistent history/category behavior.

Evidence:
- The `product_data` schema has product name, brand, ingredients, nutrition, source, image, and expiry fields, but no dog/cat category field: `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:4`, `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:7`, `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:8`, `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:9`, `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:12`, and `supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql:16`.
- `search_products(...)` returns `cache_key`, `product_name`, `brand`, `ingredient_count`, `source`, `image_url`, and `rank`, but no `pet_type`: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:28`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:29`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:30`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:31`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:32`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:33`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:34`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:35`, and `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:36`.
- Home navigates search taps to Results with `mode`, `productName`, `brand`, and `cacheKey`, but no pet type: `screens/HomeScreen.js:389`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:390`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:391`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:392`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:393`.
- Results passes its `petType` variable into search analysis, but for search taps that value is undefined because the route did not include it: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:179`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:181`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:331`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:336`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:340`.
- `_runSearch(...)` builds the verified-data payload with `petType: petType || "unknown"`: `services/analysisService.js:318`, `services/analysisService.js:381`, `services/analysisService.js:384`, and `services/analysisService.js:401`.
- The edge function includes `Pet Type: ...` in the verified-data prompt when `opffProduct.petType` exists, so `"unknown"` becomes part of the scored input: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:522`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:527`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:530`, and `services/claude.js:537`.
- History saving persists `state.result.petType`, so search results with unknown pet type can carry that ambiguity into replay/history: `services/analysisService.js:823`, `services/analysisService.js:844`, `services/analysisService.js:847`, and `services/analysisService.js:849`.

Fix:
- Add pet category to `product_data` and `search_products`, or require the user to choose dog/cat before a search result analysis starts.
- Pass `petType` from Home to Results and into `startAnalysis` for search mode.
- Include pet type in canonical cache keys where the score can differ by species, or explicitly prove that pet-food scoring is species-agnostic.
- Backfill pet category from trusted source data, not product-name guessing alone.
- Add dog-food and cat-food search fixtures that verify the selected species reaches the edge-function prompt, cache key, result, and history row.

## Forty-Eighth-Pass Signed-In History Timeout Finding

### 103. History Auth Timeout Can Save Signed-In Scans As Anonymous Entries

Impact: A signed-in user can finish a scan while Supabase session lookup is slow. History then treats the user as anonymous, writes the completed scan to the shared legacy guest key, skips Supabase sync, and later signed-in history reads do not merge that legacy key. The result is a scan that looked successful but disappears from the signed-in history list, especially on slow networks or cold auth state.

Evidence:
- `getCurrentUserId()` races `supabase.auth.getSession()` against a 3-second timeout and returns `null` on timeout or auth errors: `services/history.js:11`, `services/history.js:14`, `services/history.js:15`, `services/history.js:16`, `services/history.js:19`, `services/history.js:20`, `services/history.js:21`, `services/history.js:23`, and `services/history.js:28`.
- `getStorageKey(null)` maps that timeout path to the shared anonymous `@woof/scan_history` key: `services/history.js:4`, `services/history.js:5`, `services/history.js:32`, `services/history.js:33`, and `services/history.js:34`.
- Completed analyses call `addHistoryEntry(...)` without passing the known app auth state or user id, so history must redo the session lookup at save time: `services/analysisService.js:823`, `services/analysisService.js:844`, `services/analysisService.js:849`, and `services/analysisService.js:855`.
- `addHistoryEntry(...)` writes locally using the timed-out `userId` and only syncs to Supabase when `userId` is truthy: `services/history.js:177`, `services/history.js:179`, `services/history.js:180`, `services/history.js:185`, `services/history.js:186`, `services/history.js:190`, and `services/history.js:191`.
- Later signed-in history reads prefer Supabase and merge only the user-specific local key, not the anonymous legacy key: `services/history.js:124`, `services/history.js:125`, `services/history.js:132`, `services/history.js:146`, `services/history.js:147`, `services/history.js:148`, and `services/history.js:151`.
- The legacy key is only checked inside `migrateLocalHistoryToSupabase(...)` on sign-in, and that migration can return early after the per-user migration flag is set: `services/history.js:236`, `services/history.js:240`, `services/history.js:241`, `services/history.js:242`, `services/history.js:243`, `services/history.js:246`, and `services/history.js:248`.

Fix:
- Do not downgrade signed-in history writes to anonymous storage on an auth lookup timeout. Return an explicit `unknown` state and retry/queue the save.
- Pass the current auth user id/session from `AuthProvider` or analysis context into history writes instead of calling `getSession()` again after analysis completes.
- When signed-in history loads, detect and reconcile stray legacy entries before hiding them.
- Replace the one-time migration flag with idempotent per-entry merging, so timeout-created anonymous entries can still be recovered.
- Add a regression test where `getSession()` exceeds 3 seconds during `addHistoryEntry()`, then verify the scan appears in signed-in local and Supabase history after auth recovers.

## Forty-Ninth-Pass History Visibility Finding

### 104. "Show All" History Only Shows 10 Of 50 Stored Entries

Impact: The history service keeps up to 50 scans and the paywall sells "Full scan history & sync", but the Home screen's "Show all" toggle renders only the first 10 entries. A paying or heavy free user can see "Show all (37)", tap it, and still lose access to entries 11-37 from the UI. That creates a support/trust problem around a paid feature before marketing.

Evidence:
- The history service stores and fetches up to `MAX_ENTRIES = 50`: `services/history.js:7`, `services/history.js:139`, `services/history.js:153`, `services/history.js:185`, and `services/history.js:186`.
- Home renders history with `history.slice(0, showAllHistory ? 10 : 3)`, so expanded mode is hard-capped at 10 visible rows: `screens/HomeScreen.js:858`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:861`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:862`.
- The toggle appears whenever `history.length > 3` and labels itself with the full count, for example `Show all (${history.length})`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:876`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:890`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:891`.
- The paywall feature list promises "Full scan history & sync": `screens/PaywallScreen.js:40`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:41`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:42`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:43`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:44`.
- The public privacy page says scan history is retained as long as the user has an active account, so hiding most retained rows in the main UI weakens that promise: `docs/privacy.html:100` and `docs/privacy.html:115`.

Fix:
- Either render all loaded history entries when expanded, or add a dedicated paginated history screen.
- Make the collapsed/expanded copy truthful, for example "Show 10 recent" if the cap is intentional.
- Align the paywall feature wording with the actual UI depth, or make the UI support the promised full history.
- Add a UI test with more than 10 history rows verifying entries 11-50 are reachable.

## Fifty-First-Pass Conversion Timing Finding

### 105. Post-Scan Upsell Can Miss The Second-Scan Trigger

Impact: The Results screen intends to show a one-time upgrade prompt after a free user's second scan, but the prompt effect can read the old quota count before the async scan-count increment updates context. Because that effect does not depend on `remainingScans` or `scanCount`, it may never re-run after the count changes. A user can finish their second scan and see no intended conversion prompt, then only meet the prompt condition on a later scan or not at all if the free gate blocks the next scan first.

Evidence:
- The scan-counting effect fires when `done` is true, marks `scanCounted`, and calls `incrementScanCount()` without awaiting it: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:470`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:482`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:484`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:485`.
- `incrementScanCount()` is async for signed-in users, waits on the Supabase RPC, then updates `scanCount` after the server response; guest fallback also updates state through React's async setter path: `services/auth.js:207`, `services/auth.js:212`, `services/auth.js:215`, `services/auth.js:216`, `services/auth.js:226`, and `services/auth.js:227`.
- The post-scan prompt effect runs independently on `done`, computes `scansUsed = 3 - remainingScans()`, and returns if the pre-increment count still looks like fewer than 2 scans: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:511`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:512`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:514`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:515`.
- That effect's dependency list omits `remainingScans`, `scanCounted`, and any explicit count value, so the intended second-scan prompt does not re-evaluate when AuthContext publishes the updated quota: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:519`, `services/auth.js:240`, `services/auth.js:242`, and `services/auth.js:243`.
- The component comment says the prompt is "shown once after 2nd scan for free users", but the implementation timing does not guarantee that behavior: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:332`.

Fix:
- Make quota increment return the new count, await it in Results, and drive the post-scan prompt from that committed count.
- Or subscribe the prompt effect to an explicit `scanCount` / `remainingScans` value and guard it with `scanCounted` so it re-evaluates after the increment lands.
- Store the prompt-dismiss flag only when the user dismisses or opens the paywall, not when the prompt was skipped by timing.
- Add a test that completes the first, second, and third free scans and verifies the prompt appears exactly at the intended scan count.

## Fifty-Second-Pass Search State Finding

### 106. Stale Search Results Stay Tappable During A New Query

Impact: When a user edits a search query, Home starts the new debounced RPC but leaves the previous result rows visible and tappable until the new query returns. In a store with weak cellular service, a shopper can type a new product, see the old list still on screen under the new input, tap a stale row, and navigate to analysis for the wrong product. If the stale row also trips the existing database-contract mismatch, this can look like the searched product "is not in the database anymore" even though the tap actually used an older result.

Evidence:
- `handleSearch(text)` updates `searchQuery`, aborts the previous request, and starts loading for any query with at least two characters, but it does not clear `searchResults` at the beginning of the new search: `screens/HomeScreen.js:283`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:284`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:285`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:287`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:296`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:297`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:299`.
- The component only clears `searchResults` when the query drops below two characters or when `clearSearch()` runs: `screens/HomeScreen.js:289`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:290`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:358`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:361`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:362`.
- Search result rows render whenever `searchResults.length > 0`; rendering is not gated by `!searchLoading`, by the query that produced the rows, or by a result-query token: `screens/HomeScreen.js:667`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:668`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:670`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:673`.
- A tap on any visible row immediately snapshots that stale item, records it as a recent search, clears the current input, and navigates to Results with the old `productName`, `brand`, and `cacheKey`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:374`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:379`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:382`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:383`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:389`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:393`.
- On RPC/network error, the catch block only logs and the finally block clears loading; it does not clear stale rows or show an error state, so the old list can remain after a failed new search: `screens/HomeScreen.js:321`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:323`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:324`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:325`.

Fix:
- Clear `searchResults` or mark them as stale as soon as the query changes to a new two-plus-character value.
- Store the query/sequence that produced each result set and render/tap rows only when it matches the current input.
- On search RPC errors, show a search-specific retry/error state and disable stale rows instead of leaving old results active.
- Add a UI test that searches one product, edits to a different query under delayed/failing RPC, and verifies old rows are not tappable.

## Fifty-Third-Pass Release Packaging Finding

### 107. Onboarding Depends On Untracked Image Assets

Impact: The first-run onboarding flow now requires local PNG assets from `assets/onboarding`, but that directory is currently untracked. A local dev build can work because the files exist on this machine, while a clean clone, CI job, or EAS build from committed sources can fail module resolution or ship without the intended onboarding visuals. This is a release-readiness risk before marketing because onboarding is the first screen many acquired users see.

Evidence:
- `OnboardingScreen` statically imports three onboarding images with `require(...)`: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:35`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:37`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:38`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:39`.
- Those assets are rendered in the first-run scan and safety pages: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:155`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:160`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:259`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:283`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:293`.
- The app imports and can render onboarding before Home when the onboarding key is not complete: `App.js:12`, `App.js:150`, `App.js:199`, and `App.js:205`.
- Current git state shows the code files modified but the image directory untracked: `git status --short` reports `M App.js`, `M screens/OnboardingScreen.js`, and `?? assets/onboarding/`.
- The asset directory contains files needed by those imports, but because they are untracked they are not guaranteed to exist in another checkout or build context: `assets/onboarding/scan-bag.png`, `assets/onboarding/safety-grapes.png`, and `assets/onboarding/safety-banana.png`.

Fix:
- Commit every required onboarding asset or replace the static image imports with assets that are already tracked.
- Add a release check that runs a clean-tree install/export from tracked files only.
- Add an asset-reference check that fails when app code imports files not present in git.
- Keep large/generated design assets out of the app unless they are intentionally optimized and tracked for release.

## Fifty-Fourth-Pass Offline Runtime Finding

### 108. Supabase Failures Do Not Feed The Offline Detector

Impact: The app has a root offline banner and scanner preflight, but the network state is only updated by selected direct `fetch` wrappers. Core Supabase-backed surfaces such as Home search, history sync, product-data lookup, and analysis-cache lookup can fail repeatedly on weak cellular without calling `reportNetworkError()`. In a store aisle, the app can therefore keep showing online UI while search/history/cache requests are failing, delaying the user's recovery path and weakening the low-signal behavior the launch gate needs to prove.

Evidence:
- The offline detector flips offline only after `reportNetworkError(err)` records three network/timeout-class errors in 30 seconds: `services/network.js:37`, `services/network.js:41`, `services/network.js:42`, `services/network.js:43`, `services/network.js:45`, `services/network.js:47`, and `services/network.js:49`.
- Only `claude.js` and `opff.js` import and call `reportNetworkError` / `reportNetworkSuccess`; broad repo search found no equivalent import in `HomeScreen`, `history.js`, `cache.js`, or `auth.js`: `services/claude.js:4`, `services/opff.js:2`, `services/opff.js:129`, `services/opff.js:133`, `services/claude.js:861`, and `services/claude.js:863`.
- Home search catches Supabase RPC failures, logs them, and clears loading, but does not report the network error into `NetworkProvider`: `screens/HomeScreen.js:305`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:306`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:321`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:323`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:325`.
- Home history loading catches `getHistory()` / timeout failures, sets `historyError`, and clears data, but also does not report the failure to the offline detector: `screens/HomeScreen.js:408`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:415`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:416`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:417`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:420`.
- History and cache Supabase reads swallow or log failures and fall back locally without updating network state: `services/history.js:107`, `services/history.js:119`, `services/history.js:134`, `services/history.js:162`, `services/cache.js:155`, `services/cache.js:171`, `services/cache.js:312`, and `services/cache.js:343`.
- The root offline banner depends entirely on `useNetwork().isOnline`, so these unreported failures do not surface in the global offline UI: `App.js:216`, `App.js:219`, `App.js:230`, `App.js:231`, and `App.js:233`.

Fix:
- Route all Supabase client calls through a small wrapper that calls `reportNetworkError()` on network/timeout failures and `reportNetworkSuccess()` on successful round trips.
- At minimum, wire reporting into Home search, history load/sync, product-data lookup, analysis-cache lookup, auth refresh/profile reads, and purchase/offering fetches.
- Distinguish server/RLS/business errors from true network failures so the offline banner does not mask real backend bugs.
- Add an airplane-mode and poor-cellular test where repeated Supabase search/history failures flip the global offline UI and block new network-required actions.

## Fifty-Fifth-Pass Edge CORS Finding

### 109. Analyze Edge Function Allows Paid-AI Calls From Any Browser Origin

Impact: The main analysis edge function fronts Anthropic/OpenAI work and accepts guest traffic, but its CORS policy allows any website to call it from a browser. The Supabase anon key is necessarily public in the mobile bundle, so wildcard CORS makes it easier for a third-party webpage, ad landing page, copied snippet, or malicious site to drive browser-origin requests against the paid AI endpoint. This compounds the existing helper-mode and fail-open rate-limit findings because abuse does not need to run through the Woof app.

Evidence:
- The `analyze` function sets `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: "*"` and allows `Authorization` / `apikey` headers: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:3`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:4`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:5`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:6`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:7`.
- The function handles browser preflight by returning those headers for `OPTIONS`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:953`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:955`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:956`.
- The React Native client calls the same public edge-function URL with the public anon key in headers: `services/claude.js:3`, `services/claude.js:6`, `services/claude.js:30`, `services/claude.js:31`, and `services/claude.js:32`.
- The endpoint supports paid or sensitive AI modes including `photo`, `verified`, `human_food`, `identify`, `ingredients_lookup`, and `ocr_ingredients`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1027`, `services/claude.js:481`, `services/claude.js:523`, `services/claude.js:723`, `services/claude.js:736`, and `services/claude.js:740`.
- Anonymous requests are intentionally allowed for non-helper modes, and helper modes skip anonymous IP rate limiting entirely in a separate finding: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:963`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1034`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1035`.
- `product-lookup` has a similar wildcard CORS surface already noted in the ScrapingBee abuse finding, so the paid lookup and paid analysis endpoints share the same browser-origin exposure pattern: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:3` and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:4`.

Fix:
- Restrict browser CORS origins to the owned web/support domains that genuinely need browser access, and omit CORS entirely for mobile-only endpoints where possible.
- Require a short-lived server-issued scan/session token for paid AI modes instead of trusting only public anon-key access.
- Apply rate limits before expensive helper modes, even for browser-origin requests.
- Add an edge-function abuse test that attempts cross-origin browser calls to `analyze` and verifies untrusted origins cannot reach paid AI work.

## Fifty-Sixth-Pass Analysis Lifecycle Finding

### 110. Rekeyed Analysis Errors Schedule Cleanup Under The Wrong Key

Impact: Several analysis flows start under a temporary key and then rekey to a normalized product key after identification or search setup. If one of those rekeyed flows later times out or throws through a catch block that still reports the original temporary key, the Results screen can receive the visible error, but cleanup is scheduled against a key that no longer owns the analysis entry. The canonical entry and alias can then remain in memory for the rest of the app session, making repeat scans, retries, diagnostics, and long in-store sessions less predictable.

Evidence:
- `startAnalysis(...)` stores non-barcode work under a generated temp id, then `_runSearch`, `_runPhotoWithIngredients`, and `_runPhoto` can call `_rekey(tempId, realCacheKey, state)`: `services/analysisService.js:183`, `services/analysisService.js:184`, `services/analysisService.js:210`, `services/analysisService.js:322`, `services/analysisService.js:323`, `services/analysisService.js:499`, `services/analysisService.js:500`, `services/analysisService.js:620`, and `services/analysisService.js:621`.
- `_rekey(...)` deletes the old temp map entry, records `tempId -> realCacheKey`, and stores the same state under the new key: `services/analysisService.js:84`, `services/analysisService.js:86`, `services/analysisService.js:87`, `services/analysisService.js:89`, and `services/analysisService.js:90`.
- `_scheduleCleanup(key)` only looks up and deletes `analyses.get(key)` for the key it was given, and only removes aliases whose target equals that same key: `services/analysisService.js:62`, `services/analysisService.js:66`, `services/analysisService.js:68`, `services/analysisService.js:69`, `services/analysisService.js:70`, `services/analysisService.js:73`, and `services/analysisService.js:74`.
- The hard timeout wrapper is launched with the original temp id for search/photo modes and schedules cleanup under that stale key if the timeout fires after rekeying: `services/analysisService.js:219`, `services/analysisService.js:220`, `services/analysisService.js:221`, `services/analysisService.js:229`, `services/analysisService.js:230`, `services/analysisService.js:231`, `services/analysisService.js:234`, `services/analysisService.js:235`, `services/analysisService.js:236`, `services/analysisService.js:107`, `services/analysisService.js:111`, and `services/analysisService.js:112`.
- Rekeyed catch blocks also notify and schedule cleanup with `tempId` instead of the canonical `notifyKey`: `services/analysisService.js:440`, `services/analysisService.js:443`, `services/analysisService.js:444`, `services/analysisService.js:445`, `services/analysisService.js:564`, `services/analysisService.js:567`, `services/analysisService.js:568`, `services/analysisService.js:569`, `services/analysisService.js:760`, `services/analysisService.js:763`, `services/analysisService.js:764`, and `services/analysisService.js:765`.
- The Results subscriber resolves aliases before matching events, so this can still produce a user-visible error while the service cleanup misses the canonical entry: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:381`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:382`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:383`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:384`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:414`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:415`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:416`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:417`.

Fix:
- Make cleanup canonical-key aware: resolve aliases inside `_scheduleCleanup`, delete both the requested key and resolved key, and remove aliases where either side references the cleaned entry.
- Store the canonical key on state after `_rekey(...)`, and have `_withTimeout(...)` call cleanup/notify with the current canonical key rather than the launch key.
- In catch blocks after rekeying, notify and schedule cleanup with `notifyKey` or `resolveKey(tempId)`.
- Add service-level tests for search, photo, and photo-with-ingredients failures after rekeying that assert `analyses`, `keyAliases`, and `scheduledCleanups` are empty after TTL cleanup.

## Fifty-Seventh-Pass First-Run Persistence Finding

### 111. Onboarding Completion Can Be Lost When Storage Writes Fail

Impact: A fresh user can complete or skip onboarding, enter Home, and still have the app fail to persist that onboarding completion. On the next cold start, the same user can be shown onboarding again even though they already dismissed it, or the app can fall back to inconsistent skip behavior if the onboarding read also fails. That is not a catastrophic crash, but it is a paid-acquisition polish issue: repeated onboarding, unreliable replay state, and silent local-storage failures make first-run instrumentation and consent/version tracking less trustworthy.

Evidence:
- App startup decides whether to show onboarding by reading `@woof_onboarding_complete` and checking whether the value equals `"true"`: `App.js:152`, `App.js:163`, `App.js:164`, `App.js:168`, and `App.js:169`.
- The skip path writes `ONBOARDING_KEY` with `.catch(() => {})` and calls `onComplete()` immediately, so a write failure still transitions to Home with no user-visible error and no retry: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:390`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:391`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:392`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:393`.
- The final "Get Started" path awaits `AsyncStorage.setItem(...).catch(() => {})`; because the catch swallows the error, `onComplete()` still runs after a failed write: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:396`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:400`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:401`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:402`.
- The root completion handler only hides onboarding in memory; it does not verify persistence or keep a pending state until storage succeeds: `App.js:180`, `App.js:181`, and `App.js:182`.
- If the next startup storage read succeeds but returns no completion key, onboarding is shown again; if that read times out or rejects, the app skips onboarding through a different fallback path already noted in the guest-consent finding: `App.js:156`, `App.js:159`, `App.js:160`, `App.js:161`, `App.js:171`, `App.js:175`, and `App.js:176`.

Fix:
- Treat onboarding completion as a persisted transition: write first, verify success, then call `onComplete()`.
- On write failure, show a small retryable error or keep a session-only completion flag while logging the persistence failure to telemetry.
- If legal acceptance is added to onboarding, persist a versioned legal acceptance key separately and never swallow that write silently.
- Add a cold-start regression test that completes onboarding with a mocked AsyncStorage write failure, restarts the app, and verifies the intended recovery behavior.

## Fifty-Eighth-Pass RevenueCat Readiness Finding

### 112. Guest Paywall Can Query RevenueCat Before SDK Initialization Finishes

Impact: A new guest user can hit a free-scan limit or tap an upgrade prompt immediately after cold start, but guest purchase initialization is intentionally fire-and-forget. The paywall then calls `getOfferings()` directly, and the purchase service calls RevenueCat APIs without ensuring `Purchases.configure(...)` has completed. That creates a first-session race where products can appear unavailable, restore can fail, or the paywall can fall into the hardcoded-price state even though the App Store / RevenueCat configuration is healthy. This is a direct conversion risk under paid acquisition because the fastest upgrade attempts come from fresh installs.

Evidence:
- For guests, auth startup calls `initializePurchases(null)` without awaiting it, with a comment that guest users should not pay for purchase SDK init on cold start: `services/auth.js:292`, `services/auth.js:293`, and `services/auth.js:294`.
- `initializePurchases(...)` sets the module-level `initialized` flag only after `Purchases.configure(...)` resolves: `services/purchases.js:10`, `services/purchases.js:12`, `services/purchases.js:15`, `services/purchases.js:20`, and `services/purchases.js:22`.
- `getOfferings()` does not call or await `initializePurchases(...)`; it immediately calls `Purchases.getOfferings()` and returns `null` on any error: `services/purchases.js:45`, `services/purchases.js:47`, `services/purchases.js:48`, `services/purchases.js:49`, and `services/purchases.js:50`.
- Paywall mount calls `getOfferings().then(...)` directly and stores the result, with no SDK-ready state or retry around initialization: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:133`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:135`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:136`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:137`.
- Purchase and restore paths also call RevenueCat APIs directly through `purchasePackage(...)` / `restorePurchases(...)`, which likewise do not ensure initialization before `Purchases.purchasePackage(...)` or `Purchases.restoreTransactions()`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:172`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:193`, `services/purchases.js:86`, `services/purchases.js:88`, `services/purchases.js:111`, and `services/purchases.js:113`.
- When offerings are `null`, the paywall falls into the already-documented fallback-price/unavailable-product behavior instead of distinguishing "SDK still initializing" from real store misconfiguration: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:149`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:150`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:151`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:163`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:165`.

Fix:
- Centralize RevenueCat readiness in `services/purchases.js`: expose an `ensurePurchasesInitialized(userId)` promise and await it before offerings, purchase, restore, or customer-info calls.
- For guest startup, either await a bounded initialization before showing paywall-capable UI, or let Paywall own the initialization/loading/retry state explicitly.
- Distinguish SDK-not-ready, offering-load, store-unavailable, and no-products states in the Paywall UI and telemetry.
- Add a cold-start test where a guest opens Paywall before `initializePurchases(null)` resolves and verify offerings eventually load without showing fake purchasable prices or a "Not Available" alert.

## Fifty-Ninth-Pass Edge Request-Size Finding

### 113. Analyze Edge Function Parses Oversized Bodies Before Enforcing Image Limits

Impact: The `analyze` edge function has image-size checks, but they run only after `await req.json()` has parsed the full request body. Anonymous helper modes also skip IP rate limiting, and anonymous paid modes run their IP check only after body parsing because the code needs to know the mode. A large JSON body can therefore consume edge memory/CPU before the app rejects it as too large or rate-limited. During marketing traffic, this weakens abuse resistance and can also turn accidental oversized camera uploads into slower, more expensive failures instead of immediate `413` responses.

Evidence:
- The function defines `MAX_IMAGE_B64_LENGTH = 7_000_000` and returns `413` when `imageBase64` exceeds that field limit: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:12`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1148`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1149`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1150`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1152`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1178`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1179`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1229`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1262`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1284`.
- Those checks happen after the full body is parsed with `body = await req.json()`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1009`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1011`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1012`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1013`.
- The code comment explicitly says anonymous IP rate limiting and free-user scan limits are applied after body parsing because the mode is needed: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1007`.
- Anonymous helper modes `identify`, `ingredients_lookup`, and `ocr_ingredients` skip the general anonymous IP limiter entirely, so their oversized requests still reach body parsing before mode-specific validation rejects them: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1027`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1034`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1035`.
- The mobile scanner creates base64 JPEG payloads for the edge function after image manipulation, but server-side protection cannot rely only on client sizing: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:241`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:244`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:248`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:39`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:42`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:44`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:47`.
- `product-lookup` has the same full-body parsing pattern and validates only a minimum product-name length afterward; it has no explicit request-body or product-name maximum before parse: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1105`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1107`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1108`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1109`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1114`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1116`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1117`.

Fix:
- Reject requests with missing or excessive `Content-Length` before calling `req.json()`, returning `413` for bodies above the real edge-function limit.
- Enforce a streaming/manual body read cap if `Content-Length` is absent or untrusted.
- Apply a cheap pre-parse anonymous IP/session check before JSON parsing for public endpoints, then apply mode-specific quota after parsing.
- Add max-length validation for `productName`, `brand`, and `searchTerms` in `product-lookup`.
- Add abuse tests that send oversized JSON and oversized base64 strings to `analyze` and `product-lookup` and verify they are rejected before vendor calls or expensive parsing.

## Sixtieth-Pass Native Permission Copy Finding

### 114. Camera Permission Copy Does Not Cover Front-Package And Human-Food Photos

Impact: iOS and Android camera permission prompts should accurately explain why the app wants camera access. The native strings say Woof needs the camera to scan pet food ingredient labels, but the current primary scanner asks for the front of the package first, and the same camera screen is reused for human-food safety photos. That mismatch can hurt user trust, privacy review consistency, and App Review/Play data-safety defensibility because the permission prompt under-describes the actual camera use cases.

Evidence:
- The iOS `NSCameraUsageDescription` says camera access is needed to scan pet food ingredient labels: `app.json:26`, `app.json:27`, and `app.json:28`.
- The Expo camera plugin permission string uses the same ingredient-label-only wording: `app.json:55`, `app.json:56`, `app.json:57`, and `app.json:58`.
- The in-app camera permission screen repeats the same copy: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:279`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:286`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:289`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:290`.
- The primary pet-food scanner instructs users to capture the front of the bag, including brand, product name, and flavor, not an ingredient label: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:266`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:268`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:269`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:397`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:398`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:399`.
- The same scanner route is used for human-food photo checks, where `mode: "human_food"` routes a food photo into Results: `screens/HomeScreen.js:485`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:492`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:105`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:106`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:247`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:250`.
- Ingredient-label capture is still a real secondary use case, but it is not the only camera use: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:44`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:45`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:46`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:47`.

Fix:
- Rewrite native and in-app camera permission copy to cover all production camera uses: pet-food package identification, optional ingredient-label capture, and human-food safety photos.
- Keep the copy concise enough for OS prompts, for example: "Woof uses the camera to identify pet food packages, read ingredient labels, and check food photos."
- Re-run generated iOS/Android config and verify the real native permission strings before store submission.
- Include camera permission copy in the privacy/App Store data-map review whenever scan or human-food behavior changes.

## Sixty-First-Pass Ingredient Fallback Error Finding

### 115. OCR-Fallback Analysis Errors Can Leave Results Spinning

Impact: The database-miss recovery flow can fail without a terminal user-visible state. If the user chooses the ingredient-label path or "Use AI estimate instead", `_runPhotoWithIngredients` first tries OCR and then falls back to photo-only analysis when OCR fails. That fallback only completes when the returned analysis has no `error`; if the fallback returns an error object, the function simply returns while the analysis state remains `"running"`. Because `_withTimeout` sees the function resolve, it clears the global timeout, so Results can keep showing a loading state instead of a retryable error.

Evidence:
- `_runPhotoWithIngredients` rekeys the temp entry and leaves the state initialized as `"running"` from `startAnalysis`: `services/analysisService.js:198`, `services/analysisService.js:199`, `services/analysisService.js:228`, `services/analysisService.js:230`, `services/analysisService.js:499`, and `services/analysisService.js:500`.
- The OCR-failure branch calls photo-only analysis and only handles the success case: `services/analysisService.js:510`, `services/analysisService.js:511`, `services/analysisService.js:512`, `services/analysisService.js:515`, `services/analysisService.js:517`, `services/analysisService.js:518`, `services/analysisService.js:521`, `services/analysisService.js:524`, and `services/analysisService.js:527`.
- Other analysis branches explicitly treat `analysis.error` as a terminal error and notify Results, which shows the missing branch is inconsistent: `services/analysisService.js:284`, `services/analysisService.js:287`, `services/analysisService.js:289`, `services/analysisService.js:404`, `services/analysisService.js:426`, `services/analysisService.js:546`, `services/analysisService.js:559`, and `services/analysisService.js:561`.
- Results only exits loading on service `complete`, `need_ingredient_photo`, or `error` events; the dropped fallback-error branch emits none of those events: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:395`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:402`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:414`.
- The hard timeout wrapper clears its timeout after the analysis promise resolves, so it will not later rescue this silent return: `services/analysisService.js:98`, `services/analysisService.js:104`, `services/analysisService.js:105`, `services/analysisService.js:116`, and `services/analysisService.js:117`.

Fix:
- In the OCR-failure fallback branch, handle `!analysis || analysis.error` exactly like the other branches: clear stale partial results, set `state.error`, set `state.status = "error"`, notify with `notifyKey`, and schedule cleanup with the canonical key.
- Add a regression test where OCR fails and photo-only fallback returns `{ error: "..." }`, then verify Results shows `ErrorState` and the analysis maps clean up.
- Fold this into the explicit `photo_estimate` path from finding 64 so estimate, OCR recovery, and fallback analysis share one terminal-state helper.

## Sixty-Second-Pass Search Cancellation Finding

### 116. Cleared Search Can Resurrect Old Results

Impact: A shopper can clear or cancel search, return to the home/search surface, and then see old product rows reappear from the request they already dismissed. That is a different trust break from stale rows staying visible during a new query: here the user explicitly cleared the UI, but a late Supabase response can repopulate results and make the next tap look like Woof ignored the user's current intent.

Evidence:
- Home protects normal query changes with `searchSeqRef`, incrementing it only when a two-plus-character search starts: `screens/HomeScreen.js:281`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:298`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:309`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:310`.
- The success path still writes returned rows whenever the captured sequence equals the current sequence: `screens/HomeScreen.js:312`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:313`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:314`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:325`.
- `clearSearch()` aborts the current controller, clears the timer, input, rows, empty state, and loading flag, but it never increments `searchSeqRef` or otherwise invalidates the already-captured sequence token: `screens/HomeScreen.js:358`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:359`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:360`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:361`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:362`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:363`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:364`.
- Both the Cancel button and search-result tap call `clearSearch()`, so this can happen after a user cancels search or after a navigation event races with a just-completed request: `screens/HomeScreen.js:367`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:368`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:383`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:389`.
- Search rows render from `searchResults.length > 0` without checking whether the input is still non-empty or whether the result set belongs to the current query: `screens/HomeScreen.js:667`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:668`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:670`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:673`.

Fix:
- Increment `searchSeqRef.current` inside `clearSearch()` before aborting/clearing so every late completion becomes stale.
- Store the query string that produced each result set and render rows only when it still matches `searchQuery.trim()`.
- Null out `searchAbortRef.current` after abort/completion to avoid aborting an already-finished request on the next clear.
- Add a UI regression test where a search request resolves after Clear/Cancel and verifies the old rows do not reappear.

## Sixty-Third-Pass Barcode Contract Finding

### 117. Barcode Miss Events Are Dropped By Results

Impact: Barcode is the obvious fix for slow store scanning, but the current service/UI event contract is incomplete. If the unreachable barcode path is exposed without fixing this, a UPC/EAN that OPFF does not know can emit `barcode_not_found` from the analysis service while Results keeps showing the loading skeleton. That would turn the speed path into another "stuck scan" for exactly the products that need a fallback to photo or ingredient-label capture.

Evidence:
- `startAnalysis(...)` already routes `mode === "barcode"` into `_runBarcode(...)`: `services/analysisService.js:161`, `services/analysisService.js:162`, `services/analysisService.js:183`, `services/analysisService.js:212`, and `services/analysisService.js:214`.
- `_runBarcode(...)` treats an OPFF miss as a non-error state, sets `state.status = "not_found"`, emits `type: "barcode_not_found"`, schedules cleanup, and returns: `services/analysisService.js:261`, `services/analysisService.js:262`, `services/analysisService.js:265`, `services/analysisService.js:266`, `services/analysisService.js:267`, and `services/analysisService.js:268`.
- Results subscribes to analysis events but handles only `phase`, `update`, `complete`, `need_ingredient_photo`, and `error`; there is no branch for `barcode_not_found`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:386`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:392`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:395`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:402`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:414`.
- The loading branch exits only when `result`, `error`, `done`, or `needsLabel` changes; the dropped barcode miss event changes none of those Results states: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:652`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:655`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:687`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:713`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:720`.
- Barcode is currently not reachable from the scanner UI, but the audit roadmap already calls it out as the fastest store-scan path, so this event contract needs to be fixed before that path is exposed: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:319`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:322`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:323`, and `AUDIT_2026-06-05.md:737`.

Fix:
- Handle `barcode_not_found` in Results by stopping loading and offering the next best action: scan the front package, capture the ingredient label, or search by name.
- Or collapse barcode misses into a normal `error`/`need_ingredient_photo` event with a clear reason and retry/fallback action.
- Add a barcode-mode contract test for OPFF hit, OPFF miss, OPFF timeout, and analysis error before exposing barcode in the scanner.

## Sixty-Fourth-Pass Barcode Failure Classification Finding

### 118. Barcode Network Failures Are Misclassified As Product Misses

Impact: Even after the barcode path is exposed and the missing Results event is handled, weak store connectivity can still produce the wrong user-facing outcome. `lookupBarcode(...)` collapses OPFF timeouts, fetch failures, non-OK HTTP responses, and true catalog misses into the same `{ found: false }` shape. `_runBarcode(...)` then treats every one of those as `barcode_not_found`. A temporary OPFF outage or poor cellular connection can therefore look like "this barcode is not in the catalog" instead of a retryable network problem or offline state.

Evidence:
- `lookupBarcode(...)` sets a 4-second abort timeout around the OPFF request: `services/opff.js:97`, `services/opff.js:98`, `services/opff.js:99`, `services/opff.js:102`, `services/opff.js:103`, and `services/opff.js:105`.
- A non-OK OPFF response returns `{ found: false }` for every status, not only real not-found cases; only `404` is treated specially for caching: `services/opff.js:108`, `services/opff.js:109`, `services/opff.js:111`, `services/opff.js:112`, and `services/opff.js:113`.
- OPFF responses with `status === 0` also return the same `{ found: false }` shape: `services/opff.js:118`, `services/opff.js:119`, `services/opff.js:120`, `services/opff.js:121`, and `services/opff.js:122`.
- Fetch errors and timeout aborts are reported to the network detector, but the function still returns `{ found: false }` instead of a typed network/timeout failure: `services/opff.js:131`, `services/opff.js:132`, `services/opff.js:133`, and `services/opff.js:134`.
- `_runBarcode(...)` checks only `lookup.found`; every false result becomes `state.status = "not_found"` and emits `barcode_not_found`: `services/analysisService.js:261`, `services/analysisService.js:262`, `services/analysisService.js:265`, `services/analysisService.js:266`, and `services/analysisService.js:267`.

Fix:
- Return a discriminated result from OPFF lookup, for example `{ found: false, reason: "not_found" }`, `{ found: false, reason: "timeout" }`, and `{ found: false, reason: "network" }`.
- Treat true OPFF misses as a fast fallback to photo/search/label capture, but treat network/timeout failures as retryable or offline-specific errors.
- Report HTTP 5xx and other transient OPFF failures into the same network telemetry path instead of only returning a miss.
- Add barcode-mode tests that verify timeout and HTTP 500 do not show the same copy/actions as a real 404/catalog miss.

## Sixty-Fifth-Pass Release Packaging Finding

### 119. The Offline Network Service Is Imported But Untracked

Impact: The app now depends on a local `services/network.js` module for the root offline banner, scanner preflight, OPFF reporting, and Claude fetch reporting, but that source file is not tracked in git. A local developer session can work because the file exists on this machine, while a clean clone, CI job, or EAS build from committed sources can fail module resolution for `./services/network`. That makes offline behavior and even app startup/build reproducibility unsafe before marketing.

Evidence:
- `App.js` imports `NetworkProvider` and `useNetwork` from `./services/network`, then wraps the app shell in `NetworkProvider` and renders the offline banner from `useNetwork()`: `App.js:10`, `App.js:216`, `App.js:221`, and `App.js:231`.
- `ScannerScreen` imports `useNetwork` and blocks capture based on `isOnline`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:32`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:113`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:208`.
- The AI and OPFF service layers import the same module for network telemetry: `services/claude.js:4`, `services/opff.js:2`, `services/opff.js:129`, `services/opff.js:133`, `services/claude.js:861`, and `services/claude.js:863`.
- Current git state shows those importing files modified but `services/network.js` untracked: `git status --short -- services/network.js App.js screens/ScannerScreen.js services/claude.js services/opff.js` reports `M App.js`, `M screens/ScannerScreen.js`, `M services/claude.js`, `M services/opff.js`, and `?? services/network.js`.
- `git ls-files -- services/network.js` returns no tracked path, so a build based only on committed files would not include the module.

Fix:
- Commit `services/network.js` with the same change set that introduced the imports, or remove the imports and offline banner until the service is ready.
- Add a clean-clone/EAS export check to the release gate so untracked required source files fail before submission.
- Extend the existing untracked-asset release checklist to include source modules, not only image assets.

## Sixty-Sixth-Pass Release Packaging Finding

### 120. The Shared Error Classifier Is Imported But Untracked

Impact: The app now depends on `services/errors.js` for user-facing Results recovery copy and for the offline detector's network/timeout classification, but that module is also untracked. A local build can work while a clean clone or EAS build from committed sources fails to resolve `../../services/errors` or `./errors`. This is a release-blocking packaging risk because it sits on the core failure path: scan/search errors, quota errors, auth recovery, and offline transitions.

Evidence:
- `ResultsScreen/components.js` imports `classifyError` from `../../services/errors` and calls it inside `ErrorState`: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:27`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2757`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2760`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2762`.
- `services/network.js` imports the same classifier to decide whether fetch failures should count as network/timeout failures: `services/network.js:3`, `services/network.js:41`, `services/network.js:42`, and `services/network.js:43`.
- The module defines shared classification behavior for network, timeout, auth, quota, rate-limit, image, server, and unknown errors: `services/errors.js:1`, `services/errors.js:9`, `services/errors.js:22`, `services/errors.js:32`, `services/errors.js:38`, `services/errors.js:46`, `services/errors.js:52`, `services/errors.js:59`, `services/errors.js:67`, and `services/errors.js:83`.
- Current git state shows the importing Results component modified and `services/errors.js` untracked: `git status --short -- services/errors.js screens/ResultsScreen/components.js services/network.js` reports `M screens/ResultsScreen/components.js`, `?? services/errors.js`, and `?? services/network.js`.
- `git ls-files -- services/errors.js` returns no tracked path, so committed-source builds would not include the classifier module.

Fix:
- Commit `services/errors.js` with the error-state and network changes, or remove/revert the imports until the module is part of the tracked app.
- Add a clean-clone export/build gate that fails on any import target missing from tracked files.
- Add a small error-classifier unit test because this module now controls quota, auth, network, timeout, and image recovery copy.

## Sixty-Seventh-Pass Backend Release Contract Finding

### 121. Current Backend Contracts Depend On Untracked Supabase Files

Impact: The app's current search, product lookup, human-food quota, and history-image behavior depends on Supabase functions/migrations that are present locally but not tracked in git. If another machine, CI, or production deployment uses only committed sources, the mobile app can build while the backend it expects is missing `product-lookup`, `search_products`, human-food quota columns/RPCs, or `scan_history.product_image_url`. That creates exactly the kind of "works locally, fails in production" risk that marketing traffic will expose.

Evidence:
- `services/claude.js` constructs and calls `/functions/v1/product-lookup`: `services/claude.js:6`, `services/claude.js:7`, `services/claude.js:835`, `services/claude.js:855`, and `services/claude.js:858`.
- The corresponding local edge function directory is untracked: `git status --short -- supabase/functions/product-lookup` reports `?? supabase/functions/product-lookup/`, while `git ls-files -- supabase/functions/product-lookup` returns no tracked path.
- Home search calls the `search_products` RPC that is defined by the untracked smart-search migration: `screens/HomeScreen.js:303`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:305`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:306`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:1`, `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:7`, and `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:28`.
- Auth calls the human-food quota RPC defined by an untracked migration: `services/auth.js:172`, `services/auth.js:175`, `services/auth.js:176`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:1`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:7`, and `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:13`.
