- History enrichment expects `product_data.image_url` and synced history expects `scan_history.product_image_url`, both backed by untracked newer migrations: `services/history.js:100`, `services/history.js:107`, `services/history.js:108`, `supabase/migrations/022_history_image_url.sql:1`, `supabase/migrations/022_history_image_url.sql:3`, and `supabase/migrations/022_history_image_url.sql:4`.
- Current git state shows these required backend files untracked: `git status --short -- supabase/functions/product-lookup supabase/migrations/007_product_data.sql supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql supabase/migrations/022_history_image_url.sql` reports all of them as `??`.

Fix:
- Commit the Supabase function and every migration required by the current app contract, or remove the app calls until the backend is intentionally shipped.
- Add a backend contract gate that runs migrations from a clean checkout and verifies the required RPCs, tables, columns, and edge functions exist.
- Add a release checklist step that deploys/stages `analyze`, `product-lookup`, and migrations together with the app build, then runs smoke tests for search, product lookup, quota, and history-image sync.

## Sixty-Eighth-Pass Startup Configuration Finding

### 122. Missing Supabase Env Can Crash Before The Error Boundary Exists

Impact: Missing Supabase configuration is not just a broken-network state. The app defaults missing `SUPABASE_URL` and `SUPABASE_ANON_KEY` to empty strings, then creates the Supabase client at module import time. The installed Supabase client throws synchronously when either value is empty, which can crash the JavaScript bundle before `App` renders and before the root `ErrorBoundary` can show a recovery screen. A misconfigured EAS build can therefore open to a native redbox/crash instead of a controlled "configuration missing" state.

Evidence:
- `config/env.js` falls back to empty strings when Expo `extra` does not contain Supabase values: `config/env.js:1`, `config/env.js:3`, `config/env.js:4`, `config/env.js:6`, and `config/env.js:7`.
- `services/supabase.js` calls `createClient(SUPABASE_URL, SUPABASE_ANON_KEY, ...)` at module top level: `services/supabase.js:1`, `services/supabase.js:3`, and `services/supabase.js:5`.
- A local Node check against the installed `@supabase/supabase-js` package showed `createClient("", "")` throws `supabaseUrl is required.`, and `createClient("https://example.supabase.co", "")` throws `supabaseKey is required.`.
- `App.js` imports `AuthProvider` from `./services/auth` at module top level, and `services/auth.js` imports the Supabase client, so this failure happens during import/evaluation before the exported `App` component can render: `App.js:1`, `App.js:9`, `services/auth.js:7`, `services/supabase.js:5`.
- The root `ErrorBoundary` is instantiated only inside the rendered `App` tree, after module import has already succeeded: `App.js:22`, `App.js:147`, `App.js:201`, `App.js:213`, and `App.js:224`.
- The broader missing-env build risk is already present because `app.config.js` reads env vars directly without validation: `app.config.js:3`, `app.config.js:5`, `app.config.js:7`, and `app.config.js:8`.

Fix:
- Fail production builds in `app.config.js` when required `extra` values are missing, instead of shipping empty strings.
- Add a small runtime config validator that throws a clearly named configuration error only after the app can render a controlled fatal-configuration screen.
- Avoid top-level client construction with unchecked env values; lazily create the client after validation or export a guarded accessor.
- Add a release smoke test that runs `expo config --json` for every EAS profile and asserts Supabase URL/key and platform RevenueCat keys are non-empty.

## Sixty-Ninth-Pass Ingredient Recovery Route Contract Finding

### 123. Ingredient-Recovery Analysis Accepts Missing Image Context

Impact: The ingredient-label recovery path can start a background analysis with missing front-photo or product context instead of failing fast. This is reachable from stale navigation state, a bad deep link, or any future route reuse of `IngredientCapture`. In that case, the app can call OCR with an undefined ingredient image, fall through to photo analysis with an undefined front image, or send incomplete product names into the recovery flow. That turns a malformed recovery route into slow vendor calls and confusing Results behavior instead of a clear "scan again" state.

Evidence:
- `IngredientCaptureScreen` defensively reads `route.params || {}`, but it does not validate that `productName`, `base64`, or the original `uri` exist before rendering capture/skip actions: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:11`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:12`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:14`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:21`.
- The label-capture path always navigates to Results with `mode: "photo_with_ingredients"` and forwards the possibly missing front-photo `base64`, `productName`, `brand`, `petType`, and `uri`: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:44`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:45`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:46`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:47`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:48`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:49`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:51`.
- The skip/estimate path also navigates to `photo_with_ingredients` with no `ingredientBase64`, and likewise does not guard that the original front-photo `base64` exists: `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:59`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:63`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:64`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:65`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:66`.
- `startAnalysis(...)` validates missing inputs for `barcode`, `photo`, `human_food`, and `search`, but has no equivalent guard for `mode === "photo_with_ingredients"`: `services/analysisService.js:161`, `services/analysisService.js:162`, `services/analysisService.js:166`, `services/analysisService.js:170`, `services/analysisService.js:174`, `services/analysisService.js:178`, and `services/analysisService.js:228`.
- `_runPhotoWithIngredients(...)` immediately calls `ocrIngredients(ingredientBase64, productName, ...)`, and if OCR fails it falls back to `analyzeIngredients(base64, ...)`; with missing route context, either or both image arguments can be undefined: `services/analysisService.js:497`, `services/analysisService.js:503`, `services/analysisService.js:506`, `services/analysisService.js:510`, and `services/analysisService.js:515`.
- Results only shows `"Could not start analysis."` when `startAnalysis(...)` returns null, but this invalid `photo_with_ingredients` input currently does not return null: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:358`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:345`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:346`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:348`.

Fix:
- Add `photo_with_ingredients` validation in `startAnalysis(...)`: require enough context for the selected branch, and return null with a typed reason when inputs are missing.
- In `IngredientCaptureScreen`, render a recovery error with "Scan again" when required route params are absent.
- Split the explicit estimate path from the ingredient-label path so the service can validate different required inputs for `label_ocr` versus `photo_estimate`.
- Add route-contract tests for malformed `IngredientCapture` and malformed `photo_with_ingredients` Results params.

## Seventieth-Pass Clean-Checkout Route Finding

### 124. Ingredient Capture Screen Is Imported But Untracked

Impact: A clean checkout can fail before the core scan recovery route even loads. `App.js` imports and registers `IngredientCaptureScreen`, but `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js` is present only as an untracked local file. That means the current workspace can pass manual testing while CI, another developer machine, or an EAS build from committed sources cannot resolve the route module. Because this screen is the recovery path for incomplete package-photo analysis, losing it would directly worsen the slow/failed scan experience the app is trying to fix.

Evidence:
- `App.js` imports the screen at module top level: `App.js:20`.
- The navigation stack registers `IngredientCapture` with `IngredientCaptureScreen`: `App.js:141`.
- Git shows the screen is not tracked: `git status --short -- App.js screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js` reports `?? screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js`.
- `git ls-files -- screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js` returns no tracked path, while `git ls-files -- App.js` returns `App.js`.
- This is separate from the untracked service modules and backend contracts because it is a route component needed by the visible scan flow, not only a helper import or Supabase deployment artifact.

Fix:
- Commit `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js` with the route, or remove the `App.js` import and stack registration until the screen is intentionally shipped.
- Add a clean-checkout import-resolution gate that fails if any registered screen, service, asset, or backend contract is missing from tracked sources.
- Include `IngredientCapture` in the scan recovery smoke test so CI proves the route exists and can be opened from package-photo analysis.

## Seventy-First-Pass History Durability Finding

### 125. Signed-In History Sync Is Blocked By Local Storage Failure

Impact: A signed-in user can complete a scan and still lose the account history row if the local AsyncStorage write fails. The history service claims it always writes locally and then syncs to Supabase, but the remote write is placed after `await saveLocalHistory(...)` inside the same try block. If local storage is full, corrupted, or temporarily unavailable, the catch logs the failure and the Supabase upsert never starts. For a paid feature marketed around synced scan history, the remote account copy should not depend on a successful device-local cache write.

Evidence:
- Completed analyses save history through `_saveHistory(...)`: `services/analysisService.js:823`, `services/analysisService.js:844`, and `services/analysisService.js:855`.
- `_saveHistory(...)` calls `addHistoryEntry(...)` without `await`, so the analysis completion path does not observe whether history persistence succeeded: `services/analysisService.js:842`, `services/analysisService.js:844`, and `services/analysisService.js:856`.
- `addHistoryEntry(...)` resolves the current user, builds the new entry, and then awaits `saveLocalHistory(updated, userId)` before starting any Supabase sync: `services/history.js:177`, `services/history.js:179`, `services/history.js:180`, `services/history.js:185`, and `services/history.js:186`.
- The remote sync is nested after that local write and only begins if the earlier await succeeded: `services/history.js:190`, `services/history.js:191`, `services/history.js:192`, `services/history.js:193`, and `services/history.js:194`.
- The outer catch logs `"[HISTORY] Error saving entry:"` and returns without retrying remote sync or surfacing a user-visible warning: `services/history.js:200` and `services/history.js:201`.
- Duplicate suppression is set before the async save starts, so a failed persistence attempt can also suppress a quick retry for the same cache key: `services/analysisService.js:834`, `services/analysisService.js:835`, `services/analysisService.js:836`, and `services/analysisService.js:840`.

Fix:
- Decouple local cache persistence from account sync: for signed-in users, attempt the Supabase insert/upsert even if AsyncStorage fails.
- Return a structured result from `addHistoryEntry(...)` and await it from `_saveHistory(...)`, or queue failed local/remote saves for retry with a visible sync status.
- Move duplicate suppression after a successful persistence result, or clear the suppression marker when both local and remote saves fail.
- Add tests for signed-in history save with mocked AsyncStorage failure and mocked Supabase failure, verifying each store can succeed independently and failures are observable.

## Seventy-Second-Pass Account Recovery State Finding

### 126. Successful Account Deletion Leaves Profile Delete State Stuck

Impact: After a successful account deletion, the Profile screen can keep its local `deleting` state set to true. The UI hides the delete section because the auth state becomes guest, but the component can stay mounted. If the user signs into another account from that same Profile screen, the authenticated delete section returns with the button disabled and the spinner text still showing `"Deleting..."`. That is a trust and App Review risk around a sensitive account-control flow, especially because users testing deletion and re-sign-in are likely to revisit the same screen.

Evidence:
- The destructive confirmation sets `deleting` to true before calling `deleteAccount()`: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:99`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:101`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:103`.
- The catch path resets `deleting` and `deleteFlowOpenRef`, but there is no success-path reset after `await deleteAccount()`: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:104`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:105`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:106`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:109`.
- `deleteAccount()` clears auth state locally by setting `user` and `profile` to null, then signs out: `services/auth.js:452`, `services/auth.js:459`, `services/auth.js:460`, `services/auth.js:461`, and `services/auth.js:466`.
- Profile renders a guest sign-in prompt when `isGuest` becomes true, so the same mounted screen can navigate to Auth for a new sign-in: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:147`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:148`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:168`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:171`.
- The delete section is shown again for authenticated users but disables the button whenever the stale `deleting` state is true: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:511`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:512`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:517`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:519`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:524`.

Fix:
- Reset `deleting` and `deleteFlowOpenRef` in a `finally` block, or unmount/navigate away from Profile after successful deletion.
- Add an auth-state effect that clears destructive-action local state whenever the user id changes or becomes null.
- Add an account QA case: delete account, remain on Profile, sign in as a new account, and verify Delete Account is enabled and not stuck in a loading state.

## Seventy-Third-Pass Scan Image Orientation Finding

### 127. Scanner Skips Orientation Correction Before Vision Analysis

Impact: The scanner optimized capture speed by setting `skipProcessing: true`, but the app immediately resizes and sends that image to product identification / vision analysis. Expo's SDK 55 camera docs say photos are rotated to match device orientation only when `skipProcessing` is not enabled, and that `skipProcessing: true` returns the camera-native image orientation. On real store devices, especially if the user tilts the phone to fit a bag, the AI can receive a sideways or upside-down package image. That can directly increase "could not read product name," slow fallback steps, and "not in database" outcomes that are actually orientation failures.

Evidence:
- Scanner captures with `skipProcessing: true`, `quality: 1`, `base64: false`, and `exif: false`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:226`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:228`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:229`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:230`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:231`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:232`.
- The next step resizes the file and asks ImageManipulator for base64, but does not inspect EXIF orientation, camera orientation, dimensions, or rotate the image explicitly: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:241`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:242`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:243`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:244`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:245`.
- Results receives that base64 as the canonical analysis input for pet-food photo scans and human-food photo checks: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:247`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:248`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:250`.
- Expo SDK 55 camera documentation states that `takePictureAsync` rotates photos to match device orientation only if `options.skipProcessing` is not enabled, and the `skipProcessing` option skips orientation adjustment and may produce wrong orientation: `https://docs.expo.dev/versions/v55.0.0/sdk/camera/`.
- Because `exif: false` is used, downstream code has no orientation metadata to recover from a camera-native rotated file: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:232`.

Fix:
- Benchmark real-device capture with `skipProcessing: false` versus the current path; keep speed only if orientation remains correct across iPhone and Android devices.
- If `skipProcessing` stays enabled, request/read orientation metadata or use a deterministic native/image-manipulator rotation step before creating the base64 payload.
- Add real-device fixtures for portrait, landscape-left, landscape-right, and upside-down capture, and verify the vision input reaches identification in the expected orientation.
- Track identification failure rates by device/orientation so speed optimizations do not silently reduce first-pass scan accuracy.

## Seventy-Fourth-Pass Camera Readiness Finding

### 128. Scanner Can Capture Before The Camera Is Ready

Impact: The scanner renders an enabled capture button as soon as the camera screen appears, but it never tracks the camera-ready lifecycle before calling `takePictureAsync`. Expo's camera docs state that callers should wait for the camera-ready callback before taking a picture. On slower phones, first launch after permission, or app-resume in a store, a fast user tap can hit a not-yet-ready camera and produce a generic "Capture Failed" alert. That is a bad first-scan experience and can look like scan unreliability rather than a recoverable readiness state.

Evidence:
- Scanner keeps only `cameraRef` and `capturing` state; there is no `cameraReady` state or readiness ref: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:108`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:109`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:110`.
- `CameraView` is rendered without an `onCameraReady` handler: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:318`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:319`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:320`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:321`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:322`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:323`.
- `handleCapture(...)` allows capture whenever `cameraRef.current` exists and `capturing` is false; it does not check readiness: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:204`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:205`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:217`.
- The capture button is disabled only while `capturing`, not while the camera preview is initializing: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:403`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:404`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:405`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:412`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:413`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:414`.
- Expo SDK 55 camera documentation notes that callers should wait for the `onCameraReady` callback before calling `takePictureAsync`: `https://docs.expo.dev/versions/v55.0.0/sdk/camera/`.
- Any readiness failure falls into the generic catch and shows only `"Something went wrong. Please try again."`, so the user gets no explanation or short automatic retry: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:252`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:253`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:254`.

Fix:
- Add `cameraReady` state from `CameraView.onCameraReady` and disable/hide the capture control until true.
- Reset `cameraReady` when the screen loses focus or camera unmounts, then re-enable only after the next readiness callback.
- Show a short "Camera starting..." state instead of letting early taps produce a failure alert.
- Add a real-device QA case for first scan after permission grant, cold camera mount, app resume, and quick tap immediately after Scanner opens.

## Seventy-Fifth-Pass Scanner Interaction Layer Finding

### 129. Scanner Cancel Control Is Rendered Under A Touch-Disabled Parent

Impact: During capture/compression, the UI shows a Cancel control inside the processing card, but the card is rendered under a parent `View` with `pointerEvents="none"`. In React Native, that setting prevents the parent and its children from becoming touch targets. The result is worse than the existing cancellation-pipeline bug: the user may not be able to tap Cancel at all while the app appears to offer it. In a store aisle, this makes a slow scan feel frozen and undermines the recovery path the UI promises.

Evidence:
- `ProcessingCard` renders a `TouchableOpacity` Cancel button wired to `onCancel`: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:48`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:55`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:57`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:62`.
- That `ProcessingCard` is rendered inside the scan frame only while `capturing` is true: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:340`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:341`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:348`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:349`.
- The scan-frame parent has `pointerEvents="none"`, so its children are not intended to receive touch events: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:341`.
- The only cancel handler is `handleCancelCapture(...)`, which means this touch path is the user's only visible way to stop processing on the scanner screen: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:261`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:262`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:263`.
- The existing scanner-cancel finding covers the missing async cancellation guard after a tap; this finding is separate because the rendered control itself can be unreachable before the handler ever runs.

Fix:
- Move `ProcessingCard` outside the `pointerEvents="none"` frame overlay, or set the non-interactive corner layer to `pointerEvents="none"` while keeping the processing card touchable.
- Add an automated or manual interaction test that taps Scanner Cancel during capture and verifies `handleCancelCapture(...)` fires.
- Pair this with the cancellation-session fix so a successful tap both registers and prevents late Results navigation.

## Seventy-Sixth-Pass Scanner Back Navigation Finding

### 130. Scanner Back Can Leave Then Still Push Results

Impact: While capture/compression is running, the scanner keeps the top back button active. If a user sees a slow scan and taps back instead of the processing-card Cancel control, the async capture pipeline continues and still calls `navigation.push("Results", ...)` when compression finishes. That can pull the user into Results after they intentionally left the scanner and can start AI analysis work from a stale capture. This is a direct in-store reliability issue because users naturally back out when a scan feels stuck.

Evidence:
- `handleCapture(...)` starts the async native capture/manipulation pipeline and only guards `cameraRef.current` plus `capturing` at the beginning: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:204`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:205`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:217`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:228`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:241`.
- After compression, the pipeline unconditionally pushes Results with the captured base64 payload: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:247`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:248`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:249`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:250`.
- The top back button remains rendered and active during capture; its handler always calls `navigation.goBack()` and does not mark the capture session canceled: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:367`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:369`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:370`, and `screens/ScannerScreen.js:371`.
- Scanner has no mounted/canceled ref analogous to Results' mounted guard, so the async completion path has no way to know the screen was left before pushing Results: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:108`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:204`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:246`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:231`.
- This is separate from the visible Cancel-control findings because it uses the always-visible top navigation path, not the processing-card cancel button.

Fix:
- Disable or convert the top back button to the same cancel-session path while `capturing` is true.
- Track a capture session id plus mounted/canceled ref, and check it after every async step before calling `navigation.push(...)`.
- Add a QA case: tap capture, immediately tap the scanner back button, and verify no Results screen opens and no analysis starts after compression finishes.

## Seventy-Seventh-Pass Streaming Completion Contract Finding

### 131. Truncated Streams Can Be Saved As Completed Analyses

Impact: A first-time streamed analysis can be cut off, parsed as partial JSON, and then treated by the client analysis service as a successful completed result. Results has a UI guard that can later show an interruption error when `overallScore` is missing, but by then the service may already have written the malformed object to local result cache and scan history. That means a flaky store connection can leave behind broken history rows or local cache entries from an analysis the user saw as failed/interrupted.

Evidence:
- `_callStreaming(...)` falls back from strict `JSON.parse` to `parsePartialJson(...)` when the final streamed text is incomplete: `services/claude.js:413`, `services/claude.js:416`, `services/claude.js:417`, `services/claude.js:418`, `services/claude.js:424`, and `services/claude.js:425`.
- After the partial parse, it only checks that the result is an object; it does not require `overallScore`, `productName`, ingredients, verdict fields, or any mode-specific schema before returning success: `services/claude.js:432`, `services/claude.js:433`, `services/claude.js:436`, and `services/claude.js:439`.
- Search-mode verified analysis treats any returned object without `analysis.error` as complete, then saves it locally, saves history, and emits `complete`: `services/analysisService.js:404`, `services/analysisService.js:407`, `services/analysisService.js:409`, `services/analysisService.js:411`, `services/analysisService.js:415`, and `services/analysisService.js:416`.
- Photo-mode verified analysis follows the same pattern: `services/analysisService.js:714`, `services/analysisService.js:717`, `services/analysisService.js:720`, `services/analysisService.js:722`, `services/analysisService.js:723`, `services/analysisService.js:727`, and `services/analysisService.js:728`.
- Results detects the broken completed state and renders an interruption error only after `done && result.overallScore == null`, which does not undo the earlier local cache/history writes: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:713`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:719`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:720`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:738`.
- The server-side streaming cache path validates with `isValidAnalysis(...)` before writing to Supabase, so the missing guard is specifically on the client-side streamed completion/local-history path: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1602`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1604`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1605`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1606`.

Fix:
- Treat final streaming strict-parse failure as a failed analysis unless the partial object passes the same mode-specific validation required by the server cache path.
- Add a shared client validator before `_saveLocalResult(...)`, `_saveHistory(...)`, and `complete` notifications for pet-food and human-food analyses.
- If a stream is incomplete, emit an `error` event and avoid writing history/local cache; let the user retry or choose the ingredient-label fallback.
- Add a regression test that feeds a truncated SSE payload missing `overallScore` and verifies no local result, history row, or complete event is produced.

## Seventy-Eighth-Pass Paywall In-Flight State Finding

### 132. Paywall Can Be Dismissed While Purchase Or Restore Is In Flight

Impact: The paywall disables the subscribe and restore controls while purchase/restore is running, but the close button remains active. A user can dismiss the paywall while `Purchases.purchasePackage(...)` or `restoreTransactions()` is still in flight. When the async call later resolves, the Paywall component still calls state setters, `refreshProStatus()`, alerts, and `navigation.goBack()` from a screen the user already left. That can pop the wrong screen, show purchase/restore alerts out of context, or make a successful purchase feel like it disappeared.

Evidence:
- Paywall tracks `purchasing`, `restoring`, and combines them into `isLoading`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:97`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:99`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:100`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:155`.
- The purchase CTA is disabled while `isLoading` is true: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:355`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:356`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:359`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:362`.
- The Restore Purchases button is also disabled while `isLoading` is true: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:410`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:411`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:412`.
- The close button remains enabled and always calls `handleDismiss`, which immediately calls `navigation.goBack()`: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:224`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:225`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:226`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:207`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:208`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:209`.
- `handlePurchase(...)` resumes after `await purchasePackage(...)`, resets state, refreshes Pro status, and calls `navigation.goBack()` on success: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:172`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:173`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:174`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:176`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:178`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:180`.
- `handleRestore(...)` has the same pattern after `await restorePurchases()`: it resets state, refreshes, navigates back on success, or shows alerts on failure/no purchases: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:193`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:194`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:196`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:197`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:199`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:201`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:203`.

Fix:
- Disable or hide the close button while purchase/restore is in flight, or confirm that leaving will not cancel/lose the transaction state.
- Add a mounted/in-flight guard so late purchase/restore callbacks cannot update state or navigate from an unmounted Paywall.
- On success after a user-initiated dismiss, update entitlement centrally and show success in the current screen context instead of blindly calling `navigation.goBack()`.
- Add a paywall interaction test: start purchase/restore, tap close immediately, then resolve success/failure and verify navigation, alerts, and entitlement state remain coherent.

## Seventy-Ninth-Pass Catalog Write Integrity Finding

### 133. User OCR Upserts Can Downgrade Existing Product Data

Impact: When the ingredient-label fallback succeeds, the app writes the OCR result into the shared `product_data` catalog using the same cache key as future search and scan lookups. The `save_product_data` conflict handler then overwrites the existing ingredient list, ingredient text, ingredient count, and source unconditionally. A single bad OCR capture or malformed user contribution can replace a better catalog row, making future users see weaker search data, a lower ingredient count, or a row that `search_products` can still display but `getProductData` rejects for analysis.

Evidence:
- The OCR fallback saves every successful ingredient-label capture back into shared product data with source `user_ocr`: `services/analysisService.js:532`, `services/analysisService.js:533`, and `services/analysisService.js:534`.
- `saveProductData(...)` derives a shared cache key from brand plus product name and calls the public `save_product_data` RPC with the OCR ingredient list, text, count, and source: `services/cache.js:270`, `services/cache.js:271`, `services/cache.js:275`, `services/cache.js:279`, `services/cache.js:280`, `services/cache.js:281`, and `services/cache.js:282`.
- The `save_product_data` RPC handles `ON CONFLICT (cache_key)` by replacing `ingredients`, `ingredient_text`, `ingredient_count`, and `source` with the incoming OCR values without checking provenance, length, plausibility, or whether the existing row was better: `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:23`, `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:25`, `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:26`, `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:27`, `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:28`, and `supabase/migrations/012_fix_save_product_data.sql:29`.
- The newer nutrient-panel upsert already uses a safer merge pattern, preserving the longer ingredient list/text and the greatest ingredient count, which shows the current OCR save path is less defensive than another product-data writer in the same repo: `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:87`, `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:88`, `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:92`, `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:93`, and `supabase/migrations/018_nutrient_panel.sql:97`.
- Search exposes rows at `ingredient_count >= 3`, while analysis lookup requires at least five ingredients, so a downgrade to three or four OCR tokens can become another visible-search-then-not-found path: `supabase/migrations/021_smart_search.sql:64`, `services/cache.js:164`, `services/cache.js:186`, and `services/analysisService.js:332`.

Fix:
- Change `save_product_data` conflict handling to preserve higher-provenance rows and only accept user OCR over an existing row when it passes plausibility checks and improves completeness.
- Store user OCR contributions in a pending/contribution table with provenance, owner/session, and review/quality state instead of writing directly into the canonical search catalog.
- Require the same minimum analysis-ready ingredient threshold in user contribution writes as in `getProductData`, or mark lower-count rows as not searchable.
- Add a regression test that seeds a good catalog row, submits a weaker OCR row with the same cache key, and verifies search/analysis still use the good row.

## Eightieth-Pass Guest Human-Food Quota Finding

### 134. Guest Human-Food Reset Copy Can Disagree With Server Enforcement

Impact: The app tells free users the human-food safety check "resets tomorrow" and the signed-in quota code uses a UTC-day bucket, but the anonymous edge-function guard uses a rolling 24-hour IP rate-limit window. A guest who uses the free check late in the UTC day can see local app copy/state imply the next day's check is available, then have the server reject the request until 24 hours after the previous one. That turns a safety-check feature into inconsistent paywall/error behavior for exactly the guest users marketing will bring in first.

Evidence:
- The Home safety modal tells free users the exhausted safety check "Resets tomorrow": `screens/HomeScreen.js:929`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:930`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:931`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:932`.
- The client human-food quota mirror stores a UTC `YYYY-MM-DD` and resets when the stored date differs from today's UTC date: `services/auth.js:21`, `services/auth.js:22`, `services/auth.js:23`, `services/auth.js:41`, `services/auth.js:42`, `services/auth.js:152`, `services/auth.js:158`, and `services/auth.js:163`.
- The signed-in database quota migration is also explicitly documented as one check per UTC day, with `today DATE := (NOW() AT TIME ZONE 'UTC')::DATE`: `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:1`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:3`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:11`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:19`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:24`, and `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:25`.
- Anonymous human-food enforcement does not use that UTC-day bucket. It calls `check_ip_rate_limit` with `p_ip_address: "hf:${clientIp}"`, `p_max_requests: 1`, and `p_window_minutes: 24 * 60`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1105`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1107`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1114`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1115`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1116`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1117`.
- `check_ip_rate_limit(...)` stores `window_start`, resets only when `window_start < NOW() - interval`, and otherwise denies once `request_count >= p_max_requests`, so this is a rolling window, not a calendar-day reset: `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:5`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:8`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:31`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:44`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:45`, `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:53`, and `supabase/migrations/008_ip_rate_limits.sql:54`.

Fix:
- Make guest human-food quota use the same UTC-day semantics as signed-in users, keyed by a stable anonymous/session/device token or by an IP-plus-date row when no token exists.
- If a rolling 24-hour IP cap is intentional, change all guest-facing copy to say when the next check unlocks and return `retryAfter` from the edge function.
- Move anonymous human-food quota checks after basic input validation and before vendor calls, and make client/server quota responses share one error code.
- Add QA for guest text and photo human-food checks across UTC midnight and across retry/error cases.

## Eighty-First-Pass Quota Hardening Finding

### 135. Dev Quota Reset Helpers Are Exported Without Their Own Production Guard

Impact: The Profile UI hides quota reset controls behind the development flag, but the AuthContext reset helpers themselves do not enforce that same guard. They are exported in the production context and directly update `profiles.scan_count`, `profiles.human_food_count`, and `profiles.human_food_count_date` for the current user. This compounds the existing quota-column write risk: a future screen, stale test hook, or modified client can call a "dev-only" helper path that the implementation does not actually restrict to dev builds.

Evidence:
- `services/auth.js` comments that the dev-only helpers are "exposed unconditionally but only do anything in DEV_MODE": `services/auth.js:414` and `services/auth.js:415`.
- `resetScanCount(...)` does not check `DEV_MODE`; it sets local scan count to zero and updates the signed-in profile row to `scan_count: 0`: `services/auth.js:424`, `services/auth.js:425`, `services/auth.js:426`, `services/auth.js:427`, `services/auth.js:428`, and `services/auth.js:429`.
- `resetHumanFoodQuota(...)` also does not check `DEV_MODE`; it clears local human-food quota state and updates the signed-in profile row to reset server quota fields: `services/auth.js:434`, `services/auth.js:435`, `services/auth.js:436`, `services/auth.js:437`, `services/auth.js:438`, `services/auth.js:439`, `services/auth.js:440`, and `services/auth.js:441`.
- AuthContext exports `resetScanCount` and `resetHumanFoodQuota` even when `isDev` is false: `services/auth.js:493`, `services/auth.js:494`, `services/auth.js:497`, and `services/auth.js:498`.
- The current Profile UI only renders the controls when `isDev` is true, so the issue is the missing guard in the callable helpers, not the visible screen condition: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:362` and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:363`.

Fix:
- Add an explicit `if (!DEV_MODE) return` guard inside every dev/test helper, including `resetScanCount(...)` and `resetHumanFoodQuota(...)`.
- Do not export dev/test helpers from production AuthContext values, or export no-op functions that log a blocked development-only call.
- Move quota resets behind a service-role-only admin tool or local test harness, not a client production bundle path.
- Add a production-build test that asserts dev helpers are not present or cannot mutate quota when `__DEV__` is false.

## Eighty-Second-Pass Root Recovery Finding

### 136. Root Error Recovery CTA Uses A Missing Color Token

Impact: The root ErrorBoundary is the last-resort recovery UI when a render-time crash happens after the JavaScript bundle has loaded. Its primary recovery button uses `Colors.bg` for text color, but the exported top-level `Colors` object does not define `bg`. React Native will ignore the missing color value, so the button text can fall back to the platform default while the button background is `Colors.textPrimary` dark. In practice, "Try Again" / "Reset App" can become low-contrast or unreadable exactly when a new user needs the recovery action after a crash.

Evidence:
- The ErrorBoundary renders the fallback screen and recovery button after `hasError` is set: `App.js:22`, `App.js:25`, `App.js:48`, and `App.js:49`.
- The fallback container and CTA text both reference `Colors.bg`: `App.js:52` and `App.js:76`.
- The CTA background is `Colors.textPrimary`, a dark color in the top-level palette: `App.js:70` and `theme.js:17`.
- The top-level palette defines `background`, `card`, `surface`, and text colors, but no top-level `bg` token: `theme.js:9`, `theme.js:11`, `theme.js:12`, `theme.js:13`, `theme.js:17`, `theme.js:18`, and `theme.js:19`.
- `bg` exists only inside the nested `Colors.light` and `Colors.dark` palettes, not as `Colors.bg`: `theme.js:59`, `theme.js:60`, `theme.js:61`, `theme.js:73`, `theme.js:74`, and `theme.js:75`.
- The ErrorBoundary wraps both onboarding and the main app trees, so this fallback is meant to be user-facing recovery, not only a developer redbox replacement: `App.js:201`, `App.js:208`, `App.js:213`, and `App.js:224`.

Fix:
- Replace `Colors.bg` in the ErrorBoundary with a real token, for example `Colors.background` for the container and `Colors.buttonText` for the CTA text.
- Prefer rendering a small themed fallback component that uses the same `useTheme()` fallback behavior as other out-of-provider components.
- Add a forced-render-error QA case or lightweight component test that verifies the ErrorBoundary fallback has readable text and a working retry/reset action.

## Eighty-Third-Pass Apple Sign-In Finding

### 137. Apple Sign-In Button Is Shown Without Runtime Availability Gating

Impact: The auth screen renders a primary "Continue with Apple" path on every iOS runtime, but the implementation never checks whether Expo Apple Authentication is available before showing or launching it. Expo exposes `AppleAuthentication.isAvailableAsync()` for this exact runtime gate and documents that Apple auth UI should only be attempted after it resolves true. On unsupported iOS-like environments, future Mac/Vision exposure, simulator/device configuration gaps, or a missing native module, users can see a first-class auth button that fails only after tap. That is a conversion issue for sign-in, restore, sync, and account-deletion flows before marketing.

Evidence:
- `AuthScreen` calls `signInWithApple()` directly from the Apple handler: `screens/AuthScreen.js:83`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:84`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:85`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:86`, and `screens/AuthScreen.js:87`.
- The screen renders the Apple auth button whenever `Platform.OS === "ios"` and does not track any `AppleAuthentication.isAvailableAsync()` state: `screens/AuthScreen.js:152`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:153`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:154`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:158`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:159`, `screens/AuthScreen.js:162`, and `screens/AuthScreen.js:163`.
- `signInWithApple()` calls `AppleAuthentication.signInAsync(...)` directly after nonce generation, with no service-level availability check or typed unavailable error first: `services/auth.js:349`, `services/auth.js:350`, `services/auth.js:360`, `services/auth.js:361`, `services/auth.js:362`, `services/auth.js:363`, `services/auth.js:364`, `services/auth.js:365`, and `services/auth.js:366`.
- The installed Expo Apple Authentication package exposes the availability gate and returns false when the native module cannot support the current runtime: `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:17`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:18`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:20`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:21`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:22`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:23`, and `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthentication.ts:24`.
- The package's Apple button documentation says to only attempt rendering Apple Authentication UI when `AppleAuthentication.isAvailableAsync()` resolves true: `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthenticationButton.tsx:5`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthenticationButton.tsx:6`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthenticationButton.tsx:7`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthenticationButton.tsx:11`, `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthenticationButton.tsx:12`, and `node_modules/expo-apple-authentication/src/AppleAuthenticationButton.tsx:13`.

Fix:
- On AuthScreen mount, call `AppleAuthentication.isAvailableAsync()` and hide or disable the Apple auth option when it returns false.
- Add a service-level guard inside `signInWithApple()` that throws a typed `APPLE_SIGN_IN_UNAVAILABLE` error before launching the native flow.
- Provide a visible fallback path, such as Google or guest continue, anywhere Apple auth is unavailable.
- Add device/simulator/platform QA for Apple auth availability, cancel, success, unavailable native module, and fallback behavior.

## Eighty-Fourth-Pass Cache Prewarm Finding

### 138. Negative Analysis Prewarm Entries Can Hide Fresh Shared Cache Hits

Impact: The search prewarm layer stores "known miss" entries in memory for five minutes. During that window, `getCachedAnalysis(...)` returns the warm miss without rechecking Supabase. If another device, another user, or a late edge-function write creates a valid shared `analysis_cache` row immediately after this device prewarmed the miss, the current device will still treat the row as uncached and may run a paid analysis again. That undermines the intended instant-search path for popular products and creates avoidable AI spend under marketing traffic.

Evidence:
- Home prewarms visible search result rows by their `cache_key` values after each successful search response: `screens/HomeScreen.js:312`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:313`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:315`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:316`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:317`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:318`.
- The warm cache has a five-minute TTL: `services/cache.js:290`, `services/cache.js:292`, and `services/cache.js:293`.
- `prefetchAnalyses(...)` explicitly stores `{ hit: false }` for stale-rubric rows and for every requested key that was not returned by Supabase: `services/cache.js:320`, `services/cache.js:321`, `services/cache.js:322`, `services/cache.js:327`, `services/cache.js:328`, `services/cache.js:339`, and `services/cache.js:340`.
- `getCachedAnalysis(...)` treats any fresh warm entry as authoritative and returns it without falling through to `_getCachedAnalysisFromDb(...)`: `services/cache.js:353`, `services/cache.js:355`, `services/cache.js:356`, `services/cache.js:357`, `services/cache.js:358`, `services/cache.js:359`, and `services/cache.js:363`.
- Search and photo flows check `getCachedAnalysis(sharedCacheKey)` before deciding to run verified analysis, so a warm negative result can skip a fresh shared Supabase hit and proceed toward local-cache fallback or paid analysis: `services/analysisService.js:341`, `services/analysisService.js:342`, `services/analysisService.js:343`, `services/analysisService.js:656`, `services/analysisService.js:657`, and `services/analysisService.js:658`.
- Verified analysis calls pass the shared cache key to the edge function, and the edge function upserts successful results into `analysis_cache`, so fresh rows can appear after an earlier prewarm miss: `services/claude.js:537`, `services/claude.js:540`, `services/claude.js:542`, `services/analysisService.js:401`, `services/analysisService.js:714`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:928`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:929`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:930`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:932`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:941`.

Fix:
- Do not store negative prewarm results for the same TTL as positive hits. Either avoid negative entries entirely or give them a very short TTL such as 5 to 10 seconds.
- When a caller is about to run paid analysis, bypass or revalidate warm misses with a direct Supabase check.
- Invalidate any warm miss for a key after local analysis starts, after a local result save, and after any edge-function response that may have written the shared cache.
- Add a cache-race test: prewarm a miss, create the `analysis_cache` row, then tap the product and verify the app reads the fresh shared cache instead of starting a new analysis.

## Eighty-Fifth-Pass Product Lookup Provenance Finding

### 139. Product-Lookup Cache Hits Erase Source Provenance

Impact: The product-lookup edge function returns the real source on a fresh scrape or OPFF lookup, then writes that same source into `product_data`. On a later cache hit for the same row, the function replaces that provenance with `source: "cache"`. Any caller that uses the lookup service sees different trust metadata based only on whether the row was fresh or cached, and the Results badge treats `"cache"` as generic verified database data. That can hide whether ingredients came from OPFF, Dog Food Advisor, Cat Food Advisor, Cats.com, Amazon/Chewy/web scraping, or another source, undermining source transparency and making cache behavior materially different from the first lookup.

Evidence:
- `ProductResult.source` is the response field used to identify where a lookup result came from, and `SiteConfig.sourceName` is documented as the source name used in results: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:130`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:131`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:132`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:151`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:155`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:156`.
- Fresh product-lookup results persist the scraped or catalog source into `product_data.source`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1238`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1240`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1249`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1250`.
- The fresh response returns the original `best.source`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1262`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1264`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1265`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1266`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1273`.
- The cache-hit response reads the cached row but hardcodes `source: "cache"` instead of returning `cached.source`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1130`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1131`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1137`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1139`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1140`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1141`.
- The service wrapper logs and returns that `result.source` to callers of `/functions/v1/product-lookup`: `services/claude.js:835`, `services/claude.js:855`, `services/claude.js:858`, and `services/claude.js:878`.
- Results UI distinguishes expert/web/catalog provenance, but groups `"cache"` with verified database data: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2516`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2517`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2521`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2525`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2526`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2527`.

Fix:
- Return `source: cached.source || "cache"` from product-lookup cache hits, and add a separate `servedFromCache: true` flag when callers need cache-hit telemetry.
- Preserve source URL, image URL, rating, and provenance fields consistently between fresh and cached lookup responses.
- Add a contract test that runs a fresh lookup, reads the cache hit for the same key, and asserts source/provenance fields are identical except for the explicit cache-hit flag.
- Update Results and analytics to distinguish data provenance from transport/cache state.

## Eighty-Sixth-Pass Restored Session Migration Finding

### 140. Restored Signed-In Sessions Do Not Retry Guest History Migration

Impact: Guest-to-account history migration only runs from the `SIGNED_IN` auth event. If the app is killed, suspended, times out, or hits a transient storage/network failure before migration finishes, the next launch restores the existing signed-in session through `getSession()` and Supabase's `INITIAL_SESSION` event, but neither path retries `migrateLocalHistoryToSupabase(...)`. That means guest scans can remain stranded after account conversion until the user signs out and signs in again, which makes the history loss look permanent during the exact onboarding/upgrade moment where trust matters most.

Evidence:
- Startup restores an existing session with `supabase.auth.getSession()` and loads profile/purchases, but does not call `migrateLocalHistoryToSupabase(...)` in the `s?.user` branch: `services/auth.js:263`, `services/auth.js:264`, `services/auth.js:267`, `services/auth.js:270`, `services/auth.js:282`, `services/auth.js:291`, and `services/auth.js:297`.
- The only migration call in auth state handling is inside `if (event === "SIGNED_IN" && s?.user)`: `services/auth.js:300`, `services/auth.js:301`, `services/auth.js:307`, `services/auth.js:329`, and `services/auth.js:330`.
- The installed Supabase auth client declares an `INITIAL_SESSION` auth event separate from `SIGNED_IN`: `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/lib/types.ts:48`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/lib/types.ts:49`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/lib/types.ts:50`, and `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/lib/types.ts:51`.
- `onAuthStateChange(...)` emits `INITIAL_SESSION` to new subscribers with the current session, which this listener ignores for migration: `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:2402`, `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:2425`, and `node_modules/@supabase/auth-js/src/GoTrueClient.ts:2426`.
- Migration itself is best-effort and can return without marking completion when the Supabase upsert errors, making retry on later startup necessary: `services/history.js:236`, `services/history.js:240`, `services/history.js:276`, `services/history.js:277`, `services/history.js:281`, `services/history.js:282`, `services/history.js:283`, and `services/history.js:284`.

Fix:
- Run an idempotent guest-history reconciliation whenever a signed-in session is present, including initial `getSession()` startup and `INITIAL_SESSION`, not only `SIGNED_IN`.
- Make migration resumable per entry and record success after both local and Supabase reconciliation finish.
- Surface or log a durable migration retry state so failed migrations are retried on next foreground/startup.
- Add a regression test: create guest history, start sign-in, force migration failure or app restart, relaunch with a restored session, and verify the guest entries migrate without a manual sign-out/sign-in cycle.

## Eighty-Seventh-Pass History Quota Finding

### 141. Same-Product History Suppression Can Hide Counted Scans

Impact: The analysis service suppresses history saves for the same cache key for 60 seconds to avoid duplicate background completions. The Results screen still increments free quota for each delivered result in that window. A user who scans the same bag twice, retries quickly after a confusing result, or runs search/photo paths for the same product can spend multiple free scans while Recent Scans shows only one entry. That makes usage accounting look unfair and undermines the paid history promise because counted results are not reliably represented in the user's history.

Evidence:
- `recentHistorySaves` is a process-local cache-key timestamp map used to suppress duplicate history writes: `services/analysisService.js:35` and `services/analysisService.js:36`.
- `_saveHistory(...)` skips any save for the same cache key when the previous save is less than 60 seconds old: `services/analysisService.js:823`, `services/analysisService.js:834`, `services/analysisService.js:835`, `services/analysisService.js:836`, `services/analysisService.js:837`, and `services/analysisService.js:838`.
- The suppression marker is set before `addHistoryEntry(...)` is called, and the history entry would otherwise include a fresh `dateScanned` for each completed result: `services/analysisService.js:840`, `services/analysisService.js:844`, `services/analysisService.js:848`, and `services/analysisService.js:849`.
- Results increments pet-food or human-food quota for every completed non-history result with a product/food name, independent of whether `_saveHistory(...)` wrote an entry: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:470`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:471`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:472`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:477`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:480`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:482`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:484`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:485`.
- Home labels the saved list as "Recent Scans", so suppressing real completed scans changes the user-visible activity ledger: `screens/HomeScreen.js:838`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:840`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:841`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:861`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:862`.

Fix:
- Deduplicate only the same analysis completion event, not every completed scan for the same product key. Use an analysis instance id or route/session id rather than cache key alone.
- If a result increments quota, create a corresponding history ledger entry or explicitly mark the result as not counted.
- Move duplicate suppression behind successful history persistence and narrow the window to the actual duplicate-event race.
- Add a regression test: complete two scans for the same cache key within 60 seconds and verify quota count and history row count agree.

## Eighty-Eighth-Pass Photo Species Finding

### 142. Photo Scans Can Score Verified Ingredients With Unknown Pet Type

Impact: The photo scan path can fall back to `petType: "unknown"` when product identification does not return a dog/cat value, then continue into verified analysis or ingredient-label recovery without asking the user to choose the species. The edge function includes that pet type in the verified-data prompt, so package-photo and OCR-label results can be scored under ambiguous species context even though the product promise is dog/cat-specific. This is a scan-flow version of the search species problem and matters for in-store use because front-package photos may read brand/flavor but miss small "for dogs" or "for cats" text.

Evidence:
- The identification prompt asks Claude to return `petType`, but this is model-output JSON, not a client-side guarantee: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:446`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:463`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:464`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:472`, and `services/claude.js:711`.
- `_runPhoto(...)` accepts a successful product identification even when `identification.petType` is missing, defaulting to `"unknown"`: `services/analysisService.js:601`, `services/analysisService.js:611`, `services/analysisService.js:614`, and `services/analysisService.js:615`.
- When the database lookup hits, the verified-data payload forwards that `petType` directly into `analyzeWithData(...)`: `services/analysisService.js:696`, `services/analysisService.js:699`, `services/analysisService.js:713`, and `services/analysisService.js:714`.
- When the database misses, the same pet type is sent to the ingredient-label recovery UI and then forwarded into the OCR-verified analysis path: `services/analysisService.js:745`, `services/analysisService.js:751`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:407`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:411`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:541`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:545`, `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:44`, and `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js:50`.
- `_runPhotoWithIngredients(...)` also defaults missing pet type to `"unknown"` before verified analysis: `services/analysisService.js:539`, `services/analysisService.js:543`, `services/analysisService.js:546`, and `services/analysisService.js:549`.
- The edge function includes `Pet Type: ${safe.petType}` in the verified-data prompt whenever the field is present, so `"unknown"` is not omitted: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:522`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:527`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:530`.

Fix:
- Treat missing/unknown pet type as an intermediate confirmation state before verified pet-food scoring.
- Ask the user to choose dog or cat when package identification is otherwise confident but species is absent or ambiguous.
- Include pet type in cache/history keys where the score can differ by species, or prove with tests that the scoring is species-agnostic.
- Add scan fixtures where product name/brand are visible but dog/cat text is hidden, verifying the app asks for species instead of scoring `"unknown"`.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Third-Pass Human-Food Cache Key Finding

### 143. Human-Food Cache Writes Can Use The Model's Pet Type Instead Of The Requested Pet Type

Impact: Human-food checks require the user/request to choose dog or cat, but persistence derives species from the model's returned JSON and silently defaults missing values to dog. A cat request can therefore be saved under a dog cache key or with dog history metadata if the model omits or misstates `petType`. For a safety-sensitive feature, stored answers must preserve the user's requested species rather than trusting the generated response to restate it correctly.

Evidence:
- The client forwards the requested `petType` into human-food analysis payloads: `services/claude.js:605`, `services/claude.js:609`, `services/claude.js:610`, and `services/claude.js:611`.
- The edge function parses request `petType` and rejects `human_food` requests unless it is exactly `"dog"` or `"cat"`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1018`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1024`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1209`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1212`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1214`.
- The human-food prompt asks the model to return `petType`, but validation does not require `petType` or verify it matches the request. It only requires a non-empty `foodName` and a valid `safetyLevel`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:379`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:381`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:383`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:754`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:759`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:761`.
- `writeToCache(...)` derives the shared human-food cache key from `analysis.foodName` and `analysis.petType || "dog"`, not the validated request `petType`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:911`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:913`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:914`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:915`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:916`.
- The human-food runner saves the model result directly to local result cache and history after completion: `services/analysisService.js:462`, `services/analysisService.js:473`, `services/analysisService.js:478`, and `services/analysisService.js:480`.
- History persistence stores `state.result.petType`, so model species drift becomes saved metadata: `services/analysisService.js:842`, `services/analysisService.js:847`, and `services/analysisService.js:849`.

Fix:
- Stamp the validated request `petType` onto the human-food analysis before local save, history save, response, and cache write.
- Change `writeToCache(...)` to accept the request context or a server-normalized analysis object; never fall back human-food cache keys to `"dog"` when the request was `"cat"`.
- Treat missing or mismatched model `petType` as a repairable validation failure: overwrite with the request value or reject and retry with stricter instructions.
- Add fixtures for cat requests where the model output omits `petType` or returns `"dog"`, verifying cache key, history metadata, and UI all retain `"cat"`.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Fourth-Pass Cache Maintenance Finding

### 144. Expired Analysis Cache Cleanup Can Fail When More Than One Row Is Deleted

Impact: The scheduled `cleanup_expired_cache()` maintenance function can fail exactly when it has real work to do: deleting multiple expired `analysis_cache` rows. Expired rows are filtered out of normal reads, but failed cleanup still leaves the shared cache table and expiry index growing with dead application data. Under marketing traffic, that turns cache expiry into storage/index bloat and makes maintenance reliability depend on manual intervention.

Evidence:
- `analysis_cache` rows carry `expires_at`, and the table has an expiry index intended for cleanup: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:8`, `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:10`, `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:15`, and `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:16`.
- The cleanup migration defines `cleanup_expired_cache()` as a `SECURITY DEFINER` function meant to delete expired cache rows periodically: `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:11`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:13`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:16`, and `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:51`.
- The function performs `DELETE FROM analysis_cache WHERE expires_at < NOW() RETURNING 1 INTO deleted_count` before it reads `ROW_COUNT`: `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:21`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:22`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:23`, and `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:25`.
- That `RETURNING ... INTO` assignment expects a single returned row; a normal cleanup run can delete many expired cache rows at once, causing the function to error before it reaches `GET DIAGNOSTICS`.
- The bloat risk is meaningful because runtime cache reads rely on `expires_at` filters and cache writes only refresh rows they touch; expired rows that are never requested again need the maintenance function to remove them: `services/cache.js:370`, `services/cache.js:373`, `services/cache.js:374`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:928`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:932`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:939`.

Fix:
- Remove the `RETURNING 1 INTO deleted_count` clause and use `DELETE ...; GET DIAGNOSTICS deleted_count = ROW_COUNT;`.
- Schema-qualify the table reference and pin `search_path` while fixing the function.
- Add a migration smoke test that inserts two expired `analysis_cache` rows, runs `cleanup_expired_cache()`, and asserts both are deleted and the returned count is `2`.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Fifth-Pass Human-Food Schema Finding

### 145. Human-Food Results Can Complete With Missing Safety Guidance Fields

Impact: Human-food safety answers can be accepted as completed results with only `foodName` and `safetyLevel`. The prompt requires explanation, symptoms, portions, preparation, age guidance, and disclaimer fields, and the UI renders those fields as the actual safety guidance. If Claude returns a short but syntactically valid JSON object, the app can save and display a thin safety result with `"N/A"` or missing sections instead of treating it as an incomplete safety answer.

Evidence:
- The human-food prompt requires a structured object with `summary`, `explanation`, `toxicCompounds`, `symptoms`, `portions`, `benefits`, `alternatives`, `ageGuidance`, `preparation`, and `disclaimer`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:379`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:385`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:386`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:387`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:388`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:389`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:390`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:391`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:392`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:398`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:399`.
- The same prompt calls out `portions`, `preparation`, and `ageGuidance` as required safety details: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:420`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:421`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:422`.
- Server validation for human-food cache eligibility only checks object shape, non-empty `foodName`, and `safetyLevel` membership: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:754`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:755`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:759`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:761`.
- The non-streaming edge path uses that validation only to decide whether to write cache; it still returns the Claude payload to the client either way: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1649`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1650`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1652`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1654`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1665`.
- The client non-streaming path parses the returned text and `analyzeHumanFood(...)` emits it as the result without a schema check: `services/claude.js:471`, `services/claude.js:472`, `services/claude.js:478`, `services/claude.js:648`, `services/claude.js:653`, and `services/claude.js:655`.
- The human-food analysis service treats any returned object without `analysis.error` as complete, then saves local result/history and emits `complete`: `services/analysisService.js:462`, `services/analysisService.js:465`, `services/analysisService.js:473`, `services/analysisService.js:478`, `services/analysisService.js:480`, and `services/analysisService.js:481`.
- The UI falls back to `"N/A"` / `"Not applicable"` for missing safety fields and hides missing explanation/symptom sections, so an incomplete result can look intentionally sparse rather than failed: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:820`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:824`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:825`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:826`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:864`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:876`.

Fix:
- Make `isValidHumanFoodAnalysis(...)` enforce the full safety schema needed by the UI, including non-empty explanation, portions, preparation, disclaimer, and an age-guidance object.
- Return a 502/schema error from the edge function when a human-food result is incomplete instead of returning a payload the client can mark complete.
- Add the same human-food schema guard on the client before `_saveLocalResult(...)`, `_saveHistory(...)`, and `complete` notifications.
- Add fixtures for short JSON such as `{ "foodName": "grapes", "safetyLevel": "dangerous" }`, verifying the app shows a retryable error and does not save history/cache.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Sixth-Pass Missing Profile Quota Finding

### 146. Missing Profile Rows Can Bypass Signed-In Quota Enforcement

Impact: A signed-in user whose `profiles` row is missing can avoid the server-side free quota gate instead of being repaired or blocked. That should be rare because signup creates profiles through a trigger, but it is exactly the kind of account-state inconsistency that appears after failed migrations, trigger failures, manual support fixes, or partial deletes. In that state, paid marketing users can see inconsistent limits: the edge function does not enforce free scan/human-food quota, and the increment RPCs return successful-looking counts without creating the missing row.

Evidence:
- Profiles are intended to be auto-created by the `on_auth_user_created` trigger, but the app still depends on that row existing for quota and entitlement state: `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:23`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:24`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:26`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:36`, `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:38`, and `supabase/migrations/001_auth_and_history.sql:39`.
- The edge function reads `profiles` and enforces free quota only inside `if (profile && !profile.is_pro)`, while ignoring the select error value. If `.single()` finds no profile row, the request skips both pet-food and human-food quota enforcement: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1066`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1067`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1068`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1070`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1072`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1090`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1098`.
- The client profile loader also has no repair/upsert path; it only sets profile and reconciles quota when `!error && data`: `services/auth.js:48`, `services/auth.js:50`, `services/auth.js:54`, `services/auth.js:55`, `services/auth.js:56`, `services/auth.js:60`, and `services/auth.js:64`.
- `increment_scan_count(...)` updates `profiles` and returns `COALESCE(new_count, 0)` when no row is updated, so the client accepts a numeric `0` as success instead of falling back or repairing the account: `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:10`, `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:13`, `supabase/migrations/009_atomic_scan_count.sql:15`, `services/auth.js:212`, `services/auth.js:215`, `services/auth.js:216`, and `services/auth.js:217`.
- Human-food quota has the same missing-row failure mode: `increment_human_food_count(...)` returns `COALESCE(new_count, 1)` without inserting a row, while `get_human_food_count_today(...)` reads no row and returns `0` for the server-side gate: `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:22`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:30`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:32`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:48`, `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:49`, and `supabase/migrations/014_human_food_daily_quota.sql:51`.

Fix:
- Treat a missing profile row for an authenticated user as an account-state error: either server-side upsert a default profile before quota checks or fail closed with a visible "finish account setup / retry" error.
- Change quota RPCs so "no profile row updated" raises a typed error instead of returning `0` or `1`.
- Add a startup repair path that upserts the current user's profile row when `fetchProfile(...)` gets the "no rows" response, then re-fetches entitlement/quota state.
- Add an integration test that deletes a test user's profile row, calls pet-food and human-food analyze, and verifies the request is repaired or blocked before any vendor AI call.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Seventh-Pass Product Lookup Match Finding

### 147. Product Lookup Can Cache Wrong Amazon Or Chewy Matches Without Title Validation

Impact: Product lookup applies title/brand/flavor validation to DFA/CFA/universal web results, but not to Amazon or Chewy results. Because the final picker gives Amazon and Chewy the highest source-priority scores, a broad or ambiguous Google/Amazon search can return ingredients for a neighboring SKU, bundle, wrong flavor, or wrong brand and still be cached under the requested product's `cache_key`. After that, search/photo users can get a confident-looking "verified" analysis for the wrong product and future searches will keep reusing the bad shared row for up to 90 days.

Evidence:
- DFA/CFA scraping validates the matched page against the requested product name and brand before returning a positive result: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:319`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:323`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:328`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:330`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:332`.
- Universal web scraping has a similar positive-match gate for brand, flavor, and match ratio: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:651`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:654`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:658`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:660`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:662`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:664`.
- Chewy search selects the first Google result containing `chewy.com/` and `/dp/`, extracts ingredients and title, then returns `found: true` without checking that the page title matches the requested product, brand, or flavor: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:708`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:731`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:760`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:771`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:772`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:778`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:781`.
- Amazon search extracts the first `/dp/{ASIN}` from rendered search results, scrapes that product page, extracts ingredients and title, then returns `found: true` without checking title/brand/flavor agreement: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:807`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:831`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:832`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:863`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:875`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:881`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:884`.
- The result picker gives Amazon and Chewy the strongest source-priority bonuses, only penalizes wrong first-ingredient protein, and accepts any best score above `-50`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:970`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:971`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1004`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1005`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1014`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1020`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1025`.
- Successful lookup results are upserted into `product_data` under the requested `cacheKey`, not under a key derived from the matched page title, and are reused by later cache hits/search analysis: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1125`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1238`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1242`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1243`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1254`, `services/cache.js:153`, `services/cache.js:155`, and `services/analysisService.js:328`.

Fix:
- Run one shared `validateProductMatch(...)` guard for every positive source, including Amazon and Chewy, before `pickBestResult(...)` and before caching.
- For Amazon/Chewy, require brand agreement plus title/token/flavor agreement; if the matched page title differs, cache under the matched page's normalized key only after a human-readable confidence threshold passes.
- Store match metadata (`requested_name`, `matched_title`, `matched_url`, `match_score`, `variant_match`) and quarantine low-confidence rows instead of publishing them directly to searchable `product_data`.
- Add fixtures for ambiguous product-line queries where Amazon/Chewy returns a different flavor or bundle, verifying the lookup returns `found: false` and does not upsert `product_data`.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Eighth-Pass Streaming Parser Finding

### 148. Client Streaming Parser Can Drop Valid SSE Events Split Across Network Chunks

Impact: The client streaming parser treats each `ReadableStream` chunk as if it contains whole SSE lines. Network chunk boundaries are arbitrary, so a valid `data: {...}` event can be split between two reads. The current parser tries to parse the first half, silently discards it as malformed, then discards the second half because it no longer starts with `data: `.
