That can turn a healthy stream into missing text, incomplete JSON, streaming retries, or a slower non-streaming fallback. This is a direct store-scan latency risk because verified/photo/human-food analysis all try streaming first when `expo/fetch` is available.

Evidence:
- Streaming is enabled through `expo/fetch` and `canStream`, making this path active for builds where readable streams are available: `services/claude.js:9`, `services/claude.js:10`, `services/claude.js:11`, `services/claude.js:14`, `services/claude.js:16`, and `services/claude.js:17`.
- `_callStreaming(...)` decodes each read into `chunk`, immediately calls `chunk.split("\n")`, and parses only lines that start with `data: `; it does not preserve an unfinished line for the next read: `services/claude.js:327`, `services/claude.js:328`, `services/claude.js:331`, `services/claude.js:336`, `services/claude.js:339`, `services/claude.js:340`, and `services/claude.js:345`.
- Malformed JSON lines are silently skipped, so a split event's first half is lost instead of buffered and retried: `services/claude.js:344`, `services/claude.js:345`, `services/claude.js:346`, `services/claude.js:347`, `services/claude.js:349`, and `services/claude.js:350`.
- The final decoder flush repeats the same line parsing without any carried-over partial line buffer: `services/claude.js:380`, `services/claude.js:381`, `services/claude.js:383`, `services/claude.js:384`, `services/claude.js:385`, and `services/claude.js:389`.
- Valid streaming failures then trigger expensive retry/fallback behavior: photo analysis tries streaming twice and then starts a separate 90-second non-streaming call, verified-data analysis does the same, and human-food analysis tries streaming twice before a 60-second non-streaming fallback: `services/claude.js:489`, `services/claude.js:490`, `services/claude.js:501`, `services/claude.js:504`, `services/claude.js:552`, `services/claude.js:553`, `services/claude.js:565`, `services/claude.js:568`, `services/claude.js:615`, `services/claude.js:616`, `services/claude.js:627`, `services/claude.js:630`, and `services/claude.js:635`.
- The server-side cache branch avoids this specific bug by accumulating the full SSE text before splitting lines, which means the client can fail or fall back while the server cache branch may still parse the same upstream stream successfully: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1572`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1582`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1585`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1588`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1590`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:588`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:590`.

Fix:
- Replace the ad hoc per-chunk loop with a real SSE parser or a small buffered parser that carries trailing partial lines between reads.
- Only parse an event after a complete SSE record delimiter has arrived; preserve partial JSON/event data across chunks.
- Add tests that feed `_callStreaming` an SSE payload split at every possible byte boundary across `data:` prefixes and JSON payloads, verifying the assembled text matches the unsplit stream.
- Track streaming parse failures separately from vendor/model failures so latency metrics can show parser-induced retries.

## One-Hundred-Forty-Ninth-Pass Timeout Classification Finding

### 149. App-Triggered Fetch Timeouts Can Be Classified As User Cancellations

Impact: The offline detector is supposed to flip the app offline after repeated network or timeout failures, but several app-owned request deadlines call `AbortController.abort()` without a timeout reason. In React Native, those failures commonly surface as `AbortError` with a generic "Aborted" message. The shared error classifier treats that as `cancelled`, not `timeout`, so `reportNetworkError(...)` drops the event and the app can stay "online" through repeated OPFF/product-lookup/stream timeouts in weak store connectivity.

Evidence:
- The network detector only counts errors classified as `network` or `timeout`: `services/network.js:37`, `services/network.js:41`, `services/network.js:42`, `services/network.js:43`, `services/network.js:45`, and `services/network.js:47`.
- `classifyError(...)` explicitly handles `AbortError`, but only returns `timeout` when the error message itself contains "timeout"; otherwise it returns `cancelled` and marks the error silent: `services/errors.js:93`, `services/errors.js:94`, `services/errors.js:95`, `services/errors.js:96`, `services/errors.js:98`, `services/errors.js:104`, `services/errors.js:105`, and `services/errors.js:109`.
- The streaming analysis timeout logs a timeout but aborts with a bare `callController.abort()`, then passes the caught error into `reportNetworkError(err)`: `services/claude.js:262`, `services/claude.js:264`, `services/claude.js:265`, `services/claude.js:266`, `services/claude.js:286`, and `services/claude.js:288`.
- Barcode lookup uses the same bare-abort timeout pattern and reports the caught error to the network detector: `services/opff.js:97`, `services/opff.js:98`, `services/opff.js:99`, `services/opff.js:131`, `services/opff.js:132`, and `services/opff.js:133`.
- Product lookup sets a 25-second scraping timeout with bare `controller.abort()`, then reports caught fetch failures through `reportNetworkError(err)`: `services/claude.js:841`, `services/claude.js:842`, `services/claude.js:855`, `services/claude.js:859`, `services/claude.js:862`, and `services/claude.js:863`.
- This compounds the existing optimistic-offline and Supabase-reporting gaps because the few paths that do call `reportNetworkError(...)` can still fail to advance offline state when the failure was caused by the app's own timeout deadline.

Fix:
- Abort app-owned deadlines with explicit timeout reasons, for example `controller.abort(new DOMException("Request timeout", "TimeoutError"))`, or throw a typed timeout error from each timeout handler.
- Update `classifyError(...)` to distinguish user/navigation cancellations from known request deadlines, not only from error message text.
- Have `reportNetworkError(...)` accept an optional context such as `{ reason: "timeout", source: "opff" }` so telemetry does not depend on platform-specific AbortError messages.
- Add unit tests for `classifyError(new DOMException("Aborted", "AbortError"))` in both user-cancel and app-timeout contexts, plus integration tests that three OPFF/product-lookup timeouts flip the offline banner.

## One-Hundred-Fiftieth-Pass Dependency Declaration Finding

### 150. Runtime Imports Rely On Undeclared `expo-constants` Transitive Dependency

Impact: The app directly imports `expo-constants` in startup configuration, purchases, and the profile footer, but `package.json` does not declare `expo-constants` as a dependency. It resolves on this machine only because another Expo package currently brings it into `node_modules`. That is fragile release packaging: a clean install under a different package manager, dependency dedupe layout, Expo patch, or CI/EAS cache state can turn a working local build into a Metro "Unable to resolve module expo-constants" failure before Supabase config, RevenueCat initialization, or Profile rendering can run.

Evidence:
- `config/env.js` imports `Constants` from `expo-constants` before exporting Supabase and Google config used by core services: `config/env.js:1`, `config/env.js:3`, `config/env.js:4`, `config/env.js:6`, `config/env.js:7`, `config/env.js:9`, and `config/env.js:10`.
- `services/purchases.js` imports the same package to read RevenueCat API keys before configuring purchases: `services/purchases.js:3`, `services/purchases.js:5`, `services/purchases.js:6`, `services/purchases.js:7`, `services/purchases.js:8`, and `services/purchases.js:15`.
- `screens/ProfileScreen.js` imports `expo-constants` and reads `Constants.expoConfig?.version` for the visible app version footer: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:13` and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:121`.
- `package.json` declares many Expo modules but not `expo-constants`: `package.json:11`, `package.json:18`, `package.json:19`, `package.json:20`, `package.json:31`, and `package.json:32`.
- `npm ls expo-constants --depth=0` reports `(empty)`, confirming it is not a top-level declared dependency even though `require.resolve("expo-constants/package.json")` currently works through the installed transitive tree.

Fix:
- Add `expo-constants` to `package.json` at the SDK-compatible version and update the lockfile intentionally.
- Add `expo-doctor` or a dependency hygiene check that fails when app source imports packages missing from direct dependencies.
- Run a clean install/export in CI with an empty dependency cache before release so transitive-hoist assumptions are caught.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-First-Pass Supabase Function Config Finding

### 151. Edge Function JWT Verification Settings Are Untracked

Impact: Guest scanning, anonymous human-food checks, and product lookup depend on Supabase edge functions accepting requests that carry only the public anon key and no `Authorization` token. Locally, that behavior is controlled by `supabase/config.toml`, which sets `verify_jwt = false` for both `analyze` and `product-lookup`. That file is currently untracked. A clean checkout, CI deploy, or another developer's Supabase deploy can therefore ship the same function code with different platform-level JWT verification, causing guest requests to be rejected before the app's in-function guest/rate-limit logic runs. The failure would look like broken scans/search recovery in production even though it worked locally.

Evidence:
- The local Supabase config disables platform JWT verification for the main analysis endpoint: `supabase/config.toml:1`, `supabase/config.toml:2`, and `supabase/config.toml:3`.
- The same untracked config disables platform JWT verification for the product lookup endpoint: `supabase/config.toml:5`, `supabase/config.toml:6`, and `supabase/config.toml:7`.
- Current git state shows the function config itself is not tracked: `git status --short -- supabase/config.toml` reports `?? supabase/config.toml`, and `git ls-files -- supabase/config.toml` returns no path.
- The client explicitly supports guest function calls by returning headers with `Content-Type` and `apikey` only when no Supabase session exists: `services/claude.js:30`, `services/claude.js:31`, `services/claude.js:32`, `services/claude.js:35`, `services/claude.js:42`, and `services/claude.js:44`.
- The `analyze` function expects to handle optional auth inside function code and only validates a bearer token if one is present: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:963`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:972`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:973`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:987`.
- `product-lookup` also treats auth as optional and applies anonymous IP limiting inside the function after its own auth parsing: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1056`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1078`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1080`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1087`.

Fix:
- Commit `supabase/config.toml` or move function JWT settings into an explicit deploy script that is versioned with the app.
- Add a clean-checkout Supabase deploy dry run or staging deploy that verifies `analyze` and `product-lookup` have the intended JWT verification settings before mobile builds are promoted.
- Add smoke tests for signed-out guest photo scan, guest human-food check, and product lookup against the deployed staging functions so platform-level auth mismatches fail before marketing traffic.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Second-Pass OPFF Lookup Match Finding

### 152. OPFF Name Lookup Can Cache First Search Result Under The Requested Product

Impact: The product-lookup edge function can run OPFF in parallel with Amazon, or as the only lookup source when no ScrapingBee key is configured. That path searches OPFF by name, picks the first result with enough ingredient text, and returns it as a positive match without verifying that the OPFF product name, brand, flavor, or pet species matches the requested product. A broad or ambiguous product name can therefore publish a neighboring OPFF row into `product_data` under the requested cache key, after which search and photo flows can treat the wrong ingredients as verified for up to 90 days.

Evidence:
- OPFF name lookup sends a broad `search_terms` query with `page_size=5`, then selects the first returned product with ingredient text longer than 20 characters, falling back to the first product if none has ingredients: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:907`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:911`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:929`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:930`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:931`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:932`.
- The OPFF branch parses and returns that selected row without checking its product name, brand, flavor, category, or dog/cat species against the request: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:934`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:940`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:945`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:948`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:949`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:950`.
- OPFF participates in the first lookup tier beside Amazon, and becomes the only lookup source when `SCRAPINGBEE_API_KEY` is absent: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1174`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1177`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1179`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1205`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1206`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1207`.
- The final picker only requires `found` and at least 10 ingredients, so an OPFF-only candidate can pass even without requested-title validation: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:970`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:971`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:972`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:974`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1019`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1025`.
- Successful lookup results are upserted into `product_data` under the requested `cacheKey`, not a key derived from the OPFF matched product name, and later app searches reuse rows from `product_data`: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1125`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1238`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1242`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1243`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1254`, `services/cache.js:153`, and `services/analysisService.js:328`.

Fix:
- Run the same shared `validateProductMatch(...)` guard on OPFF candidates before `pickBestResult(...)` and before `product_data` upsert.
- Require brand/title/token/flavor agreement for OPFF name search; when OPFF returns a different but valid product, cache it only under the matched OPFF product key with explicit low-confidence provenance.
- Include pet category validation from OPFF categories/tags so cat and dog products with similar names cannot satisfy each other's lookup.
- Add fixtures for ambiguous OPFF name queries and a no-ScrapingBee configuration, verifying the function returns `found: false` or caches under the matched product key rather than the request key.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Third-Pass Photo Lookup Candidate Finding

### 153. Photo Lookup Exact-Key Candidates Can Prefer Broad AI Search Terms

Impact: After a photo scan identifies a product, the app asks the model for alternate `searchTerms` such as brand plus flavor, brand plus sub-brand, and variant-only phrases. `getProductData(...)` folds all of those into exact `cache_key` candidates and, if multiple rows exist, picks whichever exact-key row has the largest ingredient count. That exact-key branch bypasses the later token/variant scoring safeguards. A broad model-generated term can therefore win over the actual identified product or brand+product key, and the app will analyze those ingredients as verified data for the photographed product.

Evidence:
- The identification prompt explicitly requires broad alternate search terms, including brand plus flavor noun, brand plus sub-brand, and variant words alone: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:485`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:486`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:487`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:488`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:489`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:490`.
- Photo analysis passes the identified product, brand, variant/sub-brand, and model-provided `searchTerms` into `getProductData(...)`: `services/analysisService.js:611`, `services/analysisService.js:612`, `services/analysisService.js:613`, `services/analysisService.js:615`, `services/analysisService.js:644`, and `services/analysisService.js:645`.
- `getProductData(...)` treats every search term as an exact cache-key candidate alongside the canonical product and brand/product keys: `services/cache.js:145`, `services/cache.js:146`, `services/cache.js:147`, `services/cache.js:148`, `services/cache.js:149`, and `services/cache.js:150`.
- When more than one exact candidate row exists, the function chooses the row with the largest ingredient count, not the canonical product key, brand match, variant agreement, or query score: `services/cache.js:155`, `services/cache.js:158`, `services/cache.js:161`, `services/cache.js:162`, `services/cache.js:163`, and `services/cache.js:165`.
- The safer token/variant scoring logic only runs after the exact-key branch misses, so exact search-term hits are not checked by the 60% overlap threshold or variant-overlap safeguard: `services/cache.js:176`, `services/cache.js:178`, `services/cache.js:179`, `services/cache.js:233`, `services/cache.js:234`, `services/cache.js:243`, and `services/cache.js:244`.
- A matching row is immediately treated as verified ingredients and can feed shared cached analysis for the photographed product: `services/analysisService.js:649`, `services/analysisService.js:650`, `services/analysisService.js:696`, `services/analysisService.js:697`, `services/analysisService.js:699`, `services/analysisService.js:713`, and `services/analysisService.js:714`.

Fix:
- Rank exact-key candidates by source of the key first: canonical `productName`, then `brand + productName`, then high-confidence `brand + variant`, and only then broad `searchTerms`.
- Run the same brand/title/flavor/variant agreement check on exact-key candidate rows before returning them.
- Do not use variant-only or brand-sub-brand search terms as exact cache keys unless the returned row also contains the identified brand and product variant.
- Add fixtures where a broad AI term matches a richer neighboring catalog row, verifying the photo scan either selects the canonical product row or returns a label-capture fallback.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Fourth-Pass Pet-Food Schema Validation Finding

### 154. Pet-Food Analysis Validation Accepts Skeletal Successful Results

Impact: Pet-food analysis responses only need a non-empty `productName` and numeric `overallScore` to pass the server's validity check. A malformed, truncated, or under-specified model response that includes those two fields but omits ingredients, category breakdowns, verdict text, nutrition analysis, recall fields, or safety guidance can still be returned to the app, cached in `analysis_cache`, saved locally, and shown as a successful result. That produces a polished-looking but thin score page instead of a retryable "analysis incomplete" error, which is especially risky when new marketing users are judging accuracy from the first scan.

Evidence:
- Server pet-food validation only requires object shape, no `error`, `productName`, and bounded `overallScore`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:623`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:626`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:630`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:631`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:633`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:635`.
- That same validator controls whether streamed and non-streamed responses are written into the shared `analysis_cache`: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1602`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1604`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1605`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1606`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1649`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1651`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1654`.
- Client search/photo/ingredient-label paths treat any returned object without `analysis.error` as complete and can save it locally/history before emitting `complete`: `services/analysisService.js:404`, `services/analysisService.js:409`, `services/analysisService.js:411`, `services/analysisService.js:546`, `services/analysisService.js:550`, `services/analysisService.js:552`, `services/analysisService.js:717`, and `services/analysisService.js:722`.
- Results only detects a broken pet-food completion when `overallScore` is missing, so a skeletal response with a score bypasses the interruption error guard: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:713`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:719`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:720`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:750`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:757`.
- The successful pet-food layout assumes richer fields: summary rows derive red flags and beneficial ingredients from `result.ingredients`, quality breakdown uses `result.categories`, quick stats use `nutritionAnalysis`, and verdict renders only if `result.verdict` exists. Missing fields therefore silently remove the promised content instead of failing the analysis: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:790`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:795`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:987`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:993`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1020`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1093`.

Fix:
- Define a mode-specific pet-food analysis schema for `photo`, `verified`, `barcode`, and search-derived verified analysis. Require at least product name, score, verdict, ingredient array, category breakdown, and the safety/recall fields the UI and paywall copy promise.
- Reject skeletal pet-food responses with a typed 502/schema error before shared-cache writes, local-cache writes, history saves, or quota increments.
- Add the same schema validator on the client before `_saveLocalResult(...)`, `_saveHistory(...)`, and `complete` notifications so streamed responses cannot bypass server cache validation.
- Add fixtures for `{ "productName": "Test Food", "overallScore": 72 }` and for responses missing ingredients/categories/verdict, verifying the app shows a retryable error and does not cache, save history, or count quota.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Fifth-Pass Cache Metadata Finding

### 155. Shared Analysis Cache Mislabels Search And Photo Results As Barcode Lookups

Impact: The shared `analysis_cache.lookup_type` column is intended to distinguish barcode and name-based cache rows, and the database has an index on it for filtered queries. The edge function currently labels every non-human-food write that has a `cacheKey` as `"barcode"`. Search, photo, and ingredient-label verified-analysis paths also pass product cache keys, so those rows are written as barcode lookups even though they came from product-name/product-data flows. That makes cache analytics, cleanup, hit-rate reporting, and future barcode rollout decisions misleading right when the team needs accurate store-scan performance data.

Evidence:
- The cache table defines `lookup_type` as shared metadata with a default of `"name"` and a comment limiting it to barcode or name, and later migrations add an index for `lookup_type` queries: `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:2`, `supabase/migrations/004_analysis_cache.sql:4`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:7`, `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:8`, and `supabase/migrations/005_cleanup_and_indexes.sql:9`.
- `writeToCache(...)` derives `lookupType` as `"human_food"` for human-food rows, `"barcode"` for any row with a `cacheKey`, and `"name"` otherwise: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:904`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:907`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:908`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:923`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:932`, and `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:933`.
- Barcode analysis legitimately calls verified analysis with the UPC/EAN as `cacheKey`: `services/analysisService.js:245`, `services/analysisService.js:248`, `services/analysisService.js:261`, and `services/analysisService.js:281`.
- Search analysis also calls verified analysis with a product-data shared cache key, not a barcode: `services/analysisService.js:338`, `services/analysisService.js:381`, `services/analysisService.js:400`, and `services/analysisService.js:401`.
- Photo DB-hit analysis does the same with the product-data shared cache key: `services/analysisService.js:654`, `services/analysisService.js:696`, `services/analysisService.js:713`, and `services/analysisService.js:714`.
- The app already depends on cache-hit instrumentation for launch tuning, including prewarm and cache-hit behavior, so polluted lookup-type metadata undermines the metrics needed to decide whether barcode/search/photo paths are working: `services/cache.js:290`, `services/cache.js:300`, `services/cache.js:353`, `services/cache.js:397`, and `AUDIT_2026-06-05.md:128`.

Fix:
- Pass an explicit `lookupType` from the client or derive it from mode plus cache-key shape, not merely from cache-key presence.
- Use `"barcode"` only for barcode/UPC/EAN inputs, `"product"` or `"name"` for search/photo product-data analyses, and `"human_food"` only for human-food safety answers.
- Backfill existing `analysis_cache.lookup_type` rows by detecting numeric barcode-like keys versus normalized product-name keys before relying on cache analytics.
- Add a cache contract test for barcode, search, photo DB-hit, ingredient-label, and human-food writes that asserts the stored `lookup_type` matches the originating flow.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Sixth-Pass Purchase Entitlement Finding

### 156. Purchase Without Active Entitlement Can Fail Silently

Impact: RevenueCat/StoreKit can return customer info from a purchase attempt while the configured `pro` entitlement is not active. That can happen with a wrong entitlement id, a product not attached to the entitlement, delayed pending entitlement state, or sandbox/App Store configuration drift. In that state the purchase wrapper returns no success, no cancellation, and no error. The Paywall purchase handler then resets the CTA and stops, with no alert, retry, restore, or support path. A user can complete the native purchase flow or see a store confirmation, land back on an unchanged paywall/free state, and have no explanation during the highest-value conversion moment.

Evidence:
- `purchasePackage(...)` derives success solely from `customerInfo.entitlements.active["pro"]` after `Purchases.purchasePackage(...)`, then returns `{ success, cancelled: false, error: null }` even when `success` is false: `services/purchases.js:86`, `services/purchases.js:88`, `services/purchases.js:89`, and `services/purchases.js:90`.
- The purchase handler has branches for `result.success`, `result.cancelled`, and `result.error`, but no final `else` for the no-entitlement result. After `setPurchasing(false)`, that state silently returns the button to idle: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:172`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:174`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:176`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:181`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:183`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:185`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:187`.
- Missing RevenueCat package/offering is handled separately before purchase starts, so this is not the same as the already-documented unavailable-product fallback state: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:163`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:164`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:165`.
- The restore path already has an explicit no-active-purchase branch, showing "No Purchases Found" when restore returns no entitlement and no error; purchase lacks an equivalent no-entitlement branch: `screens/PaywallScreen.js:196`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:200`, `screens/PaywallScreen.js:202`, and `screens/PaywallScreen.js:203`.

Fix:
- Return a typed `no_entitlement` purchase result when RevenueCat returns customer info but the configured Pro entitlement is not active.
- Surface a clear purchase-received-but-not-active state with retry entitlement check, restore, and support/contact options instead of silently resetting the CTA.
- Log package id, product id, entitlement keys, and the expected entitlement id for this path so store/RevenueCat mapping mistakes are diagnosable without exposing sensitive customer data.
- Add a Paywall mock test where `purchasePackage(...)` resolves with customer info that lacks the `pro` entitlement, and verify the user sees an actionable message and remains in a coherent purchase state.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Seventh-Pass Scan Latency Finding

### 157. AI Request Timeouts Start After Unbounded Auth Header Work

Impact: The app presents short helper timeouts for the slow in-store scan path: identify has 15 seconds, OCR has 20 seconds, product lookup has 25 seconds, and streaming analysis waits 30 seconds for a response. Those timers currently start after `_getAuthHeaders()` finishes reading the Supabase session and possibly refreshing the token. A slow or wedged session read/refresh can therefore delay the first AI request before the helper timeout even starts, and parent cancellation does not abort the auth-header promise. A signed-in shopper with poor store connectivity can wait far longer than the visible operation budget, hit the 120-second global analysis timeout, or retry while the original request setup is still unresolved.

Evidence:
- `_getAuthHeaders()` awaits `supabase.auth.getSession()` and then awaits a shared `supabase.auth.refreshSession()` promise when the token expires within five minutes. Neither await is raced against a timeout or wired to the caller's `AbortSignal`: `services/claude.js:35`, `services/claude.js:36`, `services/claude.js:50`, `services/claude.js:53`, and `services/claude.js:57`.
- Streaming analysis gets auth headers before it creates the 30-second response timeout controller, so header lookup/refresh time is outside that timeout: `services/claude.js:254`, `services/claude.js:260`, `services/claude.js:263`, `services/claude.js:264`, and `services/claude.js:279`.
- Product identification has the same structure: it awaits auth headers first, then creates the 15-second timeout and starts the fetch: `services/claude.js:665`, `services/claude.js:669`, `services/claude.js:671`, `services/claude.js:672`, and `services/claude.js:683`.
- Ingredient OCR and product lookup also fetch auth headers before starting their 20-second and 25-second timers: `services/claude.js:723`, `services/claude.js:727`, `services/claude.js:728`, `services/claude.js:729`, `services/claude.js:835`, `services/claude.js:839`, `services/claude.js:841`, and `services/claude.js:842`.
- The analysis service's only outer guard is the 120-second hard timeout; when it fires it aborts `state.controller`, but `_getAuthHeaders()` has no signal parameter to observe that abort while it is still in `getSession()` or `refreshSession()`: `services/analysisService.js:98`, `services/analysisService.js:100`, `services/analysisService.js:101`, `services/analysisService.js:105`, and `services/analysisService.js:108`.
- Scanner mount tries to pre-refresh auth with `checkSession()`, but that helper also awaits `getSession()` and `refreshSession()` without a bounded timeout, and the scanner only logs failures instead of establishing a ready/unknown auth state before capture: `screens/ScannerScreen.js:116`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:118`, `screens/ScannerScreen.js:119`, `services/auth.js:121`, `services/auth.js:123`, `services/auth.js:130`, and `services/auth.js:132`.

Fix:
- Make `_getAuthHeaders({ signal, timeoutMs })` bounded and abort-aware; race session read and token refresh against a small timeout that returns an explicit `auth_unknown` state rather than silently waiting.
- Start per-call operation timers before auth-header acquisition, or include auth acquisition in the same request budget users experience.
- Reuse the current AuthProvider session/access token for scan requests when available, and refresh in the background before the scanner opens instead of blocking the first AI call.
- If auth is slow or unknown, show a clear "checking session / retry" state or intentionally proceed as guest only when the app was already in guest mode.
- Add tests that hang `getSession()` and `refreshSession()` while starting identify, OCR, product lookup, and verified analysis, verifying each path times out within its advertised budget and cancels cleanly.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Eighth-Pass Quota Reconciliation Finding

### 158. Guest Quota Reconciliation Can Replay Unbounded Local Counts To Server

Impact: When a guest later signs in, the app tries to preserve guest quota usage by taking the max of local AsyncStorage and server profile counts. That goal is reasonable, but the implementation trusts the local value without clamping, validating, or tying it to a scan ledger. If `@woof_scan_count` or the human-food local counter is corrupted, manually changed, restored from a bad backup, or left high by a development/test path, sign-in can immediately lock the account into a false exhausted quota and replay the difference to Supabase one RPC at a time. A single bad local value such as `1000` can produce hundreds of quota RPCs during sign-in and write a misleading server quota state that follows the user across devices.

Evidence:
- Profile load reads the local pet-food count from `AsyncStorage`, parses it as a number, and computes `Math.max(local, data.scan_count)` with no clamp to the free limit, no sanity ceiling, and no validation against actual local history rows: `services/auth.js:60`, `services/auth.js:61`, `services/auth.js:62`, and `services/auth.js:63`.
- It mirrors that reconciled value back into React state and local storage, so an oversized local value can immediately make the signed-in UI look out of free scans: `services/auth.js:64` and `services/auth.js:65`.
- If local is higher than the server profile count, it loops from `0` to `local - data.scan_count` and fires one `increment_scan_count` RPC per missing count, without awaiting, batching, clamping, or rate limiting: `services/auth.js:66`, `services/auth.js:67`, `services/auth.js:68`, `services/auth.js:69`, and `services/auth.js:70`.
- Human-food quota reconciliation repeats the same trust pattern: it reads local state, uses `Math.max(local, hfToday)`, updates local UI/storage, then loops once per local-server difference with `increment_human_food_count`: `services/auth.js:78`, `services/auth.js:82`, `services/auth.js:83`, `services/auth.js:84`, `services/auth.js:85`, `services/auth.js:86`, `services/auth.js:87`, `services/auth.js:88`, and `services/auth.js:89`.
- Normal scan increments also mirror server counts into the same local `@woof_scan_count` key, so this key is both UI cache and future sign-in reconciliation input rather than a bounded, audited ledger: `services/auth.js:207`, `services/auth.js:212`, `services/auth.js:216`, and `services/auth.js:217`.

Fix:
- Treat local quota mirrors as display caches, not authoritative migration input. Clamp guest-to-account reconciliation to the known free limits or, better, reconcile from actual local scan/history ledger rows.
- Replace per-count replay loops with a single trusted server RPC that validates an explicit bounded delta, or avoid server backfill entirely and keep guest usage device-scoped.
- Reject or reset non-finite, negative, or implausibly high local quota values and record telemetry/support breadcrumbs when corruption is detected.
- Add tests for local `@woof_scan_count = "999"`, malformed local counts, and human-food local count drift before sign-in, verifying the app does not issue unbounded RPCs or persist a false exhausted server quota.

## One-Hundred-Fifty-Ninth-Pass History Replay Finding

### 159. History Rows Can Outlive Replayable Result Payloads

Impact: The app can keep scan history rows after the result payload needed to render them has been evicted locally, expired from the shared cache, or invalidated by a schema/rubric bump. A user can see a past scan in Recent Scans, tap it, and land on "This result is no longer available" even though the history row remains visible and actionable. The message also says cached results expire after 7 days, while the backend writes shared analysis cache rows for 30 days and local result eviction is count-based. That makes history feel broken during retention-heavy paid marketing use: the app advertises history, stores 50 rows, but some rows become dead links with misleading expiry copy instead of being hidden, refreshed, or rescored.

Evidence:
- History storage keeps up to 50 rows locally and in Supabase, independent of whether the full analysis payload is still replayable: `services/history.js:7`, `services/history.js:124`, `services/history.js:134`, `services/history.js:139`, `services/history.js:177`, `services/history.js:185`, and `services/history.js:186`.
- A history row stores only lightweight metadata and a `cache_key`, not the serialized analysis needed to render Results if both caches miss: `services/history.js:54`, `services/history.js:58`, `services/history.js:59`, `services/history.js:62`, `services/history.js:63`, `services/history.js:65`, and `services/history.js:66`.
- History taps navigate directly to Results history mode with only `cacheKey` and optional human-food metadata; they do not revalidate cache availability before opening the result screen: `screens/HomeScreen.js:496`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:497`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:498`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:499`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:500`.
- Results history mode can only replay an in-memory running/completed analysis, the local result cache, or `analysis_cache`; it does not re-run the original analysis from history metadata when those layers miss: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:267`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:284`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:293`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:298`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:309`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:319`.
- The local result cache keeps only 30 full results and deletes older payloads, while history keeps 50 rows: `services/analysisService.js:7`, `services/analysisService.js:8`, `services/analysisService.js:9`, `services/analysisService.js:784`, `services/analysisService.js:788`, `services/analysisService.js:789`, and `services/analysisService.js:791`.
- Local result reads also drop stale-schema entries without repairing/removing the matching history row: `services/analysisService.js:804`, `services/analysisService.js:806`, `services/analysisService.js:809`, `services/analysisService.js:810`, `services/analysisService.js:812`, and `services/analysisService.js:813`.
- Shared analysis cache reads reject expired rows and stale-schema rows, but the failure path just returns a miss to Results history mode: `services/cache.js:374`, `services/cache.js:378`, `services/cache.js:384`, `services/cache.js:387`, `services/cache.js:389`, `services/cache.js:390`, and `services/cache.js:392`.
- The edge function writes shared analysis cache rows with a 30-day expiry, while the user-facing history miss copy says cached results expire after 7 days: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:926`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:932`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:939`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:319`.

Fix:
- Align history retention with replayable payload retention: either keep serialized user-scoped result payloads for every retained history row, or prune/disable history rows when their payload is no longer available.
- When history replay misses the local/shared cache, offer a scan-again or re-analyze path that can reconstruct the result from safe stored inputs instead of leaving the row as a dead link.
- Replace the hardcoded 7-day message with copy derived from the actual retention policy, and distinguish "expired", "old scoring model", "removed", and "offline/unavailable" cases.
- Add tests with 31+ saved analyses and 50 history rows, expired shared cache rows, and stale `schemaVersion` entries, verifying history either replays, refreshes, or removes the row coherently.

## One-Hundred-Sixtieth-Pass Results Conversion Finding

### 160. First-Scan Toast Is Marked Shown But Never Rendered

Impact: The Results screen has a one-time first-scan education toast intended to tell free users they have two scans left. That toast is imported, state is created, and AsyncStorage is immediately marked so it should not appear again, but the component is never mounted in the Results JSX. A brand-new user can complete the first scan, never see the quota education message, and still have `@woof_first_scan_toast_shown` set to `true`, permanently suppressing the intended first-scan conversion/expectation cue on that device.

Evidence:
- Results imports `FirstScanToast` from the component bundle: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:57`.
- The screen creates `showFirstScanToast` state and, after the first completed non-history free scan with a score, reads `@woof_first_scan_toast_shown`: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:497`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:498`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:499`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:500`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:502`.
- If the flag is absent, the effect writes `@woof_first_scan_toast_shown = "true"` before scheduling the toast visibility timers: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:503`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:504`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:505`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:506`.
- The returned Results tree renders the post-scan prompt, off-screen share card, and ingredient sheet, but no `<FirstScanToast visible={showFirstScanToast} />` mount point: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1154`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1155`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1168`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1169`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1183`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:1184`.
- The component itself exists and contains the intended user-facing copy, confirming this is dead UI state rather than an intentionally removed feature: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2392`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2394`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2406`.

Fix:
- Mount `FirstScanToast` in the Results success layout, positioned so it does not cover the header, share button, or paywall gate.
- Only persist `@woof_first_scan_toast_shown` after the toast has actually rendered, or keep the flag write behind a render/animation completion callback.
- Add a first-scan UI test that starts with no toast flag, completes a free scan, verifies the toast is visible once, and verifies it is not shown on the second scan.

## One-Hundred-Sixty-First-Pass Search Recovery Finding

### 161. Search Product-Not-Found Errors Retry The Same Invalid Row

Impact: When a user taps a search result that the Results pipeline later rejects as not analysis-ready, the app tells them to scan the product instead, but the only primary CTA is still "Try Again". Pressing it remounts the same search-mode Results route with the same product name, brand, and cache key, so the user can loop through the same "Product not found in database" failure instead of being routed to the scanner, ingredient-label capture, or Home search cleanup. This compounds the exact user complaint that searched products say they are no longer in the database: the app has enough context to offer the right recovery path, but it replays the broken path.

Evidence:
- The search analysis path emits a specific product-not-found error after `getProductData(...)` fails to find enough valid product data: `services/analysisService.js:328`, `services/analysisService.js:329`, `services/analysisService.js:434`, `services/analysisService.js:435`, `services/analysisService.js:436`, and `services/analysisService.js:437`.
- That error string says "Try scanning the product instead", but `classifyError(...)` has no product-not-found/search-miss category, so it falls through to the unknown fallback: `services/errors.js:113`, `services/errors.js:185`, `services/errors.js:186`, `services/errors.js:187`, `services/errors.js:188`, and `services/errors.js:189`.
- `ErrorState` defaults unknown errors to a "Try Again" button wired to `onRetry`: `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2762`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2765`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2766`, `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2767`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/components.js:2768`.
- Results passes `handleRetry` into `ErrorState` for this path: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:738`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:739`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:740`.
- For search mode, `handleRetry` replaces Results with the same `mode`, `productName`, `brand`, `cacheKey`, and `petType`, which repeats the same invalid product lookup instead of opening a scan/label fallback: `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:570`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:575`, `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:576`, and `screens/ResultsScreen/index.js:577`.
- The original search tap also stores the row into recent searches before the result has proven analysis-ready, so the same invalid row can be reopened later unless separate stale-recent handling catches it: `screens/HomeScreen.js:374`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:379`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:382`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:389`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:390`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:391`, `screens/HomeScreen.js:392`, and `screens/HomeScreen.js:393`.

Fix:
- Add a typed `product_not_found` / `catalog_miss` error kind and route it to "Scan Product" or "Capture Ingredient Label" rather than generic retry.
- In search mode, remove or disable the offending search/recent row when this error occurs, or revalidate it before letting the user tap it again.
- Keep a retry option only if retry changes the inputs, refreshes the database row, or performs a true server revalidation; otherwise it should not be the primary CTA.
- Add a UI test where a search row is returned by `search_products` but rejected by `getProductData`, then verify the Results error CTA opens scanner/label capture and does not remount the same failed search route.

## One-Hundred-Sixty-Second-Pass Onboarding Replay Finding

### 162. Replay App Intro Can Regress Completed Onboarding State

Impact: The Profile screen presents "Replay App Intro" as a harmless way to revisit onboarding, but triggering it immediately removes the persisted onboarding-complete key before the replay has been completed or skipped. If the app is killed, crashes, backgrounds long enough to be terminated, or the user force-closes during the replay, the next launch reads the missing key and treats the user like a first-run user again. That makes a profile curiosity/testing control mutate launch state, can re-show onboarding to existing users, and can confuse first-run/legal instrumentation right before marketing.

Evidence:
- Profile exposes the replay action as a normal user-facing button labeled "Replay App Intro": `screens/ProfileScreen.js:454`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:459`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:460`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:461`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:462`.
- The button handler only emits the global replay event; it does not pass an ephemeral replay flag or keep replay separate from first-run completion state: `screens/ProfileScreen.js:61`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:62`, `screens/ProfileScreen.js:63`, and `screens/ProfileScreen.js:64`.
- App startup decides whether onboarding is required by reading `ONBOARDING_KEY` and showing onboarding when the stored value is not `"true"`: `App.js:163`, `App.js:164`, `App.js:168`, and `App.js:169`.
- The replay listener removes that same `ONBOARDING_KEY` immediately, then sets `showOnboarding(true)`: `App.js:184`, `App.js:187`, `App.js:188`, and `App.js:189`.
- When `showOnboarding` is true, App replaces the normal app tree with `OnboardingScreen`, so an interrupted replay can leave the persistent key missing before the user has taken any completion action: `App.js:199`, `App.js:200`, `App.js:205`.
- The only paths that write the key back are Skip or final Get Started inside onboarding; closing/killing the app before either one leaves the key absent: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:390`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:392`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:393`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:396`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:401`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:402`.

Fix:
- Treat replay as transient UI state: show onboarding without deleting `@woof_onboarding_complete`.
- If the product wants replay completion analytics, store a separate replay/session key, not the first-run completion flag.
- Only mutate first-run completion state from the actual first-run onboarding flow or an explicit reset action.
- Add a regression test: complete onboarding, tap Replay App Intro, terminate before Skip/Get Started, relaunch, and verify the app returns to Home rather than forced onboarding.

## One-Hundred-Sixty-Third-Pass Edge Dependency Finding

### 163. Edge Functions Depend On Floating ESM Major Imports

Impact: Both Supabase Edge Functions import `@supabase/supabase-js` from `esm.sh` using only the major version `@2`, and the repository has no Deno lockfile or import map. A fresh deploy can therefore resolve a different minor/patch build of the Supabase client or a changed transitive ESM bundle than the one tested locally. Because these functions run service-role database writes, auth parsing, quota enforcement, cache reads/writes, and paid AI/product-lookup work, dependency drift can break production scan/search behavior even when the mobile app bundle did not change.

Evidence:
- The `analyze` function imports the Supabase client from a floating major URL: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:1`.
- The `product-lookup` function uses the same floating major URL: `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1`.
- Repository search found no `deno.lock`, `deno.json`, `deno.jsonc`, or `import_map.json` under the project, so there is no committed Deno dependency pin for these remote imports.
- These functions are release-critical: `analyze` starts with `Deno.serve(...)` and reads service-role Supabase env vars before auth/quota/cache/AI work, while `product-lookup` does the same before product scraping and catalog writes: `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:953`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:965`, `supabase/functions/analyze/index.ts:966`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1037`, `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1048`, and `supabase/functions/product-lookup/index.ts:1049`.
- The existing TypeScript gate is not configured for Supabase Edge Functions, so dependency/API drift is not caught by the current app `tsc` path: `AUDIT_2026-06-05.md:326`, `AUDIT_2026-06-05.md:329`, and `AUDIT_2026-06-05.md:332`.

Fix:
- Pin Edge Function remote imports to an exact known-good version, for example `@supabase/supabase-js@2.x.y`, or centralize them through a committed import map.
- Add a committed Deno lockfile / dependency cache policy and a `deno check` or `supabase functions` type-check gate for every function.
- Treat dependency updates as explicit release changes with smoke tests for authenticated scan, guest scan, product lookup, quota enforcement, cache writes, and CORS.

## One-Hundred-Sixty-Fourth-Pass Root Recovery Finding

### 164. Root Error Recovery Can Erase Completed Onboarding

Impact: The root error boundary's second recovery attempt is labeled as a local-preferences reset, but it deletes the same `ONBOARDING_KEY` that controls first-run onboarding. If a user hits a repeatable runtime error, taps "Try Again", then taps "Reset App", the app can clear completed onboarding state without the user explicitly resetting onboarding. On the next successful render or cold launch, the startup gate sees the missing key and treats an existing user as first-run again. This is a trust and instrumentation problem during launch because crash recovery can silently mutate onboarding/consent state, and it overlaps with legal acceptance risk if future Terms/Privacy acceptance remains tied to onboarding.

Evidence:
- The root `ErrorBoundary` handles a second retry by removing both `ONBOARDING_KEY` and `@woof_theme_preference`: `App.js:33`, `App.js:36`, `App.js:37`, `App.js:38`, and `App.js:39`.
- The reset UI copy only says "Reset App" and "Resets local preferences"; it does not tell the user that first-run onboarding completion will be cleared: `App.js:62`, `App.js:63`, `App.js:80`, `App.js:81`, and `App.js:83`.
- App startup decides whether onboarding is required by reading `ONBOARDING_KEY` and showing onboarding whenever the stored value is not `"true"`: `App.js:163`, `App.js:164`, `App.js:168`, and `App.js:169`.
- When `showOnboarding` is true, the app renders `OnboardingScreen` instead of the authenticated app tree: `App.js:199`, `App.js:201`, `App.js:205`, and `App.js:212`.
- The only normal paths that write the key back are Skip and final onboarding completion, so recovery can force an existing user through onboarding again before the key is restored: `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:390`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:392`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:393`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:396`, `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:401`, and `screens/OnboardingScreen.js:402`.
- This is separate from the Profile "Replay App Intro" bug: here the mutation happens from crash recovery, not from a user intentionally opening onboarding.

Fix:
- Do not clear `ONBOARDING_KEY` from generic crash recovery. Limit the root reset to preferences that are safe to discard, or move first-run/onboarding reset behind a separate explicit action with accurate copy.
- If onboarding/legal state can be corrupted, add a targeted repair flow that verifies the persisted value instead of deleting it preemptively.
- Update the fallback copy to disclose exactly which local state will be reset.
- Add an error-boundary regression test: complete onboarding, trigger a repeatable render error, press Try Again and Reset App, relaunch, and verify the app returns to Home rather than first-run onboarding unless the user explicitly chose to reset onboarding.

## Suggested Remediation Roadmap

### Day 1: Stop Trust Breakers
- Align `search_products` and `getProductData` contracts.
- Clear or disable stale search result rows while a new query is loading or failed.
- Invalidate in-flight search sequence tokens on clear/cancel so dismissed results cannot reappear.
- Route insufficient-data rows to the ingredient-label flow, not an error.
- Hide low-quality/non-food rows from search.
- Prevent user OCR upserts from downgrading existing catalog rows.
- Require Amazon/Chewy product-lookup results to pass the same requested-product match validation as other scraped sources before caching.
- Require OPFF name-search product-lookup results to validate requested title, brand, flavor, and pet species before caching.
- Make photo product-data exact-key lookup prefer canonical product keys and validate broad AI `searchTerms` before treating a row as verified.
- Add visible search error handling.
- Wire selected search row `cache_key` into analysis as an exact lookup, not dead route state.
- Make search-result analysis carry a known dog/cat pet type or ask the user before scoring.
- Make photo and ingredient-label recovery analysis carry a known dog/cat pet type or ask before scoring.
- Revalidate persisted recent-search rows before opening Results.
- Make signed-in scan history sync independent from local AsyncStorage success.
- Ensure every counted scan creates a corresponding history ledger entry, including repeated same-product scans.
- Clean HTML entities and `Brand:` prefixes from product data.
- Align guest human-food quota reset semantics with signed-in UTC-day behavior or show an exact retry time.
- Clamp and validate guest quota reconciliation before sign-in can replay local counters into server profile state.
- Repair or fail closed when an authenticated user is missing the expected `profiles` quota row.
- Fix the AuthProvider TDZ crash before any new release build.
- Ensure auth startup failure falls back to Home/guest mode instead of a blank screen.
- Fix the public App Store link before sending any traffic to the website.
- Guard Results route params and restore score-card image sharing.
- Validate ingredient-recovery route params before starting OCR or estimate analysis.
- Ensure the ingredient-capture route screen is tracked and present in clean-checkout builds.
- Fix restore instructions and prevent paywall fallback-price dead ends.
- Reset Profile destructive-action state after account deletion and re-authentication.
- Ensure RevenueCat is initialized before Paywall offerings, purchase, restore, or customer-info calls.
- Prevent Paywall dismissal while purchase or restore callbacks are in flight.
- Handle purchase-completed/no-entitlement results with an explicit retry, restore, and support state instead of silently returning to the paywall.
- Expose the barcode path or remove barcode claims/code until it is reachable.
- Make recall copy source-qualified and fix the top summary recall row.
- Align photo/history retention with privacy copy.
- Align App Store privacy nutrition labels with authenticated scan/history behavior.
- Align the free result screen with the in-app Terms promise for ingredient previews.
- Add reliable offline preflight before scan/capture/analysis.
- Validate scanner image orientation before sending photos to AI analysis.
- Block scanner capture until `CameraView` reports it is ready.
- Make the scanner processing Cancel control touchable before relying on it for cancellation.
- Prevent scanner back navigation from launching stale Results after the user leaves.
- Include auth/session header acquisition inside scan helper timeout budgets so slow token refresh cannot make in-store scans hang.
- Make Supabase search/history/cache/auth failures feed the same offline detector as AI and barcode fetch failures.
- Classify app-owned fetch deadlines as timeout/offline signals instead of silent cancellations.
- Make scanner Cancel actually prevent Results navigation and analysis start.
- Separate top-level scan rate limits from helper OCR/identify request buckets.
- Make Clear History confirm remote deletion or show an error/retry state.
- Validate streamed completion objects before saving local results or scan history.
- Require complete pet-food analysis schemas before treating a scored result as successful or cacheable.
- Buffer SSE parser lines across network chunks before relying on streaming for launch latency.
- Ensure streamed, cached, and non-streaming analysis responses use the same normalized safety/recall result.
- Fix the root ErrorBoundary fallback styling so recovery CTAs are readable.
- Keep root crash recovery from clearing completed onboarding or legal/consent state unless the user explicitly chooses that reset.
- Make Google sign-in failures visible and actionable.
- Gate Apple sign-in on runtime availability and provide a visible fallback.
- Fix human-food history replay and synced safety fields.
- Preserve the requested dog/cat context in human-food cache keys, responses, and history metadata.
- Require complete human-food safety guidance before saving or rendering a result as done.
- Make guest history migration repeatable so scans made after sign-out are not stranded.
- Retry guest-history migration on restored signed-in sessions, not only on fresh `SIGNED_IN` events.
- Prevent auth lookup timeouts from saving signed-in scan history under the anonymous legacy key.
- Make "Show all" history expose every retained entry or route to a full history screen.
- Make post-scan upgrade prompts run from committed quota counts, not stale pre-increment state.
- Guard dev/test quota-reset helpers so they are no-ops or absent in production builds.
- Persist product images found during lookup so search and history do not lose thumbnails.
- Surface veterinary/AI disclaimers at safety-decision points for free and Pro users.
- Make expired-session errors open sign-in and preserve/retry the interrupted scan.
- Stop labeling scraped/user-OCR catalog rows as verified ingredient data.
- Make onboarding completion and future legal acceptance writes retryable and verifiable instead of silently best-effort.
- Treat RevenueCat entitlement status as unknown on failures, not free.
- Make sign-out preserve or rehydrate quota state instead of resetting the in-memory scan counter.
- Block free quota-gated actions until persisted quota counts have hydrated on startup.
- Stop silently downgrading signed-in analysis requests to guest identity on token refresh failure.
- Fix Results retry/upgrade CTAs so text human-food retries and quota errors route to the promised action.
- Disclose and govern user OCR contributions before promoting them into shared catalog data.
- Fix human-food safety copy so `safe`, `caution`, and `dangerous` render distinct labels.
- Version public and in-app legal documents from one source of truth.
- Put Terms/Privacy acceptance in the guest first-use path before scans or safety checks.
- Align App Store compatibility with the platforms actually tested for launch.
- Align native appearance configuration with the in-app Auto/Light/Dark controls.
- Preserve product-lookup provenance on cache hits; use a separate cache-hit flag for telemetry.

### Day 2: Lock Down Abuse Paths
- Fix all user-scoped RPCs to enforce `auth.uid()`.
- Lock down direct profile writes to `is_pro`, `scan_count`, and human-food quota fields.
- Align RLS policies with actual client sync/cache contracts.
- Revoke broad/public function execute grants.
- Revoke public execution from internal rate-limit, cleanup, and product-data maintenance functions.
- Pin `search_path` or schema-qualify every `SECURITY DEFINER` function.
- Rate-limit all edge-function modes.
- Gate ScrapingBee-backed product lookup behind auth/session/quota.
- Make product lookup deny anonymous paid-vendor work when client IP or rate-limit state cannot be verified.
- Make the main analyze endpoint deny anonymous paid AI work when client IP or rate-limit state cannot be verified.
- Restrict `analyze` and product-lookup CORS to trusted origins or require server-issued scan tokens for browser-origin calls.
- Reject oversized edge-function bodies before JSON parsing or paid-vendor work.
- Remove shared-cache writes/reads for human-food safety answers or scope them to the owning user.
- Make cache cleanup functions bulk-safe before scheduling them in production.
- Add product-data source provenance validation/quarantine before rows enter search or shared analysis cache.
- Prevent public/client-supplied verified analysis from writing arbitrary shared cache keys.
- Move Supabase auth persistence to native secure storage.
- Move Google OAuth to PKCE code exchange on native builds.
- Fix RevenueCat identity transitions between guest, signed-in, sign-out, and delete-account states.
- Add RevenueCat timeout/error/offline tests so paid users are not downgraded by transient entitlement checks.
- Remove authenticated write access to nutrient/product-data maintenance RPCs.
- Remove/rotate hardcoded secrets in scripts.
- Add authoritative-source flags for recall claims and block AI-only "no recalls found" messaging.
- Stop syncing local photo URIs to Supabase unless there is an explicit retention model.
- Remove hardcoded service keys from quality scripts and separate live smoke tests from CI-safe tests.

### Day 3: Speed And Instrumentation
- Add scan-stage analytics and timer logging to production-safe telemetry.
- Fix shared analysis-cache `lookup_type` metadata before using cache-hit metrics to tune barcode/search/photo performance.
- Add barcode-first or barcode-secondary flow.
- Fix the barcode miss event contract before exposing barcode scanning.
- Distinguish barcode catalog misses from OPFF/network/timeout failures.
- Remove large base64 image payloads from navigation params.
- Prewarm cache for top products and top search queries.
- Revalidate negative prewarm misses before starting paid analysis.
- Clamp public search result limits and load-test broad search terms.
- Add timeout-specific UI with "scan label instead" fallback.
- Surface helper timeouts as retryable errors or label fallbacks instead of clearing the global timeout with a silent return.
- Add analysis cancellation for back, retry, and scan-another paths so slow scans do not keep paid work alive.
- Make analysis cleanup operate on canonical keys after rekeying so timeout/error paths do not leave stale entries.
- Make "Use AI estimate" skip ingredient OCR entirely.
- Make OCR-recovery fallback errors terminal and visible instead of returning with a running analysis state.
- Harden the ingredient-label recovery screen and measure recovery dropoff.
- Mark ingredient-label handoff states as paused/finalized so no stale running analyses survive the recovery flow.
- Run VoiceOver/TalkBack passes on the core funnel and fix unlabeled controls.

### Day 4: Release Gate
- Patch Expo SDK 55 package versions.
- Declare every direct runtime import, including `expo-constants`, in `package.json`.
- Resolve or document npm audit items.
- Add CI checks for `expo-doctor`, dependency audit, and app bundle validation.
- Add production build-time env validation for Expo `extra`.
- Prevent missing Supabase env from crashing during module import before React can render recovery UI.
- Align native camera permission copy with every production camera use.
- Add an intentional lint config and make lint pass for app code.
- Verify generated native permissions and remove unused microphone permission if still present.
- Align native display name with the public "Woof" brand.
- Decide whether tablet support is in scope for launch; either disable it or complete iPad QA.
- Add an Expo Updates release/rollback gate before using the production update channel.
- Run real-device tests in low-signal store conditions.
- Verify iOS and Android RevenueCat keys, offerings, purchases, restores, and entitlement sync.
- Verify legal and paywall copy against the live App Store / RevenueCat products.
- Harden legal WebViews for static content and route external legal links to the system browser.
- Verify manage-subscription links fail gracefully with fallback instructions.
- Verify recall/brand metadata coverage before advertising recall alerts.
- Update onboarding/support/public-site copy to match the real app and live database.
- Verify all first-run onboarding assets are tracked and included in clean release builds.
- Verify all imported source modules, including the offline/network service and shared error classifier, are tracked and included in clean release builds.
- Verify all Supabase functions and migrations required by the current app contract are tracked and deployable from a clean checkout.
- Verify Supabase edge-function JWT settings are versioned and match the intended guest/auth behavior after deploy.
- Add automated smoke tests before any paid marketing campaign.
- Promote scoring, scan-flow, calibration, and accuracy scripts into intentional package scripts with CI-safe defaults.
- Align package/app/EAS/store version identifiers before release.

## Launch Gate Checklist

Do not scale marketing until:
- Search result tap never produces "not found" for rows displayed as valid products.
- Search rows on screen always belong to the current query and are disabled/cleared during loading or failed refreshes.
- Search-result analysis is species-specific or explicitly asks the user for dog/cat context before scoring.
- Photo and ingredient-label scans are species-specific or explicitly ask the user for dog/cat context before scoring.
- Recent-search tap never opens stale product data without revalidation.
- Scan miss path reaches a clear next action in under 5 seconds.
- Retried or timed-out rekeyed analyses do not leave canonical service entries or aliases behind.
- Anonymous/helper AI endpoints are rate-limited.
- Product-data writes are server-validated and not publicly writable.
- Amazon/Chewy product-lookup results cannot be cached unless matched title, brand, and variant are validated against the requested product.
- OPFF name-search product-lookup results cannot be cached under the requested key unless the matched product, brand, flavor, and pet species agree.
- Photo lookup cannot choose a broad AI-generated exact search-term row over the identified product without brand and variant validation.
- Source provenance is visible and only authoritative sources are labeled verified.
- Quota RPCs cannot mutate other users.
- AuthProvider renders without a startup ReferenceError.
- Initial auth/session failures cannot leave the app on a blank screen.
- Root ErrorBoundary fallback has readable recovery controls and a tested retry/reset path.
- Root ErrorBoundary reset does not clear completed onboarding or future legal acceptance state unless the reset copy explicitly says so and the user confirms it.
- Auth/session-expired result errors provide a working sign-in recovery path.
- Users cannot directly update entitlement or quota columns from the client.
- Dev/test quota reset helpers are absent or no-op in production builds.
- Product lookup cannot bypass rate limits with forged JWT payloads.
- Authenticated helper OCR/identify calls cannot exhaust the same hourly bucket as completed scans.
- Pro entitlement checks have an unknown/grace state and never overwrite paid access on transient RevenueCat errors.
- Signing out cannot reset the free scan counter into a fresh same-session guest allowance.
- Cold start with exhausted persisted free quota cannot open Scanner or human-food Results before quota hydration.
- Authenticated users with missing profile rows are repaired or blocked before analyze calls can bypass server quota.
- Expired signed-in sessions open a reauth/retry path instead of sending paid analysis as anonymous guest traffic.
- Text-only human-food failures retry the original food name instead of returning home.
- Quota/paywall errors in Results navigate to Paywall when the CTA says "Upgrade to Pro."
- Privacy/delete-account copy accurately distinguishes personal history from retained shared catalog contributions.
- Human-food result copy renders the correct label for `safe`, `caution`, and `dangerous` states.
- Public and in-app Terms/Privacy have matching effective dates, vendors, account behavior, and subscription wording.
- Free and Pro result screens match the entitlement boundaries described in Terms, paywall, onboarding, and support copy.
- New guest users see Terms/Privacy acceptance before the first scan, search analysis, or human-food safety check.
- Onboarding completion and legal acceptance cannot silently disappear after a storage write failure.
- Signed-in scan history never downgrades to anonymous storage on slow auth/session lookup.
- Signed-in scan history still syncs to Supabase when local AsyncStorage persistence fails.
- Appearance controls match the native `userInterfaceStyle` behavior in production builds.
- Android RevenueCat configuration is verified in EAS and on a real device.
- Paywall offerings, purchase, restore, and entitlement checks always wait for RevenueCat SDK readiness.
- Paywall close/dismiss cannot leave purchase or restore callbacks navigating or alerting from a stale screen.
- Purchase flows surface a typed no-entitlement state when StoreKit/RevenueCat returns customer info without the configured Pro entitlement.
- Public website App Store link resolves to the live app listing.
- App Store listing claims match the actual scan/search flow.
- Android native permissions match actual app behavior.
- Native camera permission prompts describe package photos, ingredient labels, and human-food photos accurately.
- Scanner capture orientation is correct across portrait, landscape-left, landscape-right, and upside-down real-device photos.
- Scanner capture is disabled until camera readiness is confirmed after first permission, cold mount, and app resume.
- Scanner processing Cancel is touchable and fires its handler before any capture-cancellation acceptance test is considered valid.
- Scanner top-back during capture cannot push Results or start analysis after the user leaves.
- Account deletion clears local personal data and documents any retained anonymous contribution data.
- Account deletion followed by same-screen re-authentication leaves Profile controls enabled and accurate.
- Results screen handles missing/malformed route params without crashing.
- Ingredient-recovery routes fail fast to a scan-again state when required image/product context is missing.
- Pro share-card image sharing works on iOS and Android.
- Lint passes for app code with a committed config.
- Paywall never displays fake/fallback prices as purchasable products.
- Restore Purchases is discoverable from support instructions.
- Expo doctor passes.
- Dependency audit has no high vulnerabilities or documented accepted risk.
- Onboarding/support/legal/paywall claims match the live product and subscriptions.
- First-run onboarding builds from a clean checkout with all referenced assets present.
- Replay App Intro does not clear or corrupt the persisted first-run onboarding completion state unless the user explicitly resets onboarding.
- Clean checkout builds include every registered route screen, including `screens/IngredientCaptureScreen.js`.
- Clean checkout builds include every imported source module, including `services/network.js` and `services/errors.js`.
- Clean checkout backend deployment includes `product-lookup`, `search_products`, human-food quota RPCs, product-data schema, and history image columns.
- Clean checkout backend deployment preserves intended edge-function JWT verification for guest-capable functions.
- Supabase Edge Function imports are pinned or locked, and every function passes a Deno/Supabase type-check before deploy.
- Veterinary/AI disclaimers are visible before and during safety-sensitive decisions, including free pet-food results.
- Human-food quota path is independent from pet-food scan quota.
- Guest and signed-in human-food quotas reset with the same semantics, or guest UI shows an exact rolling-window retry time.
- Human-food history reopens correctly after sign-in, reinstall, and cross-device sync.
- Human-food cache keys and history metadata always match the user-requested dog/cat context, even when model output omits or misstates `petType`.
- Human-food results missing required safety guidance fields fail to a retryable error and are not saved to history/cache.
- Guest scans migrate correctly after first sign-in, sign-out, guest scanning, and later sign-in.
- Guest history migration retries after app restart with an already-restored signed-in session.
- Signed-in history writes survive slow `getSession()` and reconcile any legacy entries created during auth uncertainty.
- Every retained scan history row promised by storage/paywall copy is reachable from the UI.
- Retained history rows always have a replayable payload, a refresh path, or a disabled/removed state with accurate expiry copy.
- Counted scans and Recent Scans rows reconcile one-for-one unless the UI explicitly says a result was not saved.
- Guest-to-account quota reconciliation is bounded, ledger-backed, and cannot issue unbounded per-count RPCs from local storage.
- Post-scan upgrade prompts appear exactly at the intended free-scan count and never disappear because quota increment state arrived late.
- First-scan quota education renders exactly once before its AsyncStorage suppression flag is written.
- App has at least smoke tests for scan, search, history, paywall, restore, auth, and offline states.
- History sync/upsert works under RLS or uses insert-only semantics.
- Guest cache behavior is intentionally fast and verified.
- Cache hit metrics are proven accurate before ranking decisions depend on them.
- Shared analysis-cache lookup type accurately distinguishes barcode, product-name/search, photo, ingredient-label, and human-food rows.
- Production logs and telemetry use a redacted logging wrapper and never emit raw product names, food names, OAuth redirect details, model snippets, or vendor error objects.
- Production builds fail fast when required env values are missing.
- Every direct runtime import is declared as a direct dependency, not only available through transitive hoisting.
- Missing Supabase config cannot crash before the root app/error boundary renders.
- Android release track and submit credentials are verified before Android marketing.
- Supabase refresh tokens are stored in native secure storage, not AsyncStorage.
- Barcode scan mode works end-to-end or is intentionally removed from the product surface.
- ScrapingBee-backed product lookup cannot be abused by anonymous traffic and cannot publish low-quality rows directly into search.
- Analyze and product-lookup reject oversized request bodies before JSON parsing or vendor calls.
- Recall alerts distinguish FDA-verified, AI-inferred, and unverified states.
- Top result summary surfaces recall status consistently with the Safety section.
- Photo retention, history thumbnails, and privacy disclosures match real app behavior.
- Product lookup persists and returns product images consistently across fresh lookup, cache hit, search, and history.
- Product lookup cache hits preserve the original source provenance and only add a separate cache-hit flag.
- User OCR/product-data writes cannot overwrite higher-provenance or more complete catalog rows.
- App Store privacy nutrition labels match the production data map for signed-in, guest, photo, search, history, and purchase flows.
- Offline launch/scan/search/result retry behavior is verified with airplane mode and poor cellular conditions.
- Repeated Supabase search/history/cache failures flip the global offline state instead of leaving online UI active.
- App-owned fetch timeouts are counted as timeout/offline signals, while user/navigation cancellations remain silent.
- Critical controls pass a manual VoiceOver/TalkBack accessibility sweep.
- Quality scripts do not hit production or paid vendors unless explicitly requested.
- Native app display name, icon label, website, support/legal pages, and store listing use consistent branding.
- Tablet support is either disabled or verified on iPad/tablet hardware.
- Mac and Apple Vision availability is either disabled or validated with a documented compatibility pass.
- Production OTA updates require smoke tests, monitoring, and a documented rollback path.
- RevenueCat app user identity is correct after guest use, sign-in, purchase, restore, sign-out, and delete-account flows.
- Google OAuth uses PKCE code exchange and never depends on access/refresh tokens in the redirect fragment.
- Terms/privacy WebViews are restricted to static legal content or route external links through a controlled browser path.
- Manage Subscription has tested iOS/Android fallbacks when store settings cannot open.
- Internal Supabase maintenance and rate-limit functions are not executable by anon/authenticated clients.
- Expired shared cache cleanup succeeds when multiple rows expire in the same run.
- SECURITY DEFINER functions have pinned `search_path` and schema-qualified privileged table access.
- Nutrient/product-data write RPCs are service-role only and require validated provenance.
- Shared verified analysis cache writes require server-owned product provenance and cache keys.
- Warm-cache misses cannot suppress a fresh shared `analysis_cache` row before paid analysis starts.
- Public search RPC clamps `max_results` and has an abuse/load test before marketing traffic.
- Clear/Cancel search cannot be repopulated by a late Supabase response from the dismissed query.
- Barcode OPFF misses stop loading and offer a photo/search/label fallback instead of disappearing into an unhandled event.
- Barcode timeout/network/HTTP failures are retryable/offline states, not product-not-found states.
- Scanner cancel/back/retry paths are proven not to launch stale Results screens or duplicate paid AI requests.
- Scan helper requests have bounded, abort-aware auth-header acquisition and cannot exceed their user-visible timeout budgets before the request starts.
- Identify/OCR/helper timeout paths show a user action within their configured timeout and never leave Results running after a helper promise resolves silently.
- The "Use AI estimate" path makes no OCR request and reaches first analysis feedback quickly.
- OCR-fallback analysis errors show a retryable Results error and clean up the analysis entry.
- Truncated streamed responses do not emit complete events, save local results, or create scan history rows.
- Skeletal pet-food responses with only product name and score fail as incomplete and never enter shared/local cache, history, or quota accounting.
- Streaming SSE parsing preserves events split across arbitrary network chunk boundaries and does not trigger parser-induced retries.
- Ingredient-label handoff does not leave stale running analysis entries or aliases after capture, estimate, back, retry, or app backgrounding.
- Scan and ingredient-label photos are not stored in navigation route params.
- Search-result tap uses the selected row's exact cache key end-to-end.
- Search-result scores, cache keys, and history rows carry the same verified dog/cat context.
- Search product-not-found errors route to scan/label capture or row cleanup, not a retry loop against the same invalid row.
- Clear History is verified against local and Supabase storage, including remote failure handling.
- First-time streaming results, non-streaming fallback results, and cache-hit results are field-consistent after normalization and brand/recall overrides.
- Product lookup fails closed or requires authenticated quota when IP/rate-limit checks cannot be established.
- Analyze endpoint fails closed or requires sign-in when anonymous IP/rate-limit checks cannot be established.
- Untrusted browser origins cannot call paid AI edge functions with only the public anon key.
- Human-food safety answers are not readable from a shared cross-user cache.
- Google sign-in has tested success, cancel, denied-consent, and redirect-error states with visible UI feedback.
- Apple sign-in is hidden or disabled with fallback anywhere `AppleAuthentication.isAvailableAsync()` is false.
- Package metadata, Expo version, EAS build numbers, and in-app support footer identify the same release.
